Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
15 min
The Doctrine of Kalam Nafsi: Divine Speech as an Eternal Attribute
Defending the doctrine of kalam nafsi against objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi-Ash'ari doctrine of kalam nafsi and distinguish it from the Mu'tazila view, using rational and textual proofs.

Core Idea
Divine speech is one eternal attribute; its recited forms are created manifestations, not the speech itself.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut defends a cornerstone of Hanafi-Ash'ari theology: that God's speech (kalam) is an eternal attribute, not a created entity. The author refutes objections from philosophers and Mu'tazila, clarifies the relationship between the eternal meaning and its temporal expressions, and anchors the doctrine in the words of Imam Abu Hanifa. This lesson walks you through the key arguments and their usul implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central claim and opposing views
State the Hanafi position that divine speech is an eternal attribute (kalam nafsi) and the Mu'tazila position that it is created and identical with verbal expression.
The term 'kalam nafsi' refers to the meaning subsisting in God's essence.
2
Trace the objection regarding narration and mental existence
Follow the objection that speech must subsist externally, and the response that mental existence of concepts is necessary for narration but does not make the speech created.
The author distinguishes between the eternal meaning and its mental conception.
3
Examine the three possible applications of 'speech'
Analyze the three scenarios: (1) internal is metaphorical, verbal is real; (2) vice versa; (3) both are real. Understand the theological consequences of each.
Only the third, properly understood, avoids heresy.
4
Understand the solution: one attribute with multiple determinations
Study the analogy of a simple quality manifesting differently in different subjects. Divine speech is one eternal attribute that takes on temporal 'determinations' (ta'ayyunat) when expressed through tongues.
The determinations are created, but the attribute itself is uncreated.
5
Connect to Imam Abu Hanifa's statements and the Quranic proof
Review quotes from al-Fiqh al-Akbar and al-Wasaya, and the verse 'And Allah spoke to Moses directly' (4:164) to see how the doctrine is supported by transmitted evidence.
This shows that the eternal speech and the revealed Qur'an are one and the same.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بينهما، قلت: لا بد من مغايرة الحكاية للمحكي ولا يصلح لذلك معلوم : الحضوري، كما لا يخفى على ذي كياسة فإن قلت : أليس عند جمع من الفلاسفة والمتأخرين من أهل الإسلام أنه عالم بالنسب والحكايات أيضاً، قلت : ذلك الرأي باطل كما أن علمه تعالى حضوري مع بيناه في حواشينا المتعلقة بشرح المواقف فلا اعتداد به ثم هذا أيضاً يكون إشكالاً على هؤلاء القائلين، فإن قلت هذا القائل لم يورد على المختصر، وإنما أورد على تحرير شارح الشرح بأن افتقار النسبة إلى الطرفين ضروري، ولا يجوز قيامهما بها قياماً خارجياً بل القيام بصورهما العقلية وهو التعقل غاية ما لزم منه وجود الطرفين في الذهن ولا يلزم منه التعقل، قلت : لا عائبة على المصنف، فإنه قرر كلام المختصر على ما قرر شارح الشرح، ثم نقل إيراد هذا القائل ثم أجاب عنه فليس فيه تحريف أصلاً، فإن قلت : لعل مقصوده أن وجود الطرفين في النفس وجود أصلي، لأن قيام الكلام قيام خارجي فلا يكون تعقلاً، بل أمراً مصاحباً للتعقل، فلا تقرير شرح الشرح من ابتناء كلامه على التعقل قلت إن النسبة حاكية البتة، ولا بد للحكاية من تعقلها وتعقل طرفيها بالضرورة، وإن لم يكن هذا الوجود تعقلاً وكيف يكون، فإن صاحب المختصر وشارح الشرح لا يريان الاتحاد فإنهما من حزب المتكلمين، وتعقل الطرفين حين الحكاية لا يكون إلا بحصولهما في الذهن فتدبر فيه هذا كله في الإخبارات ( وأما الإنشاآت فلا خارج لها البتة فحصولها لا يكون إلا في الذهن، وكذا حصول طرفيها، لأن الإنشاء بدون تعقل الطرفين فيه معقول ( فتدبر) ثم ههنا كلام صعب هو أن الكلام النفسي الذي هو مدلول هذه الألفاظ معان مؤتلفة من جواهر وأعراض وقيامها بذات الباري عز وجل أو بأنفسنا قيام بحيث يترتب عليه الآثار وهو باطل، وإلا لزم أن يكون المتكلم بالسواد أسود، وبالعدم معدوماً أو قيام بحيث لا يترتب عليه الآثار وهو قول بالوجود الذهني، وقد منعوه وظنوه شيئاً فرياً إلا أن يقال : إن إنكار الوجود الذهني لم يقع من قدماء المشايخ الكرام، بل إنما أنكروا كون العلم عبارة عن الوجود الذهني كما قال الإمام فخر الدين الرازي في «شرح الإشارات إنا وإن سلمنا الوجود الذهني للأشياء إلا أنه ليس علماً، لكن المتأخرين إذ لم يقفوا على مرادهم شمروا الذيل لإنكار الوجود الذهني، ثم أن كون تلك المعاني موجوداً ذهنياً أيضاً باطل، لأنها كلام ومن قام به تلك متكلم فلا بد من القيام الخارجي، وقد مر أنه لا تصح البساطة أيضاً، وقد صرح به حتى أدرجه بعضهم في العقائد الضرورية، وأيضاً: إن إطلاق الكلام على النفسي مجاز، وعلى اللفظي حقيقة أو بالعكس، أو حقيقة فيهما، وعلى الأول يلزم أن يكون ما هو كلام الله تعالى حقيقة مخلوقاً حادثاً، وما هو غير مخلوق ليس كلام الله تعالى حقيقة لما قالوا : إن اللفظي حادث والنفسي قديم وعلى الثاني، أن لا يكون هذا المقروء كلام الله حقيقة هذا وإن التزم لكن لا يجترى عليه المسلم، وعلى الثالث يلزم أن قال : إن القرآن غير منزل من الرب تعالى لأنه صادق إن أراد النفسي والارتداد لا يؤاخذ من لا يثبت بالشبهة مع أنه تواتر عن الصحابة والتابعين المؤاخذة بهذا القول، وحكمهم بالقتل فأذن الحق الصراح الذي يفترض أن يعتقد ما نقل عن صاحب المواقف أنّ هذا المقروء كلام الله تعالى حقيقة، وهو صفة بسيطة قائمة بذاته تعالى وله تعلقات بالإخبارات والإنشاآت وبحسبها يكون إنشاء وخبراً وهي صفة قديمة غير مخلوقة كما في سائر الصفات، وهي المنزل على الرسول ، وإذا صدر عن اللسان بالحركة صارت ذات أجزاء لعدم مساعدة اللسان بالتكلم بالكلام البسيط، والظاهر يختلف باختلاف المظاهر ولا استبعاد فيه، وإذا صارت ذات أجزاء وكل جزء منها متعلق بمعنى فتدل ولنمثل عليه لذلك مثلاً، فإن الكيفية صفة بسيطة قارة في حد ذاتها، فإذا وجدت بالحركة صارت غير قادرة وذات أجزاء غير مجتمعة، وإذا وجدت في موضوع دفعة صارت قارة وإذا وجدت في محل صغير صارت صغيرة، وفي كبير كبيرة فكذلك صفة الكلام في ذاته بسيطة لها تعلقات بمعان مختلفة كثيرة، فإذا أراد المتكلم التكلم باللسان فتصير هي متعلقة بمعنى ملفوظة أولاً، ثم هي مع هيئة فصارت ثم هي متعلقة بمعنى آخر تكتسي تعيناً آخر وهيئة أخرى، فتكون ملفوظة ثانياً فصارت لفظة أخرى وهكذا، فالكلام الإلهي صفة واحدة قائمة بذاته تختلف تعيناته بالمحال وهي في حد ذاتها قديمة، فإذا نزل على لسان جبريل كساها تعينات بها صارت مترتبة، فإذا قرأها جبريل غير قادرة فسمعها الرسول انحفظت في صدره كما سمعت مترتبة لكن على صفة القرار، فالحقيقة واحدة وظهوراتها مختلفة، فطوراً تظهر بكسوة، وأخرى بأخرى، وظهور شيء واحد بتعينات شتى غير منكر عقلاً وشرعاً، فالقرآن المقروء وإن صدر بلسان الرسول، لكن من قال، لم يقله الله تعالى وليس كلامه فهو كافر البتة، هذا هو الذي رامه الإمام الهمام أعظم الأئمة حيث قال في الفقه الأكبر : القرآن في المصاحف مكتوب وفي القلوب محفوظ، وعلى الألسن مقروء، وعلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم منزل لفظنا بالقرآن مخلوق وكتابتنا له وقراءتنا له مخلوقة، والقرآن غير مخلوق، وأراد باللفظ التلفظ، وهو فعلنا مخلوق البتة وأراد به كسوة التعين الذي اكتساه القرآن على اللسان، وهو أيضاً مخلوق لا شك فيه واللام في قوله : القرآن غير مخلوق، للعهد أي القرآن الذي صفته أنه مكتوب ومحفوظ ومنزل ومقروء غير مخلوق في حد نفسه وإن كانت تعيناته التي في الكتابة والقراءة والحفظ والنزول مخلوقة وقال ذلك الإمام أيضاً فيه بعد تلك العبارة الشريفة وسمع موسی کلامه قال الله تعالى: ﴿ وَكَلَّمَ اللَّهُ مُوسَى تَكْلِيمًا ﴾ [النساء : ١٦٤] وقد كان الله تعالى متكلماً، ولم يكن كلم موسى كلمة بكلامه الذي هو له صفة في الأزل، وهذا الكلام منه رضي الله عنه نص في أن الكلام القديم والمنزل واحد. وقال أيضاً: ويتكلم لا ككلامنا ونحن نتكلم بالآلات والحروف والله تعالى متكلم بلا آلة ولا حرف، والحروف مخلوقة وكلام الله تعالى غير مخلوق : وهذا لأن الحروف إنما هي نحو من التعينات التي اكتسى بها الكلام عند التلفظ ولا شك أنها مخلوقة، وقال ذلك الإمام في الوصايا رضي الله عنه، ونقر بأن القرآن كلام الله تعالى ووحيه وتنزيله وصفته لا هو ولا غيره، بل هو صفة على التحقيق مكتوب في المصاحف مقروء بالألسن محفوظ في الصدور غير حال فيها والحروف والكاغد والكتابة كلها مخلوقة لأنها أفعال العباد وكلام الله سبحانه وتعالى غير مخلوق لأن الكتابة والحروف والكلمات والآيات كلها آلة القرآن لحاجة العباد إليها، وكلام الله أنحاء
Between them, I said: There must be a difference between the narration and the narrated, and direct knowledge is not suitable for that, as is not hidden from anyone intelligent. If you say: Is it not that among a group of philosophers and later scholars of Islam that He knows relations and narrations as well? I said: That opinion is false, just as His knowledge is direct as we explained in our glosses on Sharh al-Mawaqif, so it is not considered. Then this also becomes an objection against those speakers. If you say: This objector did not object to the Mukhtasar, but rather to the Tahrir of Sharh al-Sharh, because the dependence of the relation on the two sides is necessary, and it is not permissible for them to subsist in it externally, but rather subsistence by their mental forms, which is conception. The utmost necessary from it is the existence of the two sides in the mind, and conception does not follow from it. I said: There is no blame on the author, for he established the words of the Mukhtasar as Sharh al-Sharh established, then he transmitted the objection of this objector then answered it, so there is no distortion at all. If you say: Perhaps his intention is that the existence of the two sides in the soul is original existence, because the subsistence of speech is external subsistence, so it is not conception, but rather something accompanying conception, so the establishment of Sharh al-Sharh does not depend on his words being based on conception. I said: The relation is certainly narrating, and for narration there must be conception of it and conception of its two sides necessarily, even if this existence is not conception, and how could it be? For the author of the Mukhtasar and Sharh al-Sharh do not see union, for they are of the party of the mutakallimin, and conception of the two sides at the time of narration only occurs by their occurrence in the mind, so reflect. All this is in informatives. As for constructives, they have no external existence at all, so their occurrence is only in the mind, and likewise the occurrence of their two sides, because construction without conception of its two sides is conceivable. (So reflect.) Then here is a difficult statement: that internal speech, which is the meaning of these words, is meanings composed of substances and accidents, and their subsistence in the essence of God or in ourselves is a subsistence such that effects follow from it, and that is false; otherwise it would follow that the speaker of blackness is black, and of non-existence is non-existent, or a subsistence such that effects do not follow from it, and that is the statement of mental existence. And they have prevented it and thought it a monstrous thing. Except that it may be said: The denial of mental existence did not occur from the noble early scholars; rather they denied that knowledge is expression of mental existence, as Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi said in Sharh al-Isharat: 'We, even if we grant mental existence of things, it is not knowledge.' But the later scholars, when they did not grasp their intent, rolled up their sleeves to deny mental existence. Then that those meanings are mentally existent is also false, because they are speech, and whoever they subsist in is a speaker, so external subsistence is necessary. And it has passed that simplicity is also not correct, and he has stated it, even including it in necessary beliefs. Also: The application of 'speech' to internal is metaphorical, and to verbal is real, or vice versa, or real in both. On the first, it would follow that what is really God's speech is created and temporal, and what is uncreated is not really God's speech, because they said: The verbal is temporal and the internal is eternal. On the second, that this recited [Qur'an] is not really God's speech, even if this is adhered to, but a Muslim does not dare it. On the third, it would follow that the Qur'an is not revealed from the Lord, because it is true if he intends internal, and apostasy is not punished if one does not prove by doubt, whereas it is transmitted from the Companions and Successors that they punished this statement and ruled killing. So the clear truth that it is obligatory to believe is what is transmitted from the author of al-Mawaqif: that this recited [Qur'an] is truly God's speech, and it is a simple attribute subsisting in His essence, and it has relations to informatives and constructives, and according to them it becomes construction and news. It is an eternal, uncreated attribute like other attributes, and it is what was revealed to the Messenger. When it issues from the tongue by movement, it becomes having parts because the tongue does not assist in speaking the simple speech, and the manifestation differs according to the manifestations, and there is no improbability in it. When it becomes having parts, and each part of it is related to a meaning, so it indicates. Let us give an example for that: The quality is a simple attribute fixed in itself; when it exists with movement, it becomes non-determining and having parts not combined; when it exists in a subject all at once, it becomes fixed; when it exists in a small place, it becomes small; in a large, large. Likewise the attribute of speech in itself is simple; it has relations to many different meanings. When the speaker wishes to speak with the tongue, it becomes related to a meaning, uttered first, then with a form it becomes... then it becomes related to another meaning, takes on another determination and another form, so it becomes uttered second, so it becomes another word, and so on. Thus divine speech is a single attribute subsisting in His essence; its determinations vary by places, and in itself it is eternal. When it descends upon the tongue of Gabriel, it takes on determinations by which it becomes ordered. When Gabriel reads it non-determining, the Messenger hears it, it is preserved in his chest as heard, ordered but with the quality of stability. So the reality is one and its appearances are different. Sometimes it appears in one garment, another time in another. The appearance of one thing with various determinations is not denied intellectually or legally. So the recited Qur'an, even if it issues from the tongue of the Messenger, whoever says 'God did not say it' and 'it is not His speech' is certainly an unbeliever. This is what the great Imam, the greatest of imams, aimed at when he said in al-Fiqh al-Akbar: 'The Qur'an is written in the mus'hafs, preserved in hearts, recited on tongues, and revealed to the Prophet. Our pronunciation of the Qur'an is created, our writing of it and our recitation of it are created, and the Qur'an is uncreated.' He meant by 'pronunciation' the act of pronouncing, which is our action created entirely, and he meant by it the garment of determination that the Qur'an takes on the tongue, and that is also created, no doubt. The 'al' in his statement 'the Qur'an is uncreated' is for the covenant, i.e., the Qur'an whose description is that it is written, preserved, revealed, and recited is uncreated in itself, even though its determinations in writing, recitation, preservation, and revelation are created. That Imam also said in it after that noble statement: 'And Moses heard His speech.' Allah said: 'And Allah spoke to Moses directly' (4:164). And Allah was speaking, but He did not speak a word to Moses with His speech which is His attribute in eternity. This statement from him, may Allah be pleased with him, is a clear text that the eternal speech and the revealed speech are one. He also said: 'He speaks not like our speech. We speak with instruments and letters, and Allah speaks without instrument and without letter. Letters are created, and Allah's speech is uncreated.' This is because letters are only a kind of determinations that speech takes on when uttered, and there is no doubt they are created. That Imam said in al-Wasaya, may Allah be pleased with him: 'We affirm that the Qur'an is Allah's speech, His revelation, His sending down, and His attribute, not He nor other than He, rather it is an attribute in reality, written in mus'hafs, recited by tongues, preserved in chests, not residing in them. Letters, paper, and writing are all created because they are actions of servants. Allah's speech is uncreated because writing, letters, words, and verses are all instruments of the Qur'an due to the need of servants for them.' And Allah's speech [continues] in various ways.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage is a detailed theological and philosophical defense of the Hanafi-Ash'ari doctrine of internal speech (kalam nafsi) as the eternal attribute of God, as opposed to the view that divine speech is merely created verbal expressions. The text begins by addressing an objection regarding the relationship between narration (hikaya) and the narrated object, arguing that direct knowledge (ilm huduri) cannot serve as the basis for narration because narration requires a distinction between the narration and the narrated. The author refutes the claim that God knows relations and narrations in a direct manner, stating that such a view is false. He then examines an objection concerning the necessity of the two sides (the subject and object) in a relation, and concludes that the conception of both sides in the mind is necessary for narration. The discussion moves to the nature of internal speech (kalam nafsi). The author argues that if internal speech were composed of substances and accidents subsisting in God or in humans such that effects follow, that would be absurd because it would imply that the speaker becomes what he speaks of (e.g., black or non-existent). On the other hand, if it subsists without effects, that would be mental existence (wujud dhihni), which some deny. The author clarifies that the early scholars did not deny mental existence per se, but denied that knowledge is identical to mental existence, as quoted from Fakhr al-Din al-Razi. However, the author maintains that the meanings of speech cannot be mentally existent because speech requires an external subsistence in the speaker. The passage then discusses the application of the term 'speech' to internal vs. verbal. Three possibilities are examined: (1) internal is metaphorical and verbal is real, leading to the conclusion that God's real speech would be created; (2) verbal is metaphorical and internal is real, implying that the recited Qur'an is not really God's speech; (3) both are real, which according to a certain interpretation would imply the Qur'an is not revealed. The author rejects these and affirms the position of al-Mawaqif: that the recited Qur'an is truly God's speech, being a simple attribute subsisting in God, with relations to informatives and constructives, and it is eternal and uncreated. He explains that when this attribute manifests through the tongue, it acquires parts and temporal forms (ta'ayyunat) due to the limitation of the speech organ, just as a simple quality like color appears differently in different subjects. The reality is one, but its appearances vary. The text concludes by quoting Imam Abu Hanifa's al-Fiqh al-Akbar and al-Wasaya to cement the doctrine: the Qur'an is uncreated in itself, but our recitations, writings, and letters are created. The quote from the verse (4:164) about Moses hearing Allah's speech is used to show that the eternal speech and the revealed speech are one and the same.

Key Terms
الكلام النفسي (al-kalam al-nafsi): Internal speech, the eternal attribute of God that is the meaning expressed by verbal utterances.
الوجود الذهني (al-wujud al-dhihni): Mental existence of concepts in the mind, which the author argues is not the same as knowledge.
التعينات (al-ta'ayyunat): Determinations or particular manifestations of the one eternal attribute when expressed in temporal forms like letters and sounds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relationship between the eternal attribute of speech and the recited Qur'an?
A) They are identical in every respect.
B) The recited Qur'an is a created manifestation of the eternal speech.
C) The recited Qur'an is a separate uncreated entity.
D) The recited Qur'an is not God's speech.

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an is uncreated in its essence; its recited forms are temporal manifestations. Denying this is kufr.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
6 min
The Reality of the Quran: Wording and Meaning
Defining the Quran and rejecting the Ash'ari view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of the Quran as both wording and meaning, and identify the opposing Ash'ari view.

Core Idea
The Quran is both the inimitable wording and the meaning; the wording is essential.

This passage establishes the Hanafi position on the nature of the Quran. It clarifies that the Quran is not just the meaning but the composite of wording and meaning, and strongly rejects the Ash'ari view that the Quran is merely the meaning. Understanding this is crucial for later discussions on recitation and translation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Read the opening sentence and note that the Quran is defined as both nazm and ma'na.
The term 'nazm mu'jiz' is key.
2
Observe the attributes
Note which attributes (revelation, inimitability, Arabic) are attached to the wording, not the meaning.
3
Recognize the dispute
Identify the Ash'ari view that the Quran is only meaning and that wording is metaphorical.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
See how the author dismisses the Ash'ari view as unacceptable for a Muslim.
5
Derive the thamarah
Think about the practical consequence: if Quran were meaning alone, translations would suffice; but Hanafis require Arabic wording except for excuse.

اعلم أن القرآن عندنا وعند سائر الأئمة (اسم لكل من النظم المعجز والمعنى المستفاد أي لمجموعهما، والغرض من هذا أنه اسم للنظم الدال على المعنى، لأنه هو الموصوف بالإنزال والإعجاز والعربية وغيرها من الأوصاف المنصوصة نصاً جلياً بحيث لا تتطرق الشبهة إليه أما المعنى المستفاد فقط فليس بقرآن حقيقة وهذا يؤكد ما قلنا في تحقيق الكلام القديم، وإن كانت كلمات بعض أتباع الأشعرية تشعر بظواهرها أن القرآن حقيقة هو المعنى حقيقة والنظم يطلق عليه مجازاً وهذا مما لا يجترىء عليه مسلم، فإن قلت: فلم جوز الإمام الهمام السابق في الأصول والفروع ذو اليد الطولى في العلوم جواز الصلاة بالقراءة الفارسية، بل جميع اللغات خلافاً للبردعي مع أن القارىء بها لم يقرأ القرآن قال : (وقد صح رجوع) الإمام أبي حنيفة رضي الله تعالى عنه ( عن القول بجواز الصلاة بالفارسية بغير عذر) فلا إشكال وقد روى الرجوع نوح ابن مريم وفي «الكشف» ذكره الإمام فخر الإسلام في شرح المبسوط، واختاره القاضي الإمام أبو زيد وعامة المحققين وعليه الفتوى، وفيه إشارة إلى أنه يجوز القرآن بالفارسية للعذر وهو عدم العلم بالعربية وعدم انطلاق اللسان بها، وهو الصحيح، وعليه الصاحبان إقامة للمعنى مقام النظم لأجل العذر، وقد سمعت من بعض الثقات أن تاج العرفاء والأولياء صاحب السلاسل الحبيب العجمي صاحب تاج المحدثين إمام المجتهدين الحسن البصري قدس الله سرهما ووفقنا لما يرضاه بيمن بركتهما كان يقرأ القرآن في الصلاة بالفارسية لعدم انطلاق لسانه باللغة العربية والمشهور في الجواب أن هذا التجويز ليس لأجل كون القرآن المعنى فقط، بل لأن النظم ركن زائد فيجوز سقوط وجوبه. وأشار المصنف إليه مع ما فيه وله بقوله (وقولهم النظم ركن زائد تناقض) لأن الركنية هي الجزئية والزيادة الخروج (وقد يوجه بأن معناه أي معنى الركن الزائد (ما قد يسقط) وجوبه (شرعاً) وجوب الركن الآخر كالإقرار بالنسبة إلى الإيمان فإنه يسقط حالة الإكراه، فالنظم ركن زائد سقط افتراضه في الصلاة خاصة لأجل دليل لاح له، ولعله لأجل من التبعيضية في قوله تعالى : فَأَقْرَهُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْءَانِ ﴾ [المزمل : ۲۰] وكون المعنى أصلاً مقصوداً، وما في «الهداية» من الاستدلال بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنَّهُ لَفِى زُبُرِ الْأَوَّلِينَ [الشعراء: ١٩٦] وفيها المعنى دون اللفظ، مع بقاء
Know that the Quran according to us and all imams is a name for both the inimitable wording and the meaning derived, i.e., their combination. The purpose of this is that it is a name for the wording that indicates the meaning, because it is the one described as revealed, inimitable, Arabic, and other attributes clearly stated in text without doubt. As for the meaning alone, it is not truly Quran. This confirms what we said in establishing the ancient speech, even though the words of some followers of the Ash'ari school suggest in their apparent meanings that the Quran is truly the meaning, and the wording is applied to it metaphorically. This is something no Muslim should dare to say. If you say: Why then did the great imam, foremost in usul and furu', with great mastery in the sciences, permit prayer with Persian recitation, nay all languages, contrary to al-Barda'i, even though the reciter of such has not recited the Quran? He said: Imam Abu Hanifa's retraction from the opinion of allowing prayer in Persian without excuse is authentically reported, so there is no problem. This retraction was narrated by Nuh ibn Maryam, and in al-Kashf, Imam Fakhr al-Islam mentioned it in Sharh al-Mabsut. Qadi Imam Abu Zayd and the majority of the verifiers chose it, and the fatwa is upon it. It indicates that Quran in Persian is permitted due to an excuse, i.e., lack of knowledge of Arabic and inability to pronounce it. This is the correct view, and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) are upon it, substituting the meaning for the wording due to the excuse. I heard from some trustworthy persons that Taj al-‘Urafa’ and the master of the spiritual chains al-Habib al-‘Ajami, the master of Taj al-Muhaddithin, Imam of the Mujtahidin al-Hasan al-Basri – may Allah sanctify their secrets – used to recite Quran in Persian in prayer due to his inability to pronounce the Arabic language. The well-known response is that this permissibility is not because the Quran is only meaning, but rather because the wording is an additional pillar (rukn za'id), so its obligation can be dropped. The author alluded to this, with what is in it and for him, by his saying: (Their saying 'the wording is an additional pillar' is contradictory) because pillarness is partiality and additional means exit. It may be directed that its meaning is what may drop its obligation legally, like the obligation of another pillar, just as testimony (iqrar) relative to faith drops under coercion. So the wording is an additional pillar whose obligatory nature dropped specifically in prayer due to an evidence that appeared to him. Perhaps it is due to the partitive 'min' in His statement: 'So recite what is easy from the Quran' (73:20), and the meaning is the original intended, and what is in al-Hidaya of deducing from His statement: 'And indeed it is in the scriptures of the former peoples' (26:196) where the meaning is present without the wording. With remaining...
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage clarifies the Hanafi position on the reality of the Quran and addresses a practical issue. The author begins by stating that the Quran, according to the Hanafis and all imams, encompasses both the inimitable wording (al-nazm al-mu'jiz) and the meaning derived (al-ma'na al-mustafad). The Quran is primarily the wording that indicates the meaning, because attributes like revelation and inimitability attach to the wording, not to the pure meaning. The Ash'ari view that the Quran is the meaning alone and the wording is merely a metaphor is strongly rejected. Then a potential objection is raised: if the Quran is essentially the Arabic wording, how did Imam Abu Hanifa initially permit prayer with Persian recitation? The answer is that Imam Abu Hanifa later retracted that opinion, so there is no contradiction. The established fatwa is that reciting the Quran in Persian (or any language) is permissible only when there is an excuse, such as inability to read Arabic. This concession is not because the meaning alone constitutes the Quran, but because the wording is considered an additional pillar (rukn za'id) whose obligation can be dropped in the specific context of prayer under necessity. The author provides a nuanced explanation: the phrase 'additional pillar' is paradoxical because a pillar is integral. But it is reconciled by understanding it as a pillar whose obligation may be dropped by legal evidence. Evidence includes the verse 'fa'qra'u ma tayassara min al-Qur'an' (recite what is easy from the Quran) which implies partitive flexibility, and the verse in al-Hidaya that mentions the Quran being in earlier scriptures, where only the meaning is shared. This shows that the requirement of Arabic wording can be relaxed for excuse. The passage ends with a reference to al-Hasan al-Basri reciting in Persian, supporting the permissibility with excuse.

Key Terms
النظم المعجز (al-nazm al-mu'jiz): The inimitable wording of the Quran in Arabic.
المعنى المستفاد (al-ma'na al-mustafad): The meaning derived from the Quranic wording.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Quran according to the Hanafis?
A) The meaning alone
B) The wording alone
C) Both wording and meaning
D) The revelation alone

Key Takeaway
The Quran is the composite of inimitable Arabic wording and its meaning.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Reciting Quran in Persian: The Additional Pillar (الركن الزائد)
Resolving the apparent contradiction: Quran definition vs Persian recitation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on reciting Quran in a non-Arabic language in prayer and apply the concept of rukn za'id.

Core Idea
Reciting Quran in Persian is permitted for those unable to read Arabic because the wording is an additional pillar that can be dropped.

This passage addresses a practical issue: can someone pray by reciting the meaning of the Quran in Persian? While the initial opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa allowed it without restriction, he later retracted. The final ruling permits it only for those with an excuse, like inability to pronounce Arabic. The concept of 'additional pillar' (al-rukn al-za'id) is introduced to explain why the requirement of Arabic wording can be dropped.

Guided Path
1
Note the objection
The hypothetical objector points out that if Quran is Arabic wording, how did Imam Abu Hanifa allow Persian recitation?
2
Understand the retraction
The answer is that Imam Abu Hanifa later retracted his opinion.
Retraction confirmed by Nuh ibn Maryam.
3
Identify the final ruling
The fatwa is that Persian recitation is allowed only with an excuse, like inability to read Arabic.
4
Grasp the concept of rukn za'id
The explanation is that the wording is an additional pillar, meaning its obligation can be dropped by legal evidence.
The author addresses the apparent contradiction in the term 'additional pillar'.
5
Examine the evidence
The verse 'fa'qra'u ma tayassara min al-Quran' (73:20) and the verse about earlier scriptures are used as support.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
12 min
The Grave Robber and the Hadd: Usul Dispute on 'Umum
A dispute record on the grave robber's punishment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the usul principle (umum) at stake in the grave robber dispute and explain why the Hanafi school excludes him from the general ruling on theft.

Core Idea
A general text does not apply when the subject lacks a necessary condition (hirz).

The grave robber steals a shroud from a grave. The Quranic verse on theft commands amputation for 'the thief.' Is the grave robber a thief? The Hanafi school says no, because the grave is not a secure place (hirz), a condition for the hadd. This dispute turns on how we interpret the general word 'thief' and whether additional conditions are needed. In this lesson, we will dissect the usul argumentation behind this famous ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
Determine the specific legal question: Does the grave robber (al-nabbash) receive the hadd punishment (amputation) for theft? Note the Hanafi position and who opposes it.
The text states the Hanafi position with Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, opposed by Abu Yusuf and the three other imams.
2
Locate the operative usul principle
The opposing school argues that the grave robber falls under the general term 'thief' (sariq) in the Quran. Identify that this is a claim of 'umum (generality). The Hanafi response challenges the applicability of that umum based on a missing condition (shart).
The condition is hirz (secure place). The grave does not qualify as hirz.
3
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi school provides evidence: the practice of the Companions in the time of Muawiya, who imposed ta'zir, not hadd. Also, the opinions of many Companions and Tabi'un. Understand that this evidence shows that the early community did not consider the grave robber a thief deserving hadd.
This is a dalil naqli (narrative proof) that supports the usul reasoning.
4
Compare the opposing dalil
The opposing school (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali, and Abu Yusuf) argue that the grave is a hirz and the general term includes the grave robber. Their dalil is the apparent meaning of the Quranic verse. Note that this is a disagreement over the definition of hirz and the scope of 'umum.
The Hanafi response shows that the Companions' practice overrides the apparent generality.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis punish the grave robber with ta'zir (discretionary beating), while the other schools apply the hadd amputation. Recognize that this is a serious legal consequence stemming from an usul difference.
This shows how usul principles directly affect fiqh outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا أي عدم وجوب الحد على النباش (عند الإمام أبي حنيفة و الإمام محمد، خلافاً لأبي يوسف والأئمة (الثلاثة مالك والشافعي وأحمد رضوان الله تعالى عليهم وهم ظنوا أن النباش داخل في عموم السارق، واعتبروا القبر حرزاً وقول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله قول ابن عباس) وفي «فتح القدير روى ابن أبي شيبة عن الزهري قال : أخذ نباش في زمن معاوية، وكان مروان على المدينة، فسأل من بحضرته من الصحابة والفقهاء، فاجتمع رأيهم على أن يضرب ويطاف به، وعلم من هذا أن غير ابن عباس أيضاً من الصحابة الكثيرين مذهبهم كمذهبنا (والثوري والأوزاعي ومكحول والزهري كلهم من التابعين وقولهم (مذهب أمير المؤمنين (عمر) رضوان الله تعالى عليه (و) عبد الله بن مسعود و أم المؤمنين (عائشة) رضوان الله تعالى عليهم (والحسن) من التابعين وأبي ثور) من تبع التابعين كذا) في التيسير
This means the non-obligation of the hadd on the grave robber is according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf and the three Imams – Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad (may Allah be pleased with them). They thought that the grave robber is included under the generality of 'thief' and considered the grave a secure place. The opinion of Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) is the opinion of Ibn Abbas. In 'Fath al-Qadir', Ibn Abi Shayba narrated from al-Zuhri: 'A grave robber was caught in the time of Muawiya, and Marwan was in Medina. He asked the Companions and jurists present, and they agreed that he should be beaten and paraded.' From this it is known that besides Ibn Abbas, many other Companions also held our school. Al-Thawri, al-Awza'i, Makhul, and al-Zuhri, all from the Tabi'un, and their opinion is the opinion of the Commander of the Faithful Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, the Mother of the Believers Aisha (may Allah be pleased with them), al-Hasan (from the Tabi'un), and Abu Thawr (from the Tabi' al-Tabi'in). Thus in al-Taysir.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage records the famous ikhtilaf (dispute) regarding the application of the hadd (amputation) to the grave robber (al-nabbash). It presents the Hanafi position: according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the grave robber does not receive the hadd. This is opposed by Imam Abu Yusuf (who within the Hanafi school differed) and the three leading imams of other schools: Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal. They considered the grave robber to fall under the general term 'thief' in the Quranic verse and regarded the grave as a valid secure place (hirz). The text then provides support for the Hanafi position by citing the opinion of the Companion Ibn Abbas, and then references a historical incident from the time of Caliph Muawiya: when a grave robber was caught, the Companions and jurists in Medina (under Marwan) decided on a discretionary punishment (ta'zir: beating and parading) rather than the hadd, indicating that they did not consider him a thief deserving amputation. The passage then lists additional supporters: many Companions (not just Ibn Abbas) and prominent Tabi'un like al-Thawri, al-Awza'i, Makhul, al-Zuhri, and also the opinions of Umar, Ibn Mas'ud, Aisha, al-Hasan al-Basri, and Abu Thawr. This shows that the Hanafi position has strong early authority.

Key Terms
النباش (al-nabbash): One who digs up graves to steal the shroud.
الحرز (al-hirz): A secure place where property is kept safely.
الحد (al-hadd): The fixed punishment (amputation) for theft.
عموم (umum): Generality; a term that includes all individuals of a class.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Hanafi: hadd; Shafi'i: no hadd
B) Hanafi: ta'zir; Shafi'i: hadd

Key Takeaway

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
10 min
Dispute on Ta'wil: Hanafi Interpretation of 'Shah' in Zakat Hadith
Defends Hanafi ta'wil of 'shah' meaning value against Shafi'i criticism

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the concepts of ta'wil and istinbat al-manat to evaluate the Hanafi reading of the zakat hadith and identify the key textual proofs that support it.

Core Idea
The Hanafi 'shah' interpretation is istinbat al-manat – the sheep is a monetary standard, not a literal obligation.

This passage presents a classic usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over the meaning of the word 'shah' in the zakat hadith. The Hanafis argue that it refers to monetary value, while the Shafi'is insist on the literal animal. By analysing the textual proofs, you will see how the Hanafi approach qualifies as an inference of the ratio legis (istinbat al-manat) rather than a far‑fetched interpretation (ta'wil).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify exactly what the Hanafis claim about the word 'shah' in the hadith: it indicates a monetary standard, not the literal animal. Pay attention to the phrase 'istinbat al-manat'.
The Hanafis insist the literal meaning is preserved; the sheep functions as a measure of value.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
The Shafi'is argue that this is a far ta'wil because if 'shah' means value, then giving the literal sheep would be insufficient. Understand their reliance on the apparent meaning (zahir).
The Shafi'is divide ta'wil into near, far, and impossible. They classify the Hanafi reading as far.
3
Examine the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafis cite the practice of Mu'adh (accepting garments in place of grains) and the schedule of Abu Bakr (substituting animals with dirhams). These show that the Prophet and the Companions considered the monetary value as the real obligation.
These proofs are from Sunnah (ahad) but strengthened by multiple lines of evidence.
4
Distinguish ta'wil from istinbat al-manat
The Hanafis argue that they are not interpreting the word differently; they are inferring the underlying rationale (manat) of the obligation. The literal word 'shah' remains, but its function is to set the amount of value.
This distinction is crucial: istinbat al-manat does not negate the literal text; it explains why a specific term is used.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to the Hanafis, paying the monetary value of a sheep in zakat is valid and even superior. According to the Shafi'is, only the animal itself suffices. This difference affects how zakat is fulfilled today.
The thamarah al-khilaf shows that the dispute is not merely academic but has real fiqh implications.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وذلك لأن الشاة على معناها، ولا يلزم منه عدم أجزاء القيمة، فإنها لم تذكر لكونها هي الواجب، بل لكونها معيار الواجب وتقديره، فالواجب الشاة) حقيقة هذا القدر من المالية وهو المجزىء فافهم وأورد في شرح الشرح The first chapter: Ta'wil includes that which is close to understanding (so the outweighed is preponderated by a preponderator) which is the contextual clue, and that which is far from understanding, so it is not resorted to except with a strong motive, then it becomes preponderant and flows into the mind. The Shafi'is divided it into three and said: Ta'wil is near, far, and impossible. And it is not hidden what is in this. Is this not like dividing a human being into man, woman, and an engraving on a plank? Then the Shafi'is mention from it interpretations of the Hanafis: correct because it is an inferred meaning. The first principle: the Book. Among them is their statement regarding his statement (peace and blessings be upon him and his family and companions) in the letter of Amr ibn Hazm: 'In forty sheep (shah) is its value' – a statement of the saying. So either by intending the value from the word 'shah' or by estimation in the order of speech, and this interpretation is far, as it would entail that the sheep is not obligated but rather the value, so it should not be sufficient if one gives it. And what they said in the illa that zakat is to fulfill the needs of the needy, and fulfilling need through value is more severe, so it is not inferred from a source that invalidates it, and every meaning inferred from a ruling that invalidates it is invalid, as in Sharh al-Mukhtasar. The truth is that it is not ta'wil, and that their intent is that the obligation of the sheep implies the permissibility of its substitute in payment, because the consideration in zakat is the monetary value, not the form, because it is to fulfill the needs of the poor, and value is more fulfilling. And this is indicated by the text of Mu'adh (may Allah be pleased with him) as narrated by al-Bukhari (and his mu'allaqat are authentic) with a chain, and in some commentaries of al-Tahrir it is connected by Yahya ibn Adam: 'Bring me a khamis (a garment five cubits long) or a labis (a worn garment) in place of the obligatory wheat and barley, and this is easier for you and better for the Companions of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) in Medina.' Because clothes are abundant in their land, but less in Medina, and due to the Companions' occupation with worship and turning away from worldly goods, they do not find clothes, while they were in ease and wealthy, so giving clothes is easier for them. Also it is reported in the letter of the Successor of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), al-Siddiq al-Akbar (may Allah be pleased with him), according to what al-Bukhari narrated: 'Whoever has to pay the sadaqa of a jadha'ah but does not have it, and has a hiqqah, it is accepted from him, and he must give two sheep if they are available, or twenty dirhams. And whoever has to pay the sadaqa of a hiqqah but does not have it, and has a jadha'ah, it is accepted from him, and the collector gives him twenty dirhams. And whoever has to pay the sadaqa of a bint labun but does not have it, and has a bint makhad, it is accepted from him, and he gives twenty dirhams or two sheep.' And at the beginning of this book: 'This is the obligation of sadaqa which the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) enjoined.' So it became clear from this that the mention of the sheep is to specify the monetary value of the obligation and to inform of it, not that the obligatory thing is the form of the sheep. So it appears that this is inference of the underlying rationale (istinbat al-manat) and not ta'wil. For the sheep remains on its meaning, and it is mentioned because it is the standard for knowing the obligation. So counting it as ta'wil is a departure from the proper context. Rather, the objection is only what they mentioned that inference of the illa invalidates the text, and that is not permissible. The excuse for it is what we explained: changing the text is not for inference, but due to other dala'il. And whoever ponders what we said will know the refutation of the claim that if we keep the word 'shah' on its meaning, it is obligatory and value is not sufficient, and if value is intended, it is ta'wil. Yes, it is ta'wil with dalil, so it is not far. Because the sheep is on its meaning, and it does not entail non-sufficiency of value, for it is not mentioned as the obligatory thing itself, but as a standard and measure of the obligation. So the obligatory thing is the sheep in reality, meaning this amount of monetary value, and that is sufficient. Understand this. And in Sharh al-Sharh it is stated that the non-obligation of the specific entity does not entail its non-sufficiency, for the obligation comes when it is brought, which is apparent, just as it entails its non-sufficiency. And what is said in the Hashiyah of Mirzajan: 'This is nothing, because if the value of the sheep is obligatory, the principle is that its substitute is not sufficient except with an external proof.' And he is not guided to object: obligation of this sheep is not, non...
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is an usul dispute about ta'wil (interpretation away from the apparent meaning). The author defends the Hanafi position that when the Prophet (peace be upon him) said 'in forty sheep (shah) is an obligation' in the letter of Amr ibn Hazm, the word 'shah' does not mean the literal animal but its monetary value. The Shafi'is criticize this as a far-fetched ta'wil, arguing that if the obligation were value, then giving the actual sheep would not suffice. The Hanafi response is that this is not a ta'wil but an inference of the underlying rationale (istinbat al-manat): the sheep is mentioned as a standard for the monetary value that is the actual obligation. The passage adduces several proofs: the practice of Mu'adh in taking garments in place of grains, and the schedule of the Caliph Abu Bakr allowing substitutions with monetary compensation. The Hanafi argument is that the primary consideration in zakat is monetary (mal), not the particular animal or form. Therefore, paying value is permissible and even better. The author also addresses the objection that if the word 'shah' is kept literal, then value should not be accepted; he clarifies that the word functions as a designation of the standard, not the obligated entity itself. The dispute centers on the nature of ta'wil: the Hanafis argue that their interpretation is supported by strong evidence and is not a forced ta'wil.

Key Terms
التأويل (al-ta'wil): Interpretation that turns a word away from its apparent meaning to a non-apparent meaning, based on a preponderating factor.
الشاة (al-shaah): In this context, a standard for the obligated monetary value in zakat, not necessarily the literal animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position defended in this passage, what does the word 'shah' (sheep) in the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm indicate?
A) The obligation to give a literal sheep
B) The obligation to give the monetary value of a sheep
C) That the sheep is a standard for the obligated monetary amount
D) That both sheep and value are equally acceptable

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi interpretation of 'shah' in zakat is an instance of istinbat al-manat, not ta'wil, and is supported by the practice of the Companions.

Hanafi Defense of Marriage Without Wali
Hanafi rebuttal of Shafi'i objection regarding wali

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi and Shafi'i proofs regarding wali requirement and evaluate the Hanafi rebuttal.

Core Idea
The Hanafis prioritize the stronger hadith 'الأيم أحق بنفسها' over 'لا نكاح إلا بولي', allowing women to marry without a guardian.

The requirement of a wali (guardian) for a woman's marriage is a classic point of ikhtilaf between Hanafis and Shafi'is. This passage presents the Hanafi defense, arguing that the Shafi'i proof is weak and contradicted by stronger evidence. You will learn how the Hanafis reconcile conflicting hadiths and apply usul principles to derive rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the core legal question: Is a wali required for the validity of a woman's marriage?
2
Identify Shafi'i proof
Find the Shafi'i hadith 'لا نكاح إلا بولي' and note its apparent meaning and authority.
3
Identify Hanafi proof
Locate the Hanafi hadith 'الأيم أحق بنفسها من وليها' and Quran 2:230, noting their textual categories.
4
Analyze Hanafi response
Follow the Hanafi argument: the Shafi'i hadith is weak or can be interpreted consistently; the Hanafi proof is stronger and acts upon both evidences.
5
Determine thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical consequence: validity of marriage without wali in Hanafi fiqh vs. invalidity in Shafi'i fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الأول/ الكتاب النبي ، كذا في فتح القدير أيضاً، فليس في الحديث الثاني سقم إلا بالاضطراب في الإرسال والإسناد، وهو ليس سقماً عندنا، وفي «التحرير» قال بعدما بين سقم الرواية الأولى المذكورة في الاعتراض، وابداء معارض أقوى منه قال وأما الحمل على الأمة وما ذكر فإنما هو في لا نكاح إلا بولي يعني أن الحنفية لم يؤوّلوا ولم يخصصوا الحديث المذكور في الاعتراض لكونه سقيماً ومعارضاً بالأقوى، وإنما أولوا هذا الحديث، وإذا تأملت فيما تلونا علمت ما في نسبة التنزل إلى التحرير من الخطأ والله أعلم ( ولو سلم) عدم ضعفه (فعملوا بما هو أصح منه) وقد جاء من رواية مسلم الأيم أحق بنفسها من وليها» وهي) أي الأيم (من لا زوج لها بكراً كانت أو ثيباً وليس للولي في نفسها حق سوى التزويج، فهي أحق به منه) أي من الولي فينفذ نكاحها من غير إذن الولي هذا وقد يقال : الحق الذي فيه المرأة أحق يجوز أن يكون الرضا بالتزوج، وهذا ينافي قول الشافعية، فإنهم يرون الإجبار على البكر البالغة في التزوج، وبعض الشافعية يخصصونه بغير البكر، فيرد عليهم اعتراض التأويل البعيد قهقرى ويؤيد ذلك بقوله تعالى: ﴿حَتَّى تَنكِحَ زَوْجًا غَيْرَهُ ﴾ [البقرة: ۲۳۰] لإسناد النكاح إلى المرأة، والقول بأن جهة الإسناد وجود الأذن منها والرضا به ارتكاب للتجوز من غير دليل، وارتكابه ليس أولى من ارتكابه في الحديث المذكور فإذا صحت مباشرتها للتزوج بحديث مسلم وإشارة قوله تعالى : فلا بد إما التخصيص بالأمة والصغيرة ونظائرهما وتخصيص العام ليس الاحتمالات البعيدة فإنه شائع ذائع، وقد عرفت أن هذا التخصيص فقط غير واف (وإما التأويل بالأول إلى البطلان (وهو) أيضاً (شائع) والحق التأويل الذي ذكرنا، وقال مطلع الأسرار الإلهية قدس سره إن معنى الحديث الثاني أن لا نكاح لمن عليه الولاية إلا بولي للنكاح وهو أعم من المرأة الناكحة ووليها وحينئذ لا تأويل، ثم إنه لا بد للشافعية من تخصيصه بنكاح المرأة ثم البكر منها فيلزم المحذور قهقرى على أن مفهومه المخالف (صحة نكاحها بإذن وليها وأنتم لا تقولون به فإن النكاح عندكم لا ينعقد بعبارات النساء، وقد يقال : إن قيد من غير إذن الولي خرج مخرج العادة، فإن العادة أن لا تنكح المرأة نفسها إلا إذا لم يأذن الولي، ولك أن تقول : إن منطوق الاستثناء في حديث لا نكاح إلا بولي جواز نكاح المرأة عند حضرة الولي ،وإذنه، مع أنهم لا يقولون به، ولو تنزلنا وسلمنا أن الحديثين صحيحان خاليان عن المعارض، فمن أين يمنعون النكاح بعبارات النساء وإنما اللازم منه الإذن فتدبر
The first principle / the prophetic book, likewise in Fath al-Qadir. So there is no defect in the second hadith except the confusion in mursal and isnad, and that is not a defect with us. In al-Tahrir, he said after clarifying the defect of the first narration mentioned in the objection and presenting a stronger counter-evidence, he said: 'As for limiting it to the slave woman and what was mentioned, that is only in 'لا نكاح إلا بولي' meaning that the Hanafis did not interpret or specify the hadith mentioned in the objection because it is defective and opposed by stronger evidence, but they interpreted this hadith.' If you ponder what we have recited, you will know the error in attributing reduction to al-Tahrir. And Allah knows best. (Even if we accept) its lack of weakness, (they acted upon what is more authentic than it) and it has come from the narration of Muslim: 'The non-virgin is more entitled to herself than her guardian.' She (the non-virgin) is one who has no husband, whether virgin or previously married, and the guardian has no right over her person except for marriage. So she is more entitled to it than him, i.e., the guardian. Thus her marriage is valid without the guardian's permission. This, and it may be said: The right in which the woman is more entitled could be consent to marriage, and this contradicts the Shafi'is, for they hold compulsion over the adult virgin in marriage. Some Shafi'is specify it for non-virgins, so the objection of far-fetched interpretation is thrown back at them. This is supported by His saying: 'until she marries a husband other than him' (Quran 2:230), attributing the marriage to the woman. To say that the aspect of attribution is the existence of her permission and consent is an unjustified metaphor, and employing it is not better than employing it in the mentioned hadith. So if her direct act of marriage is established by Muslim's hadith and the indication of His statement, then inevitably either specification to slave women, minors, and their likes (and specification of the general is not among remote probabilities, for it is widespread; and you know that this specification alone is insufficient) or interpretation leading to nullity (and it too is widespread). But the correct interpretation is what we mentioned. And the author of Matali' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyya (may his secret be sanctified) said: The meaning of the second hadith is 'There is no marriage for the one who has guardianship except with a guardian for the marriage', which is more general than the woman who marries and her guardian. In that case, no interpretation is needed. Then the Shafi'is must specify it to the woman's marriage, then to the virgin among them, so the problem is thrown back at them. Also, its counter-indication (the validity of her marriage with her guardian's permission) is something you do not accept, for according to you, marriage is not concluded by women's expressions. It may be said: The restriction 'without the guardian's permission' came as a customary expression, for custom is that a woman does not marry herself unless the guardian does not permit. But you may say: The explicit wording of the exception in the hadith 'لا نكاح إلا بولي' permits the woman's marriage in the presence and permission of the guardian, even though they do not accept it. Even if we concede and accept that both hadiths are authentic and without opposition, how can they forbid marriage by women's expressions while the necessary implication is permission? So reflect.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul dispute defending the position that a woman can contract her own marriage without a wali. The author addresses the Shafi'i objection based on the hadith 'لا نكاح إلا بولي' (no marriage except with a guardian). The Hanafi response is twofold: first, the hadith is not authentic (sigham) due to weakness in transmission; second, even if authentic, it is opposed by a stronger hadith from Muslim: 'الأيم أحق بنفسها من وليها' (the non-virgin is more entitled to herself than her guardian). The Hanafis interpret the latter as granting the woman the right to choose and contract. They also cite Quran 2:230 which attributes marriage to the woman ('حتى تنكح'). The passage argues that Shafi'is, who insist on a wali, must resort to far-fetched interpretations or arbitrary specification (e.g., excluding virgins or slave women). The author also presents an alternative interpretation of the hadith by Matali' al-Asrar: the hadith means 'there is no marriage for the one who has guardianship (i.e., the wali) except with a guardian', i.e., the wali needs a wali, which is absurd, showing the hadith cannot be taken literally. Finally, the Hanafi practice of acting upon both hadiths (by specifying the first to minors and slaves and following the second for adult free women) is presented as more comprehensive.

Key Terms
أيم (ayyim): A woman who has no husband, whether virgin or previously married (thayyib).
ولي (wali): Guardian, usually the nearest male relative (father, grandfather, etc.) with authority over a woman's marriage.
سقم (suqm): Defect or weakness in a hadith's chain or text.
تخصيص (takhsis): Specification of a general text to a subset of its instances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i claim that a woman cannot marry without a wali?
A) The Shafi'i hadith is weak and cannot be used as proof.
B) The woman's marriage is valid without wali because of the stronger hadith.
C) Both hadiths are authentic but the Hanafis choose to ignore the Shafi'i one.
D) The Shafi'i hadith applies only to virgins.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position on marriage without wali is built on preferring a stronger hadith over a weaker one, and reconciling all proofs through specification and interpretation.

Refuting the Abrogation of the Share of Relatives in Khums: Usul Analysis
Refuting the claim that the share for relatives in khums is abrogated

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi argument against the abrogation of the relatives' share in khums by identifying and applying the key usul principles: negation of illa does not necessitate negation of hukm, and a zanni ijma cannot abrogate a qat'i general text.

Core Idea
Negation of a cause does not automatically negate the ruling; a zanni ijma cannot abrogate a qat'i general text.

This passage engages a classic usul dispute: has the share of the Prophet's relatives in khums been abrogated? Some argued that since the illa (support for the Prophet) ceased after his death, the ruling ceases. The author refutes this using two key usul principles: first, the absence of an illa does not necessarily remove the hukm (as exemplified by raml in tawaf); second, the claimed ijma is ahad (zanni) and cannot override a qat'i general text from the Quran. We will dissect this argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue and Opposing Positions
State the contested ruling: whether the share of relatives (dhu al-qurba) in khums is abrogated. Identify the Hanafi position (not abrogated) and the opposing view (abrogated) held by some earlier Hanafis like al-Tahawi.
2
Analyze the Illa Argument
Examine the claim that because the illa (nusrah/support) is gone, the ruling is removed. The author rebuts using the raml example: the jogging in tawaf remains recommended even though its original cause (showing strength to the polytheists) is no longer present. Thus, negation of illa does not necessitate negation of hukm.
This is a critical usul principle: the ruling may persist for other reasons or as a general prescription.
3
Examine the Ijma Claim
Some scholars cite an ijma that the share has ceased. The author argues that this ijma is ahad (isolated) and thus zanni in transmission. According to Hanafi usul, a zanni proof cannot oppose a qat'i general text (amm qat'i). Therefore, the ijma cannot abrogate the verse.
Contrast this with the share for those whose hearts are reconciled: there, the Quran itself indicates the cause, and the ijma is mutawatir, so it can be abrogated.
4
Address the Objection from Umar's Practice
It is reported that Umar gave Ali from khums. The author explains this as due to poverty, not as the specific share for relatives. This preserves the principle that the general share remains, but actual distribution is subject to need.
This shows that practice of the Companions must be interpreted in light of usul principles.
5
Evaluate the Final Hanafi Position
The author concludes that the share is not dropped (ghayr saqit), but relatives are not exclusively entitled to it; rather, they are among the recipients (masarif), and the Imam has discretion to allocate according to what is most beneficial. This balances the qat'i text with practical flexibility.
This position aligns with Imam Malik's view, showing cross-madhhab convergence on the principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الأول/ الكتاب وهم بمنزلة واحدة في النسب ؟ فقال : إنهم لم يفارقونا في الجاهلية والإسلام، وإذا كان هذا السهم للنصرة فبعد وفاة الرسول صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم لم تبق نصرته، فانتفى الحكم بانتفاء العلة وهذا ليس من النسخ في شيء كما في سهم المؤلفة من الزكاة . ثم هذا لا يكفي للمطلوب من غير معاونة حديث الاجماع كما وقع عن بعض مشايخنا، فإنه لا يلزم من انتفاء علة شرع الحكم انتفاؤه كما وقع في الرمل في الطواف وأما إذا دل الاجماع على السقوط فلا مرد له فعلم أن تلك العلة كانت مبقية للحكم أيضاً، فإن قلت : فمن أين يعطون للفقراء منهم مع أنهم لم يبقوا مصارف بهذا الاجماع، وقد اختار الشيخ أبو الحسن الكرخي إعطاءهم، وهو المختار للفتوى لا ما اختاره الطحاوي من عدم الإعطاء أصلا؟ قلت: لعل ذلك لدخولهم في الفقراء، وإنما يقدمون تكريماً وتشريفاً لا للسهم الذي أعده الله تعالى لهم على الاستقلال، ومن ههنا اندفع القدح في الاجماع بإعطاء أمير المؤمنين عمر أمير المؤمنين علياً من الخمس، وذلك لأن هذا الإعطاء لعله كان للفقر، لأن أمير المؤمنين علياً لم يكن له غنى فارغاً عن الحوائج الضرورية، هذا غاية الكلام في هذا المقام، لكن بعد بقي فيه كلام، لأن هذا الإجماع آحادي فلا يعارض الآية القاطعة على أصلنا من قطعية العام فلا يبطل به الحكم المتقرر بها، بخلاف سهم المؤلفة، فإن في نص الكتاب إشارة إلى علية التأليف حتى يتبادر إلى الفهم أن الإعطاء للحاجة إلى التأليف، ونقل الإجماع بالتواتر المعنوي فلا مرد له، إلا أن يقال : إن هذا العام مخصوص كما فصار ظنياً فافهم، والأشبه أن هذا السهم غير ساقط لكنهم غير مستحقين إياه بل مصارف والخيار إلى الإمام في العمل بالأصلح والأليق كما عليه الإمام مالك، والله تعالى أعلم بأحكامه
The first origin: The Book, and they are like one in lineage? He said: They did not separate from us in Jahiliyyah and Islam. And since this share was for support, after the death of the Messenger of Allah, his support remains no more, so the ruling is negated by the negation of the cause, and this is nothing like abrogation, as in the share of those whose hearts are reconciled from zakat. Then this is not sufficient for what is required without the assistance of the hadith of ijma as occurred from some of our scholars, because it is not necessary that the negation of the cause of legislation of a ruling necessitates its negation, as occurred in the jogging in tawaf. But if ijma indicates the cessation, there is no rejection of it, and then it is known that that cause was also preserving the ruling. If you say: From where do they give to the poor among them, even though they did not remain as recipients by this ijma, and Sheikh Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi chose giving to them, and that is chosen for fatwa, not what al-Tahawi chose of not giving at all? I say: Perhaps that is because they are included among the poor, and they are given precedence as honor and respect, not for the share that Allah prepared for them independently. And from here the criticism of the ijma is repelled by Commander of the Faithful Umar giving Commander of the Faithful Ali from the khums, because that giving was perhaps for poverty, because Commander of the Faithful Ali did not have wealth free from essential needs. This is the utmost discussion in this place, but after that there remains speech, because this ijma is ahad and cannot oppose the qat'i verse according to our principle of the qat'iyyah of the general, so it does not invalidate the ruling established by it, unlike the share of those whose hearts are reconciled, for in the text of the Book there is an indication of the causality of reconciliation so much so that it immediately comes to mind that the giving is for the need of reconciliation, and the transmission of ijma by tawatur ma'nawi is not rejectable, unless it is said that this general is specified and thus became zanni, so understand. And the more likely is that this share is not dropped, but they are not entitled to it; rather, they are recipients, and the choice is for the Imam to act according to what is most beneficial and appropriate, as Imam Malik holds. And Allah knows best His rulings.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute concerning the share of relatives (dhu al-qurba) in khums. The author argues against the claim that this share is abrogated. He begins by stating the position that the share was for supporting the Prophet, and after his death, the cause (illa) is gone, so the ruling ends. However, he refutes this by noting that negation of cause does not necessarily entail negation of ruling, as seen in the jogging during tawaf which remains recommended despite the absence of the original cause. Then he discusses the role of ijma: some scholars rely on an ijma that the share has ceased. He counters that this ijma is ahad (isolated) and cannot override a qat'i general text from the Quran. He distinguishes this from the share for those whose hearts are reconciled, where the Quran itself indicates the cause, and the ijma there is transmitted by tawatur ma'nawi. He also addresses the objection that Umar gave Ali from khums, explaining that this was due to poverty, not as the specific share. The author concludes that the share is not dropped, but the recipients are not exclusively entitled; rather, the Imam has discretion to allocate it to the most suitable.

Key Terms
ذوي القربى (dhu al-qurba): Relatives of the Prophet (peace be upon him) entitled to a share of khums.
علة (illa): The effective cause that justifies a ruling; here, the support (nusrah) for the Prophet.
إجماع آحادي (ijma ahaadi): An isolated consensus not transmitted by multiple chains, thus zanni.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the ijma is not from the companions
B) Because the ijma is ahad (isolated) and thus zanni, while the verse is qat'i
C) Because the Quranic verse is mutashabih
D) Because the illa of nusrah is still present

Key Takeaway
A zanni proof (isolated ijma) cannot abrogate a qat'i general text; furthermore, the absence of a cause does not automatically remove the ruling.

Hanafi Position: Nahi Does Not Imply Fasad
Refutes the claim that prohibition implies corruption in ritual acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on nahi and fasad, and apply the distinction between essence and description to a practical example.

Core Idea
Prohibition does not automatically invalidate an act; the act remains valid in essence but corrupt in description.

This passage from *Fawatih al-Rahamut* defends the Hanafi principle that nahi (prohibition) does not necessitate fasad (invalidity) in shar'i acts. It refutes the opposing Shafi'i view by arguing that the prohibited act is valid in its essence (asl) but defective in its description (wasf). The text also addresses whether the shar'i meaning of a term becomes impossible when prohibited, and asserts the preponderance of the shar'i metaphor over linguistic reality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Key Claim
First, note the Shafi'i position: nahi (prohibition) implies fasad (corruption/invalidity). The Hanafi school denies this automatic implication.
2
State the Hanafi Counter-Claim
The text asserts: 'an iqtidaa al-nahy lil-fasad fi al-shar'iyyat mamnu'; bal huwa muqtadd li al-sihha.' So the prohibition implies validity, not corruption.
The act is sahih bi-aslihi (valid in essence) but fasid bi-wasfihi (corrupt in description).
3
Understand the Essence/Description Distinction
The Hanafi ruling: 'al-munhi 'anna al-shar'i sahih bi-aslihi fasid bi-wasfihi.' This means the act fulfills its essential elements but is defective due to a prohibited attribute (e.g., location, time).
Example: prayer at a usurped place is valid (essence) but sinful (description).
4
Examine the Analogy with 'Qur''
The text uses an analogy: 'qur'' is ambiguous (mujmal) but context clarifies its meaning. Similarly, the word 'salat' (prayer) in a prohibitory context does not lose its shar'i meaning; the context (nahi) does not render it ambiguous.
This shows that nahi does not make the shar'i term impossible (ta'addur).
5
Analyze the Second Counter-Argument
Even if the shar'i meaning were impossible, the text argues that the linguistic reality is not automatically determined; rather, the shar'i metaphor is preponderant (al-majaz al-shar'i arjah). The phrase 'al-zhahir fi al-jawab man' ta'addur al-shar'i' confirms this.
The Hanafi position is that nahi itself implies sihha; only if independent evidence (dalil) indicates fasad does nahi become metaphor for negation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عندها، ألا ترى أن لفظ القرء مشترك، فهو مجمل، مع أنه لا إجمال للقرينة في خصوص هذا، فكذا لفظ الصلاة فتدبر والجواب على أصول الحنفية: أولاً: أن اقتضاء النهي للفساد في الشرعيات ممنوع بل هو مقتض للصحة، فالمنهي عندنا الشرعي صحيح بأصله فاسد بوصفه. وثانياً: أن تساوي المجاز الشرعي والحقيقة اللغوية ممنوع بل المجاز أرجح لقربه، أو فالشرعي أن النهي يحمل على النفي فلا يتعذر الشرعي * هذا المذهب (الرابع) دليله (تعذر) المعنى الشرعي في النهي كما مر في دليل الإمام حجة الإسلام فتعين اللغوي) فأما في الأمر غير متعذر (قلنا) أوّلاً (التعذر) للشرعي (ممنوع) كما عند الشافعية (و) ثانياً (لو سلم) تعذر الشرعي كما هو التحقيق عند محققي أصحابنا عند دلالة الدليل على الفساد (فالتعين) للغوي (ممنوع) بل المراد الهيئة، لأن المتبادر (بل المساواة أيضاً (ممنوعة) فإن الهيئة مفهومة، والأظهر في الجواب منع تعذر الشرعي فإن النهي عندنا للصحة، وأما إن دل الدليل على الفساد لذاته، فالنهي مجاز عن النفي واللفظ الشرعي على حقيقته ولو سلم فالتعين ممنوع فتدبر
Then, do you not see that the word qur' is ambiguous, so it is mujmal, yet there is no ambiguity due to the context in this specific case; similarly the word salat - so reflect. And the answer according to the principles of the Hanafis: First, that the implication of prohibition for corruption in shar'i matters is denied; rather it implies validity. So the prohibited, according to us, is shar'an valid in its essence, corrupt in its description. Second, that the equality of shar'i metaphor and linguistic reality is denied; rather the metaphor is preponderant due to its closeness, or [the claim] that the shar'i [meaning] becomes impossible, so the linguistic is determined. As for the command, it is not impossible. We say: first, the impossibility of the shar'i is denied, as according to the Shafi'is. And second, even if we concede the impossibility of the shar'i – as is the verified position of our verifying scholars when evidence indicates corruption – then the determination of the linguistic is denied; rather what is intended is the form, because what is immediately understood... Even equality is also denied, because the form is understood. The clearest answer is to deny the impossibility of the shar'i, for according to us prohibition implies validity. But if evidence indicates corruption per se, then the prohibition is a metaphor for negation, and the shar'i term remains in its reality. Even if conceded, the determination [of the linguistic] is denied. So reflect.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi disputation defending their position that nahi (prohibition) in shar'i rulings does not necessitate fasad (invalidity). The text begins by analogizing the word salat to the ambiguous word qur' to show that context can remove ambiguity. Then it presents the Hanafi argument: first, nahi implies sihha (validity) rather than fasad; the act is valid in its essence but defective in its description (e.g., prayer at a usurped place). Second, they argue that when a shar'i term becomes impossible due to prohibition, it does not automatically revert to its linguistic meaning; rather, the shar'i metaphor is preponderant. They reject the Shafi'i claim of ta'addur (impossibility) and insist that the shar'i reality remains. The discussion includes multiple rounds of rebuttal, emphasizing that nahi in Hanafi thought is for sihha, and only if specific evidence points to fasad does the prohibition become metaphorical for negation — even then, the shar'i term holds.

Key Terms
النَّهْي (al-nahy): Prohibition; a demand to abstain from an act.
الفساد (al-fasad): Corruption or invalidity of an act in terms of its legal effect.
المجاز الشرعي (al-majaz al-shar'i): A shar'i term used metaphorically, e.g., using 'salat' for du'a in certain contexts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the effect of nahi (prohibition) on a shar'i act?
A) It necessitates absolute invalidity (fasad).
B) It implies validity (sihha) in essence with corruption in description.
C) It makes the act a metaphorical command.
D) It requires the act to be linguistic in meaning.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, prohibition (nahy) does not automatically invalidate an act; the act remains valid in its essence, though its description may be corrupt.
