Does Silence Void Pre-emption? Critiquing the Indication of Silence
Debating whether silence indicates abandonment of pre-emption right

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi debate on whether the pre-emptor's silence indicates abandonment of the right, applying usul principles of dalalat al-hal to critique legal arguments.

Core Idea
Silence alone does not prove abandonment; context matters in interpreting its legal indication.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut presents a critical refinement of the Hanafi position on pre-emption (shuf'ah). The author challenges the majority view that silence after learning of a sale voids the pre-emptor's right. The debate hinges on the usul concept of dalalat al-hal (indication of circumstances): does silence necessarily signal disinterest? The lesson examines the arguments, the critique, and the broader implications for how jurists derive rulings from non-verbal evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Demands
The passage distinguishes between immediate demand (talab al-muwathaba) and confirmatory demand (talab al-taqrir). Understand their definitions and the majority ruling on delaying them.
Majority says delaying immediate demand beyond the session voids pre-emption.
2
State the Majority Hanafi Argument
The majority (incl. al-Karkhi) argues that silence indicates disinterest; otherwise, the buyer would be deceived. This is based on a reading of the hadith 'al-shuf'atu liman wathab'.
They treat silence as a form of expression (dalalat al-hal) that proves abandonment.
3
Present the Author's Critique
The author denies that silence necessarily indicates disinterest. He gives examples: a person may delay claiming a right due to pressing needs. He also questions the source for requiring confirmatory demand.
The critique is methodological: silence is not a strong enough proof to override the general principle that rights are not lost by mere delay.
4
Analyze the Usul Dimension
The debate revolves around the legal value of silence. Is it a definitive indication (qat'i) or presumptive (zanni)? The author argues it is zanni and thus cannot override the default preservation of rights.
This relates to the broader usul principle: al-sukut la yufid al-i'rad (silence does not indicate disinterest) unless there is additional evidence.
5
Evaluate the Thamarah al-Khilaf
If silence does not void the right, the pre-emptor can claim after a reasonable delay, as long as no harm to the buyer. This affects court rulings on pre-emption claims.
The practical consequence: judges should not automatically dismiss pre-emption claims based solely on delay.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنه أيضاً سكوت الشفيع عن طلب مواثبة أو (تقرير) قالوا: للشفعة شروط : منها طلب المواثبة هو أن يطلب الشفعة كما علم بالبيع فإن أخر إلى انقضاء المجلس بطلت شفعته على ما اختاره الإمام الكرخي من الرواية والأكثرون على أنها تبطل كما سكت حتى لو وصل إلى الشفيع كتاب والشفعة في أوله وقرأ الكتاب إلى آخره بطلت الشفعة . ومنها طلب التقرير، وهو طلبها عند البائع إن كان ذا يد أو عند المشتري إن كان كذلك، أو عند العقار ولا بد من الإشهاد فيهما ليمكن إثباتهما عند القاضي، واستدلوا بأن السكوت دليل الإعراض، فإنه لو لم يكن معرضاً لطلبه وإلا لزم التغرير، وهذا القيد فيه نظر فإن دلالة هذا السكوت على الإعراض ممنوعة، إذ كثير ما يسكت رجل عن طلب حقه على إرادته ثم يطلبه بعد يوم أو بعد فراغه عن الأشغال الضرورية كيف وهل هذا الحق إلا كسائر الحقوق؟ ولا تبطل بالتأخير مدة مديدة فكذا هذا ، وأما التغرير فإنما يلزم لو أخر إلى أن يتصرف المشتري، أما التأخير عن المجلس فكلا فإن قلت : قد استدل في «الهداية» بقوله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام : الشفعة لمن واثب قلت: إن صح هذا الحديث فهو دليل مستقل على اشتراط طلب المواثبة لا على دلالة حال الشفيع وقت السكوت عنه على الإعراض، ثم اشتراط طلب التقرير من أين هذا فافهم. (ومنها طلب الخصومة، وهو طلبها عند القاضي وهذا إنما يحتاج إليه إن أعرض المشتري أو البائع عن إعطاء حقه، ولا يجب تعجيله حتى لو أخر مدة مديدة لا تبطل. وعن الإمام محمد أن ليس له التأخير إلى ما وراء الشهرين فتدبر .
And from it also is the silence of the pre-emptor regarding the immediate demand or confirmation. They said: For pre-emption there are conditions: among them is the immediate demand, which is that he demands pre-emption as soon as he learns of the sale, for if he delays until the end of the session, his pre-emption is nullified according to the narration chosen by Imam al-Karkhi, and the majority say that it is nullified as he remained silent, so much so that if a letter reaches the pre-emptor and the pre-emption is at its beginning and he reads the letter to its end, the pre-emption becomes void. And among them is the demand for confirmation, which is to demand it from the seller if he is in hand, or from the buyer if he is, or at the property, and it is necessary to have witnesses in both so that they can be proven before the judge. And they argued that silence is evidence of disinterest, for if he were not disinterested he would have demanded it, otherwise deception would occur. But this condition is questionable, for the indication of this silence regarding disinterest is denied, since often a man remains silent about demanding his right while intending it, then demands it after a day or after finishing essential tasks. How so? Is this right not like other rights? They are not nullified by delay for a long period, so likewise this. As for deception, it only occurs if he delays until the buyer acts, but delay after the session does not. If you say: In al-Hidayah it was argued by his saying, peace be upon him and his family and companions: 'Pre-emption is for the one who makes immediate demand.' I say: If this hadith is authentic, it is an independent proof for the condition of immediate demand, not for the indication of the pre-emptor's state at the time of silence about disinterest. Then the condition of demand for confirmation, where does this come from? So understand. And among them is the demand for litigation, which is to demand it before the judge, and this is only needed if the buyer or seller refuses to give his right, and it is not necessary to hasten it, so much so that if he delays for a long period, it is not nullified. From Imam Muhammad: he may not delay beyond two months. So reflect.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage discusses the conditions of pre-emption (shuf'ah) and whether the silence of the pre-emptor indicates abandonment of the right. The author presents two types of demand: immediate demand (talab al-muwathaba) and confirmatory demand (talab al-taqrir). The majority, including Imam al-Karkhi, hold that delaying the immediate demand until the end of the session nullifies pre-emption. The author then critiques this view, arguing that silence does not necessarily indicate disinterest; a person may remain silent out of busyness and still intend to claim later. The passage also references a hadith used in al-Hidayah but notes that it only establishes the immediate demand condition, not that silence itself indicates disinterest. Finally, it mentions the demand for litigation and a view from Imam Muhammad that delay beyond two months voids the right. The text reflects internal Hanafi debate on this issue.

Key Terms
طلب المواثبة (talab al-muwathaba): Immediate demand for pre-emption upon learning of the sale, before leaving the session.
طلب التقرير (talab al-taqrir): Confirmatory demand made to the seller, buyer, or at the property with witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's critique, why does silence not necessarily void pre-emption?
A) Because the hadith about immediate demand is weak.
B) Because silence may be due to valid reasons such as busyness.
C) Because pre-emption is a right that cannot be waived by inaction.
D) Because the pre-emptor must have witnesses to prove his demand.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the indication of silence (dalalat al-sukut) is context-dependent; for pre-emption, the default is that the right remains unless there is clear evidence of abandonment, and delay due to valid reasons does not automatically void the right.

The Qarin's Tawaf: Hanafi Preference for Prophetic Action over Statement
A fiqh benefit summarizing a cross-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi and Shafi'i proofs for the qarin's tawaf and identify which type of sunnah (fi'l vs qawl) the Hanafis prioritize.

Core Idea
Hanafis require two tawafs for the qarin based on Prophetic action; Shafi'is suffice with one based on a Prophetic statement.

This lesson examines a classic usul dispute that arises when two different forms of sunnah evidence appear to conflict: the actual practice (fi'l) of the Prophet versus his verbal statement (qawl). The case of the qarin's tawaf provides a clear example of how each school weighs these sources differently, revealing fundamental methodological principles in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ikhtilaf
State the exact point of disagreement: how many tawafs and sa'y does the qarin need?
Qarin = one performing Hajj and Umrah together in one ihram.
2
State each school's proof
Identify the textual evidence (dalil naqli) used by Hanafis and Shafi'is.
Hanafis rely on the Prophet's action (fi'l), Shafi'is on his statement (qawl from Tirmidhi).
3
Classify the sunnah type
Categorize each proof: is it fi'l (action) or qawl (statement)? Determine its epistemological weight in Hanafi usul.
Fi'l of the Prophet is considered a stronger indicator of obligation when it is unambiguous.
4
Analyze the Hanafi preference
Explain the Hanafi reasoning for giving precedence to the action over the statement, considering the possibility of interpretation (ta'wil) of the hadith.
The Shafi'i hadith may be interpreted as one tawaf for both or as one tawaf for each; the action clarifies the ambiguity.
5
Note the incomplete text
Acknowledge that the source passage is cut off; the full Hanafi counter-argument is not provided.
This limitation means we rely on standard Hanafi usul principles to complete the reasoning.

Source Text

فائدة اختلفوا في أن القارن عليه طوافان وسعيان للعمرة والحج أو واحد لهما، فإمامنا وصاحباه ذهبوا إلى الأول والشافعي إلى الثاني، واستدل بما مر عن رواية الترمذي، وبقوله

Commentary
This is a fiqh benefit (fa'idah) summarizing a well-known dispute: the qarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah together) must perform two tawafs and two sa'y according to Hanafis, one for Umrah and one for Hajj. Al-Shafi'i holds that one each suffices, relying on the hadith of Ibn Umar transmitted by Tirmidhi: 'One tawaf and one sa'y suffice for both.' The Hanafi position relies on the action of the Prophet (two tawafs) as reported by Nasa'i. The text is cut off, so the full Hanafi counter-argument is not present.

Key Terms
القارن (al-qarin): One who enters ihram for both Hajj and Umrah without separation
طواف (tawaf): Circumambulation of the Kaaba, a pillar of Hajj and Umrah
سعي (sa'y): Walking seven times between Safa and Marwah, a pillar of Hajj and Umrah
فعل النبي (fi'l al-nabi): Action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as a source of law

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Two tawafs: one for Umrah and one for Hajj.
C) Three tawafs.
D) None, because qiran is invalid in Hanafi.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes an explicit Prophetic action over a general Prophetic statement when deriving the ruling for the qarin, illustrating a foundational usul principle of preference (tarjih).

The Permissibility of Delaying Interpretive Bayan (Bayan al-Tafsir)
Ruling with proofs on delaying bayan al-tafsir, with dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that the delay of bayan al-tafsir is permissible until the time of need, and distinguish it from bayan al-taghyir.

Core Idea
Hanafis permit delaying tafsir until needed; taghyir cannot be delayed.

In this passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut, the author explains the Hanafi position on delaying bayan (clarification) of a divine command. The key distinction is between interpretive bayan (bayan al-tafsir), which explains an ambiguous text, and amending bayan (bayan al-taghyir), which changes a ruling. The Hanafis argue that tafsir can be delayed until the time of need, while taghyir cannot. This lesson will walk through the proofs and the inter-school dispute.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish tafsir from taghyir
Identify the two types of bayan: tafsir (interpretive explanation) clarifies an ambiguous (mujmal) text, while taghyir (amending explanation) changes or abrogates a ruling. According to the Hanafi school, only tafsir may be delayed.
This distinction is crucial because the ruling on delay depends on it.
2
State the Hanafi position
The chosen view (al-mukhtar) is that delaying bayan al-tafsir until the time of need is permissible. The text says: 'وأما بيان التفسير إلى وقت الحاجة فالمختار الجواز'.
The 'time of need' is when the obligation becomes immediately binding.
3
Examine the primary Quranic proof (75:16-19)
Analyze the verse: 'ثُمَّ إِنَّ عَلَيْنَا بَيَانَهُ'. The word 'thumma' indicates delay (tarakhi). Thus, the promise of bayan comes after the initial revelation, proving that explanation can be postponed.
The Hanafi response to objections about the meaning of 'thumma' is that it is for delay, not just sequence.
4
Analyze the opposing argument
The opponents (Hanbalis, al-Sayrafi, Mu'tazila) require simultaneous bayan. They cite Quran 5:67 (يَأَيُّهَا الرَّسُولُ بَلِغْ) claiming it commands immediate conveyance. The Hanafi response is that the verse does not necessitate immediacy; failure to convey immediately does not negate the message.
Al-Ash'ari reportedly convinced al-Sayrafi to retract his view.
5
Apply to a concrete scenario
Consider a modern ambiguous command: Allah says 'Pay zakat' but does not specify the nisab or rate. According to the Hanafi view, the detailed explanation can be delayed until the time of payment, as long as the general obligation is accepted.
This flexibility allows for gradual understanding and implementation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيه أي في التأخير (مصلحة) يطلع عليها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم، فيجب التأخير حينئذ المنكرون (قالوا) قال الله تعالى: ﴿يَأَيُّهَا الرَّسُولُ بَلِغْ مَا أُنزِلَ إِلَيْكَ حَتَّى [المائدة: ٦٧] والأمر ههنا للفور وإلا فوجوب التبليغ (مطلقاً سواء كان على الفور أو متراخياً (معلوم عقلاً) من الرسالة فلا حاجة إلى الإبانة (قلنا) لا نسلم أنه للفور، وأما إبانة التبليغ مع كونه معلوماً عقلاً فلأنها لفائدة، و(فائدته تقوية العقل أي تقوية ما حكم به العقل (بالنقل، أقول : يدل على ذلك أي عدم كونه للفور ما بعده) هو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِن لَّمْ تَفْعَلْ فَمَا بَلَّغْتَ رسالته [المائدة: ٦٧] فإن عدم فعل التبليغ على الفور لا يوجب عدم تبليغ الرسالة رأساً، وهذا ظاهر، إلا أن يتحمل التكلف ويقال : لما كان وجوب التبليغ الفوري عندهم فتركه ترك التبليغ المستحق الذي هو الرسالة فتدبر (وقد يجاب في «التحرير» بأنه ظاهر في تبليغ المتلو) وهو القرآن الشريف، فلا يلزم منه إلا عدم جواز تأخير تبليغه لا عدم جواز تأخير التبليغ مطلقاً، والمدعي هذا دون ذلك وفيه ما فيه فإن كلمة ما عامة والتخصيص من غير دليل على أنه نزل في تبليغ حكم غير متلو كما ورد في بعض الروايات ولا يتوهم أنها ليست على عمومها، فإن بعض ما أنزل أسرار بين الله ورسوله صلوات الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه فلا يصح التبليغ، لأن الآية ظاهرة في العموم، فلا تسمع دعوى أن بعض ما أنزل أسرار ممنوع التبليغ إلا عن البعض الغير المتأهلين وهو لا ينافي وجوب التبليغ مطلقاً فافهم .
مسألة
لا يجوز تأخير البيان أي بيان التفسير عن وقت الحاجة إليه (وهو وقت تعلق التكليف تنجيزاً موسعاً كان التكليف أو مضيقاً (وقيل) في «التحرير» هو وقت تعلق التكليف التنجيزي (مضيقاً) وهذا التخصيص تحكم فإنه لو تأخر عن وقت تعلق التكليف فيكون تكليفاً بالمجهول طلباً لإتيانه ولو موسعاً، وإتيان المجهول محال من المكلف فلا يجوز هذا التأخير (إلا عند مجوز تكليف ما لا يطاق لكن ينبغي أن لا يقع عندهم أيضاً. أما) تأخير بيان التفسير (إلى وقت الحاجة فالمختار الجواز وأما بيان التغيير فلا يجوز تأخيره كما مر (وعند الحنابلة) والصيرفي (وجماعة من (المعتزلة كعبد الجبار والجبائي وابنه (المنع) أي منع جواز التأخير إلى وقت الحاجة، بل يجب المقارنة إلا أن الاسفراييني ذكر أن الأشعري قدس سره نزل ضيفاً على الصيرفي فناظره وهداه إلى الحق فرجع عن المنع إلى الجواز ( وأبو الحسين جوز التأخير في البيان التفصيلي) دون الإجمالي لنا :أولاً: قوله تعالى : ﴿لا تُحرك بِهِ لِسَانَكَ لِتَعْجَلَ إِنَّ عَلَيْنَا جَمعَهُ وَقُرَ انَهُ فَإِذَا قَرَأَنَهُ فَاتَّبِعْ قُرْهَانَهُ ثُمَّ إِنَّ عَلَيْنَا بَيَانَهُ ﴾ [القيامة : ١٦ - ١٩) وثم للتراخي فيجوز التراخي فإن قلت البيان عام لتخصيص العام فينبغي أن يجوز مؤخراً، قلت : البيان يطلق في العرف على التفسير غالباً ، فهو المتبادر على أنه يخصص بما عداه لدليل قاطع قد أن الإضافة جنسية، فثبت تأخير جنس البيان، وقد مر عدم جواز تأخير التغيير فلزم تحقق الجنس في التفسير، فإنه هو الحق، وإلا لزم عدم جواز مقارنة بيان التفسير أيضاً، هذا ولنا فيه كلام من وجهين :
الأول : أن المراد بالبيان تبليغ نظم المنزل، كما ورد في الصحيح عن ابن عباس أنها نزلت لما كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم يتعب لسانه في سرعة القراءة على محاذاة قراءة جبريل خشية النسيان فنزلت والمعنى : لا تحرك لسانك بالقرآن عند تبليغ المبلغ لأجل التعجيل، فإن علينا جمعه في صدرك، وعلينا قراءتك إياه : فإذا قرآنا بلسان جبريل فاقرأه على قراءته بعد ذلك، ثم علينا تبيينه إلى الخلق بلسانك، ومع هذا الاحتمال لا يقوم حجة فتأمل فيه
والثاني : سلمنا أن البيان بمعنى التفسير لكن كلمة ثم إنما دخلت على الجملة، فلو أفاد التراخي أفاد التراخي في ثبوت مضمون الثانية بعد مضمون الأولى فكون البيان على الله مؤخر عن كون الجمع في الصدر والقراءة أَتَتَّخِذُنَا هُزُوا قَالَ أَعُوذُ بِاللَّهِ أَنْ أَكُونَ مِنَ الْجَهِلِينَ قَالُوا ادْعُ لَنَا رَبَّكَ يُبَين لَنَا مَا هِيَ قَالَ إِنَّهُ يَقُولُ إِنَّهَا بَقَرَةٌ لا فَارِضُ وَلَا بِكْرُ عَوَان بَيْنَ ذَلِكَ فَافْعَلُوا مَا تُؤْمَرُونَ ) [البقرة : ٦٧ و ٦٨] إلى آخر القصة والبقرة المأمورة كانت معينة) عند الله (بدليل البيان مؤخراً) ولو لم يكن بياناً لكان المأمور متجدداً، وهو باطل (فإنه لم يؤمر بمتجدد اتفاقاً) فتعين البيانية مع التأخير، ولا يخفى على المتأمل أن هذا إن كان بياناً كان بيان تغيير لا تفسير فليس من الباب، نعم : استدل بها في كتاب الشافعية حيث أخذوا المسألة عامة (وأجيب بأنها) كانت مطلقة في ابتداء الأمر، ثم نسخ إطلاقها، وتعينت بعد السؤال تشديداً عليهم) لما استهزؤوا وطلبوا بيان النص مع علمهم بالمراد، فلا نسلم أنه لم يؤمروا بمتجدد، نعم : لم يؤمروا بمباين ما أمروا به أوّلاً، بل أمروا بفرد من أفراده (القول ابن عباس رئيس المفسرين الذي قال فيه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم: «اللهم علمه الكتاب» رواه البخاري (لو ذبحوا أي بقرة لأجزأهم ، لكنهم شدّدوا على أنفسهم فشدّد الله عليهم) رواه ابن جرير وابن أبي حاتم من طرق لكن بلفظ : لو أخذوا أدنى بقرة. كذا في «الدرر المنثورة»، وفيها أيضاً برواية البزار عن أبي هريرة مرفوعاً عن النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم: «أن بني إسرائيل لو أخذوا أدنى بقرة لجزاهم ذلك» أو «الأجزأت عنهم وفي رواية ابن أبي حاتم بزيادة، لكنهم شدّدوا فشدّد الله عليهم وبرواية ابن جرير عن قتادة قال : ذكر لنا أن النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم كان يقول : إنما أمر القوم بأدنى بقرة، لكنهم لما
In it (the delay) there is a benefit known to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and Companions), so delay is obligatory then. The deniers said: Allah said: 'O Messenger, convey what has been sent down to you...' [5:67] and the command here is for immediacy, otherwise obligation of conveyance is absolute, whether immediate or delayed, known rationally from the message, so there is no need for clarification. We said: We do not accept that it is for immediacy. As for clarifying conveyance despite being known rationally, it is for a benefit, and its benefit is strengthening reason i.e., strengthening what reason has judged by transmission. I say: What indicates that it is not for immediacy is what follows His saying: 'If you do not, then you have not conveyed His message' [5:67]; for failure to convey immediately does not entail failure to convey the message entirely. This is apparent, unless one forces [an interpretation] and says: since immediate conveyance is obligatory in their view, leaving it is leaving the required conveyance which is the message, so reflect. And it may be answered in 'al-Tahrir' that it is apparent in conveying the recited [text] i.e., the noble Quran, so it only entails impermissibility of delaying its conveyance, not impermissibility of delaying conveyance absolutely. The claimant is this without that, and there is something in it. For the word 'ma' is general, and specification without evidence that it was revealed concerning conveying a non-recited ruling as mentioned in some narrations, and do not imagine that it is not general, for some of what was revealed are secrets between Allah and His Messenger, so conveyance is not valid, because the verse is apparent in generality, so the claim that some of what was revealed are secrets prohibited from being conveyed except to some who are not qualified is not heard, and it does not negate the obligation of conveyance absolutely, so understand.
Issue
It is not permissible to delay the bayan i.e., the bayan of tafsir beyond the time of need for it (which is the time of attachment of obligation immediately, whether the obligation is expansive or narrow. And it was said in 'al-Tahrir': it is the time of attachment of immediate obligation narrowly. This specification is arbitrary, for if it is delayed beyond the time of attachment of obligation, then it becomes an obligation of the unknown, demanding its performance even if expansive, and performing the unknown is impossible for the obligatee, so this delay is not permissible except for one who permits obligating the impossible. But it should not occur in their view either. As for) delaying bayan of tafsir (to the time of need, the chosen view is permissibility. As for bayan of taghyir, its delay is not permissible as passed. (And according to the Hanbalis) and al-Sayrafi (and a group of Mu'tazila like Abd al-Jabbar, al-Jubba'i and his son (the prohibition) i.e., prohibition of delaying to the time of need; rather, simultaneity is obligatory, except that al-Isfara'ini mentioned that al-Ash'ari (may Allah sanctify his secret) stayed as a guest of al-Sayrafi, debated him, guided him to the truth, so he retracted from prohibition to permissibility. (And Abu al-Husayn permitted delay in detailed bayan) but not summary. Our proofs: First: His saying: 'Do not move your tongue with it to hasten it. Indeed, upon Us is its collection and its recitation. So when We have recited it, then follow its recitation. Then indeed, upon Us is its explanation' [75:16-19]. And 'thumma' is for delay, so delay is permissible. If you say: bayan is general, so specification of the general should be permissible delayed. I say: bayan in custom is mostly used for tafsir, so it is the predominant meaning, and it can be specified by what is other than it due to conclusive evidence, and the addition is generic, so the delay of the genus of bayan is established, and the impermissibility of delaying taghyir has passed, so the genus is realized in tafsir, for it is the truth; otherwise, the permissibility of simultaneity of tafsir bayan would also be impermissible. This and we have speech in it from two aspects: First: that what is meant by bayan is conveying the arrangement of the revealed [text], as came in the authentic [hadith] from Ibn Abbas that it was revealed when the Messenger used to tire his tongue in speed of reading matching Jibra'il's reading for fear of forgetfulness, so it was revealed. The meaning: Do not move your tongue with the Quran when conveying the message for haste. Indeed, upon Us is its collection in your chest, and upon Us is your recitation of it; so when We have recited it by the tongue of Jibra'il, then recite it according to his recitation after that; then upon Us is its clarification to the creation by your tongue. And with this probability, it is not a proof, so reflect. And the second: We grant that bayan is in the sense of tafsir, but the word 'thumma' enters the sentence. If it indicates delay, it indicates delay in the existence of the content of the second after the content of the first. So the existence of bayan from Allah is delayed after the collection in the chest and the recitation upon him, and this does not entail the existence of bayan after the ambiguous, delayed. Rather, the truth is that 'thumma' here is for transition from one topic to another, due to no delay between the two contents. And the meaning (Allah knows best) is that upon Us is collection and recitation, then upon Us is something else which is bayan and tafsir, so understand. (And) our (second proof: the giving of prayer and zakat (for example)) for they are ambiguous (clarified by act and speech gradually, and were not clarified immediately after revelation, as appears from tracing histories. (And) our (third proof: the permissibility of intending belief in summary, then belief (in detail) after bayan, then action) in that delay contains a great benefit, so it is permissible. (And he argued) for the chosen view also (by His saying): 'Indeed, Allah commands you to slaughter a cow. They said: Do you take us in mockery? He said: I seek refuge in Allah from being among the ignorant. They said: Call upon your Lord to clarify to us what it is. He said: Indeed, He says: It is a cow neither old nor young, middle-aged between that; so do what you are commanded.' [2:67-68] to the end of the story. And the commanded cow was (specific) with Allah (by the evidence of bayan delayed). And if it were not bayan, then the commanded would be renewed, which is false. (For they were not commanded with something renewed by agreement.) So bayan with delay is established. And it is not hidden from the contemplator that if this is bayan, it is bayan of taghyir not tafsir, so it is not from the topic. Yes: it was argued with it in the book of the Shafi'is where they took the issue general. (And it was answered that it) was absolute in the beginning, then its absoluteness was abrogated, and it became specific after the question as a severity upon them) when they mocked and sought clarification of the text while knowing the intent. So we do not accept that they were commanded with something renewed. Yes: they were not commanded with something contrary to what they were commanded initially; rather, they were commanded with an individual from its individuals. (The saying of Ibn Abbas, the chief of interpreters, about whom the Messenger said: 'O Allah, teach him the Book' - Bukhari narrated: (If they had slaughtered any cow, it would have sufficed them, but they made it difficult on themselves, so Allah made it difficult on them) narrated by Ibn Jarir and Ibn Abi Hatim via multiple chains but with wording: 'If they had taken the lowest cow.' This is in 'al-Durr al-Manthur', and in it also via al-Bazzar from Abu Hurayra raised to the Prophet: 'That the Children of Israel if they had taken the lowest cow, it would have sufficed them' or 'it would have been accepted from them.' And in a narration of Ibn Abi Hatim with an addition: 'But they made it difficult, so Allah made it difficult on them.' And via Ibn Jarir from Qatada who said: It was mentioned to us that the Prophet used to say: 'Indeed the people were commanded with the lowest cow, but when they...'
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the permissibility of delaying interpretive bayan (bayan al-tafsir) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author begins by stating the general principle: it is not permissible to delay bayan (i.e., explaining ambiguous texts) beyond the time of need, where need is defined as the time when the obligation becomes immediately binding, whether the obligation is expansive (muwassa') or narrow (mudayyaq). However, the chosen view (al-mukhtar) is that delaying tafsir bayan until the time of need is permissible. This is contrasted with bayan al-taghyir (amending bayan), which cannot be delayed. The author then presents the opposition: the Hanbalis, al-Sayrafi, and a group of Mu'tazila (like Abd al-Jabbar, al-Jubba'i, and his son) prohibit delaying bayan to the time of need; they require simultaneity. He notes that al-Ash'ari convinced al-Sayrafi to retract. Abu al-Husayn permitted delay in detailed bayan but not in summary bayan.

The author provides three proofs for the Hanafi position. First, from the Quran (75:16-19), where 'thumma' indicates delay, so bayan can be delayed. He addresses two objections: (1) that the verse might refer to conveying the Quranic text, not tafsir, and (2) that 'thumma' indicates sequence, not necessarily delay in the sense of postponed explanation. He refutes both. Second, he points to the gradual revelation of rulings on prayer and zakat, which were not explained immediately after revelation but over time. Third, he argues that delayed bayan allows for a benefit: first believing in summary, then in detail, then acting, which is a gradual process.

Finally, he discusses the story of the cow (2:67-68) as an argument used by the Shafi'is. The Hanafi response is that the cow command was initially absolute, then abrogated to specificity as a punishment, so it does not prove permissible delay of tafsir. He cites Ibn Abbas that any cow would have sufficed, but they made it difficult. This story is an example of bayan taghyir, not tafsir, so it does not apply to the ruling on tafsir.

Key Terms
البيان (al-bayan): Specification (takhsis) and explanation (tafsir) of an ambiguous (mujmal) text. The author distinguishes between bayan al-tafsir (interpretive explanation) and bayan al-taghyir (amending explanation).
التفسير (al-tafsir): The explanation of the meaning of an ambiguous (mujmal) text. In this passage, it is the type of bayan that is permitted to be delayed until the time of need.
التغيير (al-taghyir): The amendment or alteration of a ruling (naskh or specification that changes the previous ruling). Unlike tafsir, taghyir cannot be delayed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, delaying which type of bayan is permissible until the time of need?
A) Bayan al-taghyir (amending bayan)
B) Bayan al-tafsir (interpretive bayan)
C) Bayan of the Quranic text itself
D) Bayan of rulings related to prayer only

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits delaying interpretive bayan (tafsir) until the time of need, but never delays amending bayan (taghyir).

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
10 min
The Epistemological Status of Khabar Wahid: Zann or Qat'?
Analyzing the debate over khabar wahid's epistemological value

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on khabar wahid's certainty, explain the logical argument against the opposing school, and evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the epistemological difference.

Core Idea
Khabar wahid yields probability, not certainty — the possibility of error remains even when the report seems preponderant.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut plunges into a foundational usul dispute: does a single-narrator report (khabar wahid) produce certainty (qat') or only probability (zann)? The issue is not merely academic — it affects how we weigh revealed evidence and derive rulings. The author presents a sophisticated logical exchange between the Hanafi school and the Mutakallimin/Shafi'i position, then resolves it firmly in favor of the Hanafi view. You will walk through the arguments, the logical analysis of preponderance and preventers, and see why Hanafis insist that khabar wahid remains zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalalah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opposing claim
What does the opponent (Mutakallimin/Shafi'i) assert about khabar wahid? Find the claim that it yields certainty through a chain of premises: consensus gives probability, probability is preponderant, remove ambiguity, efficient cause present.
The opponent argues that probability itself becomes preponderant with certainty, so the preventer (ambiguity) is removed.
2
Locate the Hanafi counter-premise
The Hanafi response denies that probability is preponderant with certainty. Identify the specific point of denial: 'we do not concede that probability is preponderant with probability.' Understand why this denial blocks the opponent's conclusion.
The Hanafis shift the focus to the persistence of the possibility of error, even if preponderance exists.
3
Analyze the logical refutation (conditional propositions)
The text uses logical tools: universal conditional vs. universal possible. How does the Hanafi response show that the opponent's premises do not necessitate certainty? Follow the explanation about 'probability is preponderant as long as it exists' and the possibility of non-preponderance in absence.
The key insight: even if the report gives probability at a given moment, that probability is not guaranteed to persist because the report's thubut is zanni.
4
Examine the second preventer
Even if the first preventer (total ambiguity) is removed, a second preventer remains: the possibility that the opposite side is preponderated. Explain how this second preventer is inherent to zann and prevents qat'.
The Hanafi answer: 'the preventer of certainty is ambiguity and the possibility of the opposite side as preponderated. Here, although the first preventer is removed, the second takes its place.'
5
Apply to a concrete example (salat and riba)
The passage gives the examples of the terms 'salat' and 'riba'. Even when defined by khabar wahid, the mind grasps the meaning, but this grasping is based on strong probability, not absolute certainty. Contrast this with preponderance by personal opinion (ra'y) which does not yield even immediate understanding.
This example illustrates the thamarah al-khilaf: the ruling derived from khabar wahid is zanni, whereas rulings from mutawatir or Qur'an are qati.

وهو الأصل الأول/ الكتاب صاحب «الكشف» إنكاراً بليغاً واستدل بما أشار إليه المصنف بقوله (لنا) أن الحكم الثابت منه لازم بقطعي هو الكتاب مثلاً وظني هو البيان و اللازم من القطع والظن إنما هو الظن) فالحكم الثابت المظنون وغاية ما يقال من قبلهم أن البيان إنما يفيد تبادر أحد المعنيين، فإنه إنما يفيد معرفة معنى اللفظ وتبادر المعنى من قطعي الثبوت يوجب القطع البتة، وذلك لأن احتمال عدم إرادة هذا المعنى من اللفظ الذي تبين وضعه واستعماله بالمبين احتمال على خلاف المتبادر . احتمال لا يعدّ عرفاً ولغة، فلا يضر القطع بالمعنى الأعم، وهذا بعينه كما يقال : النص قطعي مع احتماله التأويل، وعلى هذا فلا نسلم أن هذا الحكم لازم من القطعي والظني بمعنى أنهما مقدمتاه، بل من القطعي المتبادر منه هو إنما الظن في سبب التبادر، وإن أريد أن الظني له دخل ما في الإفادة فلا نسلم أنه يفيد الظن وهذا بخلاف الظاهر المصروف بظني، فإن هذا الصرف لا يوجب تبادر المصروف إليه بل إنما يفهم بملاحظة القرينة، فإذا كانت القرينة مظنونة محتملة ففهم المعنى أيضاً محتمل فتأمل فإنه موضع تأمل القاطعون (قالوا: خبر الواحد يوجب الظن (قطعاً لأن قد أجمع عليه إجماعاً قاطعاً (والظن مرجح قطعاً) لأنه ضد التساوي، وإذا ثبت الترجيح قطعاً (فبطل المساواة قطعاً) وهو ظاهر فارتفع المانع عن القطع وهو الإجمال (قطعاً، وقد فرض المقتضى للقطع قطعاً لأنه الكتاب أو الخبر المتواتر فلزم الحكم قطعاً (قلنا) هذا (منقوض بمعرفة المراد من المشترك بالرأي غير الخبر الذي هو يفيد الظن قطعاً) فإن مقدمات الدليل جارية فيه، أقول) الحل لدليلهم (أنا لا نسلم أن الظن مرجح (ظنّاً) فلم يرتفع المانع قطعاً إن قيل : لو كان الظن مرجحاً (ظناً لجاز اجتماع بمرجح قطعاً بل) إنما يرجح الظن مع المساواة وهما لأن مقابل الظن جائز وهماً فلزم اجتماع الضدين وهماً (مع أن إمكان اجتماع الضدين محال عقلاً، قلت: (اللازم من ترجيح الظن ظناً (صدق قولنا : الظن ليس وهماً لأنه مقابلة وصدقه يجوز بانتفاء الظن وهما لأن السالبة قد تصدق بانتفاء الموضع، وهذا الانتفاء بنا على أن الخبر من (الآحاد فيجوز نسيان الراوي فيجوز ارتفاعه من البين (والسر) فيه أن قولنا : الظن مرجح قطعاً مشروطة عامة، فإن معناه مرجح ما دام ظناً، وقولنا : الظن ليس بمرجح ممكنة عامة و أن الموجبة المشروطة لا تنافي السالبة الممكنة فيجوز الاجتماع بينهما) أي بين هاتين القضيتين فلا يلزم الاجتماع بين الظن والمساواة فتفكر) فإن فيه كلاماً ظاهراً، فإن الوصف في هاتين القضيتين عين الذات، فقولنا: الظن ضرورية معناه مرجح ما دام موجوداً، ولا شك في التنافي بين الضرورية والممكنة، فإن قلت : مقصوده أن قولنا : المظنون راجح قطعاً مشروطة عامة والمظنون ليس راجحاً، وهما ممكنة عامة، قلت: لا ينفع فإن المستدل لم يأخذهما في الدليل، وإنما أخذ ترجيح الظن فلا يضره، وربما يوجه بأن الضرورة فيه مقيدة بزمان الوجود، فإن معناه الظن مرجح ما دام موجوداً، وإمكان عدم الترجيح حال العدم، فالمراد بالمشروطة المشروطة بقيد الوجود، وبالممكنة الممكنة بهذا النحو من الإمكان كذا قرر مطلع الأسرار الإلهية والدي قدس سره العزيز. ثم قرر الدليل بأن الظن مرجح قطعاً ما دام موجوداً، فارتفع المانع في حال وجوده : مرجح قطعاً فلزم القطعية حال وجوده فتم المطلوب، لأن الدعوى القطعية بعد تبيين الخبر، ولا يجوز في تلك الحال عدم الترجيح ولو وهماً، فإنه تجويز اجتماع الضدين، ثم قرر الجواب بأن إفادة الخبر الظن قطعاً، ممنوع فإنه يجوز ارتفاع الخبر من البين لكونه ظني الثبوت فيرتفع الظن به فلا هذا الظن وهذا لأن نفس وجوده وإن كان مقطوعاً، لأنه يعلم بالوجدان، يرجح لكنه يمكن زواله بزوال الخبر، فلا يكون مقطوعاً بقاؤه، فلا يفيد القطع بالترجيح، وأما نفس وجود الظن من غير القطع فلا يفيد أصلاً هذا ولا يظهر لهذا وجه، فإن إفادة الخبر الظن مما أجمع عليه كما إن شاء الله تعالى. ومنع المقدمة الإجماعية لا يجوز. فبعد ملاحظة سيجيء هذا الإجماع لا يمكن منع إفادة الخبر الظن وبعد التنزل للمستدل أن يقول الخبر مفيد للظن قطعاً فارتفع المانع حين وجود الخبر قطعاً، فلزم القطع بالحكم في تلك الحال قطعاً، وهو المطلوب، فإنهم لا يدعون القطع بعد ظهور عدم وجود البيان وكذب الخبر فتدبر، فإذن الحق في الجواب ما أفاده هو قدس سره من منع ارتفاع المانع فإن المانع من القطع الإجمال، وجواز الطرف المقابل مرجوحاً، وههنا وإن ارتفع المانع الأول لكن قام الثاني مقامه، فإن الظن بالشيء يوجب تجويز الطرف المقابل مرجوحاً، هذا ثم لهم أن يقرروا بأن الخبر مفيد للظن بالوضع والاستعمال قطعاً، وهذا الظن يوجب التبادر قطعاً. وتبادر المراد من القطعي رافع للمانع قطعاً لوجود المقتضى، وبالجملة أن هذا الظن موجب للتبادر، وهو يوجب القطع، وكيف لا يوجب التبادر وأنه متى علم أن الصلاة في الشرع ما هو ولو بخبر الواحد والربا ما هو يتسارع الذهن عند سماع اللفظين إلى معناهما الشرعي مكابرة، وليس هذا إلا كما إذا أخبر الخليل أو الأصمعي أن لفضاً وضع في لغة العرب لهذا المعنى يتسارع الذهن عند السماع إليه البتة وهذا أولى منه فإن هذا الظن قوي معاضد بالإجماع، وهذا هو الذي ريم في الاستدلال المشهور بأن الحكم بعد تبيين الخبر مضاف إلى القطعي فيكون مقطوعاً يعني أن الحكم بعد تبيين الخبر يستفاد منه أن الحكم بعد تبيين الخبر يستفاد منه لأجل التبادر فيفيد القطع. لأن المراد به المعنى الأعم، وهو الذي لا يحتمل المقابل احتمالاً ناشئاً عن دليل. وبعد التبادر أحد معنيي فاحتمال عدم الإرادة كاحتمال التأويل في النص فلا اعتداد به، وهذا بخلاف ترجيح المشترك بالرأي فإنه لا يوجب التبادر فتأمل فيه فإنه موضع تأمل.
He said: The first principle / the author of 'al-Kashf' strongly denied and argued with what the author indicated by his saying (for us) that the ruling established from it is necessary from a certain (qat'i) source like the Book and from a probable (zanni) source like the explanation (bayan), and the necessary from certainty and probability is only probability. So the ruling is established as probable. The utmost that can be said by them is that explanation only conveys the immediate understanding (tabādur) of one of the two meanings, for it only conveys knowledge of the meaning of the word, and the immediate understanding of a meaning from a certain source necessitates certainty absolutely, because the possibility that this meaning is not intended from the word whose usage and conventional meaning have been explained by the explainer is a possibility contrary to the immediate understanding, a possibility not counted customarily or linguistically, so it does not harm the certainty of the general meaning. This is exactly as it is said: the text (nass) is certain despite its possibility of interpretation. Accordingly, we do not concede that this ruling is necessitated from the certain and the probable in the sense that they are its two premises; rather from the certain that which is immediately understood is only probability in the cause of immediate understanding. If it is intended that the probable has some role in the conveyance, we do not concede that it conveys probability. This is unlike the apparent (zahir) that is diverted by a probable (zanni) [indication], for this diversion does not necessitate immediate understanding of the diverted meaning, but rather it is understood only by considering the contextual evidence (qarīna). So if the contextual evidence is probable and possible, then understanding the meaning is also possible. Reflect, for it is a place of reflection for those who assert certainty. They said: A single-narrator report (khabar wāhid) necessitates probability (zann) with certainty because there is decisive consensus (ijma' qāti') on it, and probability is a preponderant with certainty because it is the opposite of equality. And when preponderance is established with certainty, then equality is invalidated with certainty, which is apparent, so the preventer of certainty, which is ambiguity (ijmāl), is removed with certainty, and the efficient cause for certainty is assumed with certainty because it is the Book or the mutawātir report, so the ruling is necessitated with certainty. We said: This is refuted by knowing the intended meaning from a homonym (mushtarak) through opinion (ra'y) not through a report which conveys probability with certainty, for the premises of the argument apply to it. I say: The solution to their argument is that we do not concede that probability is preponderant with probability, so the preventer is not removed with certainty. If it is said: if probability were preponderant with probability, then it would be possible for two preponderants to coexist? Rather, probability only preponderates when there is equality and a possibility, because the opposite of probability is permissible as a mere possibility, so it would necessitate the coexistence of two opposites as a mere possibility, while the possibility of the coexistence of opposites is rationally impossible. I said: The necessary from the preponderance of probability with probability is the truth of our statement: probability is not a mere possibility because it is its opposite, and its truth is possible by the absence of probability as a mere possibility, because a negative can be true by the absence of the subject. This absence is based on the report being from the ahad (khabar wāhid), so it is possible that the narrator forgot, so it is possible that it disappears from the picture. The secret is that our statement 'probability is preponderant with certainty' is a universal conditional, meaning it is preponderant as long as it is probability, and our statement 'probability is not preponderant' is a universal possible, and a conditional affirmative does not contradict a possible negative, so coexistence between them is permissible, meaning between these two propositions, so the coexistence between probability and equality is not necessary, so reflect. For there is apparent speech in it, because the description in these two propositions is identical to the essence. So our statement 'probability is necessary' means it is preponderant as long as it exists, and there is no doubt about the contradiction between the necessary and the possible. If you say: His intent is that our statement 'the probable is preponderant with certainty' is a universal conditional, and 'the probable is not preponderant' is a universal possible, I say: It does not help, because the arguer did not take them in the argument; he only took the preponderance of probability, so it does not harm him. Perhaps it can be directed that the necessity in it is restricted to the time of existence, i.e., its meaning is that probability is preponderant as long as it exists, and the possibility of non-preponderance is in the state of non-existence. So what is meant by the conditional is the conditional restricted by the restriction of existence, and by the possible is the possible in this manner of possibility. Thus decided the one who ascends to the divine secrets, may Allah sanctify his noble spirit. Then he decided the argument that probability is preponderant with certainty as long as it exists, so the preventer is removed in the state of its existence: it is preponderant with certainty, so certainty is necessitated in the state of its existence, so the desired is achieved, because the claim of certainty is after the explanation (tabyīn) of the report, and it is not permissible in that state the absence of preponderance even as a mere possibility, for it would be permitting the coexistence of opposites. Then he decided the answer that the report's conveying probability with certainty is denied, for it is possible that the report disappears from the picture because it is probable in transmission (zannī al-thubūt), so the probability due to it disappears. So neither is this probability [of preponderance] nor is that [the original probability?]. This is because the mere existence of the report, although it is certain (known by introspection), preponderates, but it can disappear with the disappearance of the report, so its persistence is not certain, so it does not convey certainty in preponderance. As for the mere existence of probability without certainty, it conveys nothing at all. This has no apparent face, for the report's conveyance of probability is a matter of consensus as Allah wills. Denying the consensus premise is not permissible. After noting this consensus that will come, it is not possible to deny the report's conveyance of probability. After conceding for the arguer that the report conveys probability with certainty, the preventer is removed at the time of the report's existence with certainty, so certainty of the ruling is necessitated in that state with certainty, which is the desired. For they do not claim certainty after the appearance of the absence of explanation and the falsehood of the report, so reflect. So the truth in the answer is what he (may his secret be sanctified) imparted: that the removal of the preventer is denied. For the preventer of certainty is ambiguity (ijmāl) and the possibility of the opposite side as preponderated. Here, although the first preventer is removed, the second takes its place. For probability of a thing necessitates permitting the opposite side as preponderated. Then they have the argument that the report conveys probability in conventional usage (wad' and isti'māl) with certainty, and this probability necessitates immediate understanding with certainty. And the immediate understanding of the intended from a certain [source] removes the preventer with certainty due to the existence of the efficient cause. In summary, this probability necessitates immediate understanding, and that necessitates certainty. And how does it not necessitate immediate understanding? When it is known what 'salat' is in the law, even by a khabar wāhid, and what 'riba' is, the mind races upon hearing the two words to their legal meanings; to deny this is obstinacy. This is no less than if al-Khalīl or al-Aṣma'ī reported that a word has been placed in the Arabic language for this meaning, the mind races upon hearing it to that meaning absolutely. And this is more fitting, for this probability is strong, supported by consensus. And this is what is intended in the famous argument that the ruling after the explanation of the report is attributed to the certain, so it becomes certain, meaning that the ruling after the explanation of the report is derived from it, because of immediate understanding, so it conveys certainty, because what is meant by it is the general meaning (al-ma'nā al-amm), which does not admit the opposite possibility based on evidence. And after immediate understanding of one of the two meanings, the possibility of non-intention is like the possibility of interpretation (ta'wīl) in the nass, so it is not considered. This is unlike the preponderance of a homonym by opinion, for it does not necessitate immediate understanding. Reflect, for it is a place of reflection.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul al-fiqh dispute about the epistemological value of khabar wāhid (single-narrator report). The author presents an opposing argument that khabar wāhid yields certainty (qat') because (1) there is consensus that it gives probability (zann), (2) probability is preponderant (rājih) with certainty, so the preventer of certainty (ambiguity) is removed, and (3) the efficient cause for certainty (the Book or mutawātir) is present. The Hanafi response refutes this by denying that probability is preponderant with certainty; rather, it only gives probability. The argument delves into logical propositions, discussing conditional and possible statements, and concludes that the existence of probability does not remove the possibility of the opposite side. The Hanafi position is that khabar wāhid remains zannī al-thubūt and zannī al-dalāla, so it cannot produce certainty. The author supports this with examples of legal terms like salāt and ribā, showing that even with khabar wāhid, the mind immediately understands their meanings, but that immediate understanding is based on probability strengthened by consensus, not absolute certainty. The passage ends by contrasting this with preponderance of a homonym by personal opinion, which does not give immediate understanding.

Key Terms
الظن (al-zann): Probable belief; strong inclination of the soul towards a conclusion without certainty.
القطع (al-qat'): Certainty; decisive knowledge that admits no possibility of error.
الخبر (al-khabar): A report; specifically khabar wāhid (single-narrator report) in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in this passage, which of the following best explains why khabar wahid does not yield certainty even after its explanation?
A) Khabar wahid is not from the Qur'an, so it cannot give certainty.
B) The report's transmission is probable (zanni al-thubut), so its existence is not persistent, and a second preventer (the possibility of the opposite side) remains.
C) Khabar wahid contradicts qiyas, which is more certain.
D) The Sahaba did not accept khabar wahid as a source of law.

Key Takeaway
Khabar wahid yields probability (zann), not certainty (qat'), because its transmission is probable and the possibility of the opposite side persists despite preponderance.

The Epistemic Status of Khabar al-Wahid: Certainty or Probability?
Debate on certainty of solitary reports

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi argument that khabar al-wahid can yield certainty through immediate understanding (tabaddur) and evaluate the opposing view that it only yields probability.

Core Idea
A solitary report yields certainty when its meaning is grasped immediately, removing the impediment of ambiguity.

This lesson examines a foundational debate in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: does a solitary report (khabar al-wahid) provide certainty (qat') or only probability (zann)? The passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut defends the Hanafi position that, despite the report's probabilistic transmission, its meaning can become certain when it is immediately understood (tabaddur). This has profound implications for how rulings derived from such reports are classified.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
State the issue: whether khabar al-wahid yields certainty or probability. Note both sides.
The opponent holds that consensus affirms probability; the Hanafis argue that probability can become certainty.
2
Examine the Hanafi claim
Understand that the Hanafi position hinges on the existence of the report (certain as a historical fact) and the concept of immediate understanding (tabaddur).
The text says: 'as long as the report exists, it is certain' and 'tabaddur removes the impediment'.
3
Analyze the opponent's objection
The opponent argues that because the report's transmission is only probable (zanni al-thubut), its indication remains probable. The text counters that the existence of the report is certain, and immediate understanding is a psychological fact that overrides general probability.
The key term is 'المانع' (impediment): ambiguity and possibility of the opposite.
4
Trace the Hanafi response via tabaddur
The response shows that once immediate understanding occurs, the possibility of the opposite is disregarded, just as in the case of a clear Quranic verse. Thus certainty is achieved.
Example: When one hears the word 'الصلاة' after learning its legal meaning from a solitary report, the mind immediately grasps the legal meaning, producing certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المفاد ما دام الخبر باقياً قطعاً، وهو مرجح فواتح الرحموت شرح مسلم الثبوت الجزء الثاني فلزم القطعية حال وجوده فتم المطلوب، لأن الدعوى القطعية بعد تبيين الخبر، ولا يجوز في تلك الحال عدم الترجيح ولو وهماً، فإنه تجويز اجتماع الضدين، ثم قرر الجواب بأن إفادة الخبر الظن قطعاً، ممنوع فإنه يجوز ارتفاع الخير من البين لكونه ظني الثبوت فيرتفع الظن به فلا هذا الظن وهذا لأن نفس وجوده وإن كان مقطوعاً، لأنه يعلم بالوجدان، يرجح لكنه يمكن زواله بزوال الخبر، فلا يكون مقطوعاً بقاؤه، فلا يفيد القطع بالترجيح، وأما نفس وجود الظن من غير القطع فلا يفيد أصلاً هذا ولا يظهر لهذا وجه، فإن إفادة الخبر الظن مما أجمع عليه كما إن شاء الله تعالى. ومنع المقدمة الإجماعية لا يجوز. فبعد ملاحظة سيجيء هذا الإجماع لا يمكن منع إفادة الخبر الظن وبعد التنزل للمستدل أن يقول الخبر مفيد للظن قطعاً فارتفع المانع حين وجود الخبر قطعاً، فلزم القطع بالحكم في تلك الحال قطعاً، وهو المطلوب، فإنهم لا يدعون القطع بعد ظهور عدم وجود البيان وكذب الخبر فتدبر، فإذن الحق في الجواب ما أفاده هو قدس سره من منع ارتفاع المانع فإن المانع من القطع الإجمال، وجواز الطرف المقابل مرجوحاً، وههنا وإن ارتفع المانع الأول لكن قام الثاني مقامه، فإن الظن بالشيء يوجب تجويز الطرف المقابل مرجوحاً، هذا ثم لهم أن يقرروا بأن الخبر مفيد للظن بالوضع والاستعمال قطعاً، وهذا الظن يوجب التبادر قطعاً. وتبادر المراد من القطعي رافع للمانع قطعاً لوجود المقتضى، وبالجملة أن هذا الظن موجب للتبادر، وهو يوجب القطع، وكيف لا يوجب التبادر وأنه متى علم أن الصلاة في الشرع ما هو ولو بخبر الواحد والربا ما هو يتسارع الذهن عند سماع اللفظين إلى معناهما الشرعي مكابرة، وليس هذا إلا كما إذا أخبر الخليل أو الأصمعي أن لفضاً وضع في لغة العرب لهذا المعنى يتسارع الذهن عند السماع إليه البتة وهذا أولى منه فإن هذا الظن قوي معاضد بالإجماع، وهذا هو الذي ريم في الاستدلال المشهور بأن الحكم بعد تبيين الخبر مضاف إلى القطعي فيكون مقطوعاً يعني أن الحكم بعد تبيين الخبر يستفاد منه أن الحكم بعد تبيين الخبر يستفاد منه لأجل التبادر فيفيد القطع. لأن المراد به المعنى الأعم، وهو الذي لا يحتمل المقابل احتمالاً ناشئاً عن دليل. وبعد التبادر أحد فاحتمال عدم الإرادة كاحتمال التأويل في النص فلا اعتداد به، وهذا بخلاف ترجيح المشترك بالرأي فإنه لا يوجب التبادر فتأمل فيه فإنه موضع تأمل.
The derived meaning: as long as the report exists, it is certain, and it is a preponderator. Fawatih al-Rahmut Sharh Muslim al-Thubut, part two. Thus certainty is necessary at the time of its existence, so the desired is complete, because the claim of certainty is after the explanation of the report, and it is not permissible at that time to lack preponderance even hypothetically, for that would be allowing the conjunction of opposites. Then he answered that the report's yielding of probability is certain is prevented, because it is possible for the report to disappear from existence due to its being probabilistically established, so probability disappears with it; thus this probability does not last. This is because its very existence, although certain (known by direct experience), can cease with the cessation of the report, so its remaining is not certain, so it does not yield certainty of preponderance. As for the mere existence of probability without certainty, it is of no use at all. This seems baseless: that the report yields probability is a matter of consensus, God willing. Denying the consensus-based premise is not allowed. After noting this consensus, it is impossible to deny that the report yields probability. After concession, the proponent can say: the report certainly yields probability, so the impediment is removed at the time of the report's existence, so certainty of the ruling necessarily follows at that time. That is the desired conclusion, for they do not claim certainty after the appearance of the absence of clarification or the falsification of the report. So reflect. Thus the correct answer is what he (may his secret be sanctified) provided: preventing the removal of the impediment. For the impediment to certainty is ambiguity and the possibility of the opposite side being preponderated. Here, although the first impediment is removed, the second takes its place: probability of a thing necessitates allowing the opposite side as preponderated. Then they can argue: the report yields probability by convention and usage certainly, and this probability necessitates immediate understanding certainly. The immediate understanding of the intended meaning from a certain source removes the impediment certainly due to the existence of the requisite. In sum, this probability necessitates immediate understanding, which necessitates certainty. How could it not necessitate immediate understanding? When it is known what prayer is in the law, even by a solitary report, and what usury is, the mind immediately grasps their legal meanings upon hearing the two terms—this is undeniable. This is just like when al-Khalil or al-Asma'i informs that a word is used in the Arabic language for a meaning; the mind immediately goes to it upon hearing. This is even more so because this probability is strong, supported by consensus. This is what is intended in the famous argument: the ruling after the explanation of the report is attributed to something certain, so it is certain. Meaning: the ruling after the explanation of the report derives from it due to immediate understanding, so it yields certainty. Because the intended meaning is the more general meaning, which does not admit the opposite probability arising from evidence. After immediate understanding is achieved, the possibility of non-intention is like the possibility of ta'wil in a nass, so it is disregarded. This is unlike preponderation of a homonym by opinion, which does not cause immediate understanding. So reflect on this, for it is a place of reflection.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is a dispute within usul al-fiqh regarding the epistemic value of khabar al-wahid (solitary report). The author engages with an opponent who claims that khabar al-wahid only yields probability (zann), not certainty (qat'). The author argues that during the existence of the report (before any contradictory evidence or falsification), the report yields certainty of its meaning because the possibility of the opposite is effectively removed. The opponent counters that the report's thubut (establishment) is itself probabilistic, so its indication is also probabilistic. The author responds by distinguishing between the initial existence of the report (which is certain as a historical fact) and its ongoing existence, which can cease. He then reframes the debate: the consensus that khabar al-wahid yields probability is not denied, but once immediate understanding (tabaddur) occurs, it produces certainty. This aligns with the Hanafi position that a clear nass from a solitary report can be qat'i in dalala. The passage ends with a caution that this contrasts with preponderation of a homonym by opinion, which does not cause immediate understanding.

Key Terms
الخبر (al-khabar): A report or narration that conveys information about a ruling, specifically khabar al-wahid (solitary report) in this context.
الظن (al-zann): Probability; a speculative belief that is not certain.
القطع (al-qat'): Certainty; knowledge that admits no doubt.
التبادر (al-tabaddur): Immediate understanding or mental grasping of a meaning upon hearing a term without deliberation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what removes the impediment (man') to certainty from a khabar al-wahid?
A) The consensus that it yields probability
B) The immediate understanding (tabaddur) of its meaning
C) The possibility of the opposite being weightier
D) The existence of a contradictory report

Key Takeaway
A solitary report can yield certainty when its meaning is immediately understood, as the psychological clarity of tabaddur overrides any residual probability in transmission.
