وجود المعلق عليه، وإن قالوا إنه لإنشاء الحكم التعليقي؟ قلنا إنه على تقدير الخبرية للإخبار عن اللزوم والتعليق على الكائن في نفس الأمر، وبالجملة ما هو جوابكم فهو جوابنا (أقول : القيد مغير كما في سائر الإخبارات والإنشاآت ألا ترى النهار موجود يدل على الوقوع) الحالي (فلما علق بشرط لا يوجد إلا بعد وجوده فإنه يدل حينئذ على الوقوع وتغير عما دل عليه حال الانفراد (وكذلك : أنت طالق على الإنشائية كما هو مذهب الخصم (طلاق في الحال وإنشاء له وبعد التعليق ليس كذلك بل إنشاء بطلاق يوجد عند المعلق عليه فكذلك الحال حال ،الخبرية، فإنه يكون إخباراً عن طلاق يكون واقعاً في المستقبل عند وجود الشرط، فلا نسلم أنه كان ماضياً لم يصح التعليق، بل يصح ويتغير في الماضي إلى الاستقبال، بل يخلع عن الحكم الماضوي، ويكون حكم بينه وبين المعلق عليه باللزوم (ثم لما كان المعنى الموجب من مقتضيات الخبر كان تعليقه مستلزماً لتعليقه كيف لا ولو وجد المعنى الآن لكان الخبر عن الحكم التعليقي كاذباً، بل إنما يستدعي وجود المعنى الموجب عند وجود الشرط لا غير ولذا قلنا : التعليق يمنع السببية كما مر ) ولا يخفى أن الإخبار يقتضي وجود اللزوم بين الطرق ودخول الدار مثلاً، ولا يكون لزوم إلا باعتبار الشرع سببية العقد الشرطي النفسي له، وهذا القدر ضروري ومتحقق. وأما أنه هل هو سبب لوقوع الطلاق عند وجود الشرط، فالنزاع فيه باق بحاله، وقد مر مع ماله وعليه فلا نعيده (وقد يجاب) في شرح الشرح» بأنه إخبار عن وقوع تعليق الطلاق مثلاً في الذهن فلا ينافي كونه ماضياً (وهو ليس بشيء لأن الماضي إنما يدل على وقوع مصدره) في الزمان الماضي والتعليق يقتضي وقوع مصدره عند وجود الشرط لا غير وأما وجود تعليقه في الماضي فبمعزل عما نحن فيه لأنه ليس مدلولاً لصيغة طلقت، وهو ظاهر جداً (و) قالوا (رابعاً) لو كانت الصيغ المذكورة إخباراً (يلزم عدم الفرق بينه خبراً) الطلاق الواقع من قبل (أو إنشاء) أي وقوع الطلاق بهذا اللفظ لأنه خبر على كل تقدير (وهو) أي انتفاء الفرق باطل ولذلك لو قال للرجعية المطلقة في العدة طلقتك سئل عن نيته، فإن نوى الإنشاء يقع الطلاق الآخر وإن نوى الإخبار لا يقع (أقول) الملازمة ممنوعة، بل الفرق بأنه (مرة إخبار عما حصل به اقتضاء وبه يقع الطلاق (و) مرة أخرى ليس كذلك) بل هو إخبار عن الطرق الواقع لا بالاقتضاء وإلا ظهر في العبارة أن يقال مرة إخبار عن تطليق حاصل بإنشاء نفسي لم يحك عنه أصلاً أولاً، ومرة إخبار عن التطليق المحكي بالحكاية أولاً وعلى الأول يقع طلاق آخر بوجود الموجب مرة ثانية، وعلى الثاني لا يقع لعدم تكرار الموجب، وقد يجاب بأن الفرق بين ما إذا قصد إيقاع الطلاق وبين ما إذا قصد الإخبار عن طلاق سابق أنه في الأول يقصد الحكاية عن طلاق غير محقق يخبر عن وقوعه فالشرع يعتبره واقعاً لصدق هذا الكلام، فيقع طلاق آخر، وفي الثاني يقصد عن طلاق واقع ،محقق، فهو صادق في الإخبار، فلا يحتاج إلى اعتبار وقوع آخر وهذا بناء على ما مر نقله عن البعض في تحقيق الإخبارية مع ما عليه فتذكر. قال شارح الشارح : أن القطع بالفرق المذكور إنما هو في الحكاية عن الخارج، وأما في الحكاية عما في الذهن فدقيق تحقيقه أن الإنشاء يدل على حدوث البيع بهذا اتصاف اللفظ والإخبار عن حدوث البيع من الكلام النفسي والتغاير بين الحكاية، والمحكي عنه بالاعتبار، فالمحكي عنه هو إحداث البيع القائم بالنفس والحكاية هو من حيث إنه مدلول اللفظ ،مطابقة، وأنت لا يذهب عليك أن هذا مع ابتنائه على التغاير الاعتباري لا يفيد لأن المستدل إنما ألزم عدم الفرق بين ما إذا قصد الحكاية عن طلاق واقع أو بيع واقع، وبين ما إذا قصد حدوث آخر لكونه إخباراً على كل حال هذا لا يدفع ذلك، وبيان الفرق بينه حال كونه إنشاء وبينه حال كونه إخباراً مما لا طائل والقطع بالفرق في الحكاية عن الخارج لا يضره، بل يفيد بطلان اللازم فلا وجه له إلا بالإرجاع إلى ما قال المصنف (وقد يقال) في الجواب : (الفرق بينه خبراً وبينه إنشاء إنه إخبار عن (الذهن أي عن الإنشاء القائم بالذهن (مرة) فيقع آخر (وأخرى عن الخارج أي عن الطلاق الواقع في الخارج وفيه ما فيه) فإنك قد عرفت أن السبب الموجب لوقوع الطلاق هو الإنشاء القائم بالنفس وبه تصير المرأة مطلقة في الخارج، والرجل بائعاً والمال مبيعاً، فنحو طلقتك وأنت طالق حكاية عن هذا الإنشاء الذهني أو الأثر المرتب عليه فلا وجه لهذا الفرق ؛ نعم : قد يكون إخباراً عن الإنشاء الأول الذي به وقع الطلاق مرة، وحكى عنه أولاً وعلم وجوده بهذه الحكاية فلا يقع طلاق آخر، وقد يكون إخباراً عن إنشاء ذهني آخر غير الأول . فيقع آخر، ولذا يسأل في الرجعي كما قد مر، وقد يقال في الاستدلال على الإنشائية بأن : أنت طالق وطلقتك لو كانا خبرين كان الأول خبراً عن المرأة بالطلاق والثاني عن اتصاف الزوج بالتطليق، فهذا المخبر عنه ثابت من قبل أم لا . وعلى الثاني فلا إخبار، بل يكون إنشاء لتطليق الزوج وصيرورة المرأة متصفة به فإنهما قد تحققا بهذا، وعلى الأول يلزم أن تكون المرأة مطلقة قبل هذا الكلام وهو ظاهر الفساد لأن الطلاق إنما يقع به لا قبل، والقول بنوط الحكم بهذا اللفظ كما في السفر والشقة لا يفيد، لأن الشارع قد أناط الحكم على السفر ولم يعتبر المشقة فيه أصلاً إنما هو إبداء للحكمة منا، وأما ههنا فقد قلتم إن إيقاع الطلاق قد أناطه الشرع بعقد القلب، وإنما هذا حكاية وإخبار عنه لا دخل له في الإيقاع، وأيضاً لا بد لهذه الإناطة من دليل شرعي لأنه لا يهتدي إليه العقل، ولا يجوز نصب الأسباب ،بالرأي وأيضاً : لا يكون حينئذ هذا من قبيل المقتضى فإنه يثبت بالمقتضى، وهذا ما ثبت من قبل، والجواب عنه : أن المخبر عنه ثابت قبل التكلم بهذه الأخبار، وأن المرأة مطلقة قبله بالإنشاء النفسي، وليس فيه فساد أصلاً، وإناطة الحكم على هذا اللفظ مع كونه إخباراً لغة لأنه اعتبر سببية الإنشاء النفسي لئلا يلزم اعتبار الكلام الكاذب ومعنى نوط الحكم بهذه الصيغ أن العقد النفسي المخبر عنه إنما جعل سبباً شرعاً عند هذا الإخبار مقدماً عليه، فيكون ظهور سببيته بهذه الأخبار، ويكون الوقوع أيضاً عنده والدليل عليه وقوع الطلاق والبيع عند استعمال هذه الصيغ، وهذا هو الدليل على أن الحال حال السفر والمشقة، ثم لما كان اعتبار سببية هذا المعنى النفسي لوقوع الطلاق وصيرورة المرأة مطلقة إنما هو مشروط بإرادة الحكاية لإناطة الشارع الحكم بهذه الألفاظ لا على النفسي كيف اتفق كما أن إناطة الرخصة بالسفر دلت على أنه لا اعتبار للمشقة كيفما اتفقت بل حال كونها مقارنة للسفر وكان سببية هذا الإنشاء
The existence of the suspended-upon matter, and if they say it is for creating the suspensive ruling? We say it is on the assumption of declarativeness to inform about necessity and suspension upon what exists in reality. In short, what is your answer is our answer. (I say: The restriction changes as in all reports and performatives; do you not see that 'the day exists' indicates occurrence) in the present tense. (So when it is suspended upon a condition that does not exist except after its existence, it then indicates occurrence and changes from what it indicated in isolation. And likewise: 'You are divorced' in the performative sense as is the opponent's doctrine (is a divorce immediately and a performative for it, and after suspension it is not so, but rather a performative of divorce that occurs at the occurrence of the suspended-upon matter. So likewise the situation in the declarative case, for it is an informing about a divorce that will occur in the future at the existence of the condition. So we do not concede that it was past and suspension is invalid; rather it is valid and changes from past to future; rather it sheds the past ruling and has a relation between it and the suspended-upon matter of necessity. (Then since the intended meaning is from the implications of the report, its suspension necessitates its suspension; how could it not? For if the meaning existed now, the report about the suspensive ruling would be false, but it rather demands the existence of the meaning at the existence of the condition only, not otherwise. Hence we said: Suspension prevents causality as previously mentioned.) And it is not hidden that reporting necessitates the existence of necessity between the paths and entering the house, for example, and there is no necessity except by virtue of the law's making the mental conditional contract a cause for it. And this much is necessary and realized. As for whether it is a cause for the occurrence of divorce at the existence of the condition, the dispute remains as it is, and it has passed with its arguments, so we shall not repeat it. (And it may be answered) in the commentary of the commentary: that it is an informing about the occurrence of the suspension of divorce, for example, in the mind, so it does not preclude it being past (and it is nothing, because the past tense only indicates the occurrence of its verbal noun) in past time, and suspension demands the occurrence of its verbal noun at the existence of the condition only; and as for the existence of its suspension in the past, it is far from what we are discussing because it is not the meaning of the form 'I divorced', and this is very apparent. And they said (fourthly) if the mentioned formulas were reports, then (lack of difference would follow between it being a report) of the divorce that occurred previously (or a performative) i.e., the occurrence of divorce with this word, because it is a report on every assumption (and it) i.e., the negation of difference (is false). Hence if one says to a revocable divorced woman in her waiting period 'I divorced you', he is asked about his intention: if he intends performative, the other divorce occurs; if he intends report, it does not occur. (I say) the implication is denied; rather the difference is that (sometimes it is a report about what occurred with an entailment and thereby divorce occurs), and (sometimes it is not so) rather it is a report about the actual path without entailment; otherwise it would appear in the expression that one could say it is a report about a divorce achieved by a mental performative that was not reported at all firstly, and sometimes a report about the divorce narrated by the first narration; in the first case another divorce occurs by the existence of the cause a second time, and in the second it does not occur due to non-repetition of the cause. And it may be answered that the difference between when one intends to effect divorce and when one intends to report about a previous divorce is that in the first he intends to narrate about a divorce not yet realized, informing of its occurrence, so the law considers it occurred for the truthfulness of this speech, so another divorce occurs; in the second he intends about a realized, actual divorce, so he is truthful in the report, so there is no need to consider another occurrence. And this is based on what was previously transmitted from some in verifying the declarative nature and its implications, so remember. The commentator on the commentary said: That the certainty about the mentioned difference is only in the narration about external reality; as for the narration about what is in the mind, its precise verification is that the performative indicates the occurrence of the sale with this characterization of the word, and the report about the occurrence of the sale from the mental speech; and the difference between the narration and the narrated-about is by consideration: the narrated-about is the bringing-into-being of the sale standing in the self, and the narration is in terms of being a meaning of the word by correspondence. And it does not escape you that this, being based on consideration-based difference, does not benefit, because the proponent merely claimed the lack of difference between when one intends narration about an actual divorce or actual sale and when one intends another occurrence, because it is a report in every case; this does not refute that. And explaining the difference between it being a performative and it being a report is useless, and the certainty of difference in narration about external reality does not harm him; rather it proves the falsity of the consequent. So there is no way except by referring to what the author said. (And it may be said) in answer: (The difference between it being a report and it being a performative: it is a report about the mind i.e., about the performative standing in the mind (sometimes) so another occurs, and (sometimes about external reality i.e., about the divorce occurring in external reality, and in it is what is in it). For you have known that the cause that necessitates the occurrence of divorce is the mental performative, and by it the woman becomes divorced in external reality, and the man a seller and the property sold. So something like 'I divorced you' and 'You are divorced' are narrations about this mental performative or the effect depending on it; so there is no justification for this difference. Yes: sometimes it is a report about the first performative by which divorce occurred once, and it was narrated about it firstly and its existence was known by this narration, so no other divorce occurs; and sometimes it is a report about another mental performative other than the first, so another occurs. Hence the question in the case of the revocable divorce, as previously. And it may be said in arguing for the performative nature: that 'You are divorced' and 'I divorced you' if they were reports, the first would be a report about the woman being divorced and the second about the husband being characterized with divorcing. So is this reported thing established before or not? If not, there is no report; rather it is a performative for the husband's divorcing and the woman becoming characterized with it, for they are realized by this. If it is established before, then it would require the woman to be divorced before this speech, which is evidently corrupt because divorce only occurs by it, not before. And the claim of attaching the ruling to this word as in travel and hardship does not benefit, because the Lawgiver has attached the ruling to travel and did not consider hardship at all; it is only an expression of wisdom from us. But here you have said that the effecting of divorce has been attached by the law to the contract of the heart, and this is merely a narration and report about it, having no role in effecting. Also, this attachment requires a legal proof because reason cannot guide to it, and it is not permissible to establish causes by opinion. Also, then this would not be of the type of entailment (muqtada), for it is established by the entailment, and this is not established before. The answer to it: that the reported thing is established before speaking these reports, and the woman is divorced before it by the mental performative, and there is no corruption in that at all. And the attachment of the ruling to this word while being a report linguistically is because the law considered the causality of the mental performative to avoid considering false speech. And the meaning of attaching the ruling to these formulas is that the mental contract reported about is made a legal cause at the time of this report, preceding it; so its causality appears by these reports, and the occurrence is also at that time. The proof of it is the occurrence of divorce and sale upon using these formulas. And this is the proof that the situation is like travel and hardship. Then, since the consideration of the causality of this mental meaning for the occurrence of divorce and the woman becoming divorced is conditional on the intention of narration, because the Lawgiver attached the ruling to these words not to the mental meaning however it happens—just as the attachment of dispensation to travel indicates that hardship is not considered however it happens but rather when it is concomitant with travel—and the causality of this mental performative...
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute (ikhtilaf usuli) about the nature of divorce pronouncements like 'anti taliq' (you are divorced) and 'tallaqtuki' (I divorced you). The key question: Are these utterances declarative (ikhbar) or performative (insha')? The Hanafis argue they can be either depending on intention, while opponents claim they are inherently performative. The text presents the fourth argument (raabi'an) of the opponents: if these formulas were reports, there would be no difference between reporting a past divorce and performing a new one, which is false because in practice we distinguish (e.g., asking the husband's intention when saying 'tallaqtuki' to a woman in her iddah). The Hanafi response is that the difference lies in the presence or absence of entailment (iqtida'). When the utterance reports a mental performative that entails a new divorce, it occurs; when it merely reports a past actual divorce, it does not. The discussion deepens into the concept of nafsani (mental) speech: the cause (sabab) of divorce is the mental insha', and the uttered words are either a report of that mental act or a new mental act. The commentator refines the argument by distinguishing between narration about external reality vs. narration about the mind, ultimately affirming that the Hanafi position correctly preserves the distinction between ikhbar and insha' while maintaining the legal effect. The passage also analogizes to sale contracts and to the concept of 'illah (ratio legis) in travel dispensation.

Key Terms
إخبار (ikhbar): A statement that reports or informs about a fact or event, presupposing its existence prior to the statement.
إنشاء (insha'): A performative utterance that brings into being what it signifies (e.g., the divorce or sale) at the moment of utterance.
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspending a ruling (e.g., divorce) upon a condition; the utterance indicates that the ruling will occur in the future when the condition is fulfilled.
إنشاء نفسي (insha' nafsani): A mental performative act existing in the self or mind, which serves as the actual cause (sabab) of the legal effect, such as the intention to divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position discussed in this passage, if a man says to his revocably divorced wife (in iddah) 'tallaqtuki' without any additional context, what should be determined?
A) The divorce automatically takes effect because the utterance is inherently performative.
B) The husband's intention must be asked: if he intended insha', a new divorce occurs; if ikhbar, no divorce.
C) The utterance is always a report of the previous divorce, so no new divorce occurs.
D) The utterance is invalid and no divorce occurs because it is a repetition.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi distinction between ikhbar and insha' in divorce utterances preserves the role of intention and is supported by practical legal inquiry.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Definition of Truth and Falsehood: The Hanafi View
Defining truth and falsehood and addressing the liar paradox

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of truth (sidq) and falsehood (kidhb) in reports, and explain why the liar paradox does not undermine the definition.

Core Idea
Truth is correspondence with reality; falsehood is lack thereof – the Hanafi standard for evaluating reports.

In usul al-fiqh, the classification of a report as true or false is foundational for evaluating evidence. The Hanafi school, following the majority, defines truth as correspondence (mutabaqa) with reality. This lesson unpacks that definition and addresses the classic liar paradox that some claim creates an exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core definition
What does the author state as the definition of sidq and kidhb? Note the terms 'mutabaqa li al-waqi'' and 'adam mutabaqa'.
2
Analyze the liar paradox
The text presents a paradox: a statement that declares itself false. Understand why it seems to be neither true nor false.
This paradox is known as the 'liar paradox' or 'judhr asamm'.
3
Examine the Hanafi resolution
The author mentions al-Dawani's solution: it is not a khabar (report) because it lacks a referent, so it is exempt from the true/false dichotomy.
The statement is self-referential and does not report an external fact.
4
Contrast with the intended dichotomy
The disjunction (true/false) is real and exhaustive for all genuine reports. The paradox is a sophism.
The majority view holds that all reports are either true or false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الخبر عند الجمهور إما صادق أو كاذب لأنه إما مطابق للواقع الذي هو المخبر عنه، وهو (أولاً) مطابق، وهو الكاذب، وهذه المنفصلة حقيقية دائرة بين النفي والإثبات ونزاع من نازع ليس إلا في إطلاق لفظ الكذب والصدق لغة هل هما لهذين المعنيين لا في صدق هذه المنفصلة (وما قيل كل اخباري اليوم كاذب ولم يتكلم بغيره، أو كلامي هذا مشيراً إلى هذا كاذب (ليس بصادق ولا كاذب، وإلا كان كاذباً وصادقاً معاً لأنه لو كان الحصر بما إذا لم يكن هناك اعتقاد إلا أن يتكلف ويراد بعدم المطابقة أعم من أن يكون اعتقاداً لكن لا يطابقه، أو لا يكون اعتقاد أصلاً، لكن يكون صالحاً لتعلق الاعتقاد لئلا يختل بالإنشاء وتمسك (تمسكاً بقوله تعالى ﴿إِذَا جَاءَكَ الْمُتَفِقُونَ قَالُوا نَشْهَدُ إِنَّكَ لَرَسُولُ اللَّهِ وَاللَّهُ يَعْلَمُ إِنَّكَ لَرَسُولُهُ وَاللَّهُ يَشْهَدُ إِنَّ الْمُنَافِقِينَ لَكَذِبُونَ ﴾ [المنافقون: ١] فقد أثبت الله لهم الكذب في قولهم وَإِنَّكَ لَرَسُولُ اللَّهِ أنه مطابق للواقع من غير ارتياب وشك فعلم أن الصدق ليس المطابقة للواقع ولا الكذب عدمها، فبطل قولكم، وهذا ينفي قول الجاحظ أيضاً، فتعين قولنا : هو أن الصدق مطابقة الاعتقاد والكذب عدمها (وأجيب) بمنع أن الله كذبهم في قولهم إِنَّكَ لَرَسُولُ اللهِ بل المعنى أنهم كاذبون في (الشهادة فكذبهم في قولهم نشهد وذلك لأن الشهادة الإخبار عن صميم القلب والاعتقاد به، وهذا ظاهر إذا كان نشهد إخباراً كما هو مقتضى الصيغة، وأما إذا كان إنشاء للشهادة فالكذب باعتبار تضمنها الإخبار بأنهم معتقدون ولا شك أن الإخبار بالشهادة، وكذا إخبار أنهم معتقدون غير مطابق للواقع، ولك أن تقرر بأن قولهم: «نشهد أنك لرسول الله كناية عن الإخبار بإيمانهم، فمقصودهم الإخبار بأنهم مؤمنون ثابتون على إيمانهم، وعبروا عنه بما هو ملزوم الإيمان وهو الشهادة عن صميم القلب فرد الله عليهم أنهم بحسب الواقع فإنهم صادقون فيه بل في زعمهم الباطل فإنهم كانوا يزعمون إنهم كاذبون، وههنا جواب آخر هو : أن المعنى أن ديدنهم الكذب وعدم مطابقة كلامهم للواقع لا الكذب في
Then according to the majority, a report (khabar) is either true or false, because it either corresponds to reality which is the reported thing, or it does not correspond; the first is true, and the second is false. And this disjunction is real, encompassing affirmation and negation. The dispute of those who dispute is only about the linguistic application of the terms 'falsehood' and 'truth' – whether they are for these two meanings – not about the truth of this disjunction. And what is said: 'Every statement I make today is false' and he does not say anything else, or 'This statement of mine, pointing to this, is false' – it is neither true nor false, otherwise it would be both false and true together, because if it were true corresponding to reality, its subject would be characterized by falsehood, and this is this very report, so it would be false; and if it were false, its predicate would be denied of its subject which is this report, so if it is denied, truth would be established. This sophism is called 'a stubborn root' (judhr asamm). We have mentioned the answer to it in al-Sullam and we have explained in its commentary that it is not complete. The verification of al-Dawani is that it is not a report, so there is no impossibility in being devoid of both. And this cuts off the sophism. It has other answers, were the art not strange, we would elaborate on it with its pros and cons. And al-Nazzam of the Mu'tazila said: A report is either true or false, because it either corresponds to belief; it is true whether it corresponds to reality or not; or it does not correspond to belief; it is false whether it corresponds to reality or not. It is not hidden that the enumeration fails when there is no belief, unless one goes to the trouble and intends by non-correspondence something more general: that it is a belief but does not correspond to it, or there is no belief at all, but it is suitable for belief to be attached, so as not to fail with insha'. And they held fast to His statement: {When the hypocrites come to you, they say: 'We bear witness that you are indeed the Messenger of Allah.' And Allah knows that you are indeed His Messenger, and Allah bears witness that the hypocrites are indeed liars.} [Al-Munafiqun: 1]. So Allah established falsehood for them in their saying 'And you are indeed the Messenger of Allah' despite it corresponding to reality without doubt. Thus it is known that truth is not correspondence to reality and falsehood is not its absence. So your statement is invalidated. And this also negates the statement of al-Jahiz. So our statement is determined: that truth is correspondence to belief and falsehood is its absence. (And it was answered) by denying that Allah called them liars in their saying 'You are indeed the Messenger of Allah'; rather the meaning is that they are liars in the testimony (shahada), so He called them liars in their saying 'We bear witness'. And that is because testimony is information from the core of the heart and belief in it. This is apparent if 'we bear witness' is informative, as is required by the form. But if it is a construction (insha') of testimony, then the falsehood is due to its implying the information that they believe, and there is no doubt that the information of testimony, and likewise the information that they believe, does not correspond to reality. And you can establish that their saying 'We bear witness that you are the Messenger of Allah' is a metaphor (kinaya) for the information of their faith. So their purpose was to inform that they are believers, steadfast in their faith, and they expressed it by what is implied by faith, which is testimony from the core of the heart. So Allah refuted them, that they are liars in their claim, because they are hypocrites, and they have no belief in reality at all. (Or) the calling them liars is in their claim of knowledge and belief necessitated by hypocrisy. (Or) we concede that the calling them liars refers to their saying {You are the Messenger of Allah}, but not in terms of reality, for they are truthful in that, rather in their false opinion, for they used to think they were liars. And here is another answer: that the meaning is that their habit is falsehood and that their speech does not correspond to reality, not that they are liars in
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage discusses the definition of truth (sidq) and falsehood (kidhb) in reports (khabar). The majority (Jumhur) define truth as correspondence (mutabaqa) with reality, and falsehood as lack thereof. The passage addresses the liar paradox and then presents the view of al-Nazzam from the Mu'tazila, who defines truth as correspondence with belief, not reality. He uses Quran 63:1 as evidence, where the hypocrites say 'You are the Messenger of Allah' which is true in reality, yet Allah calls them liars. The Hanafi response refutes this by analyzing the verse: Allah calls them liars in their testimony (shahada), not in the statement itself, because they are pretending to believe. The passage offers multiple interpretations (ta'wilat) to undermine the Mu'tazilite argument, concluding that the Hanafi definition (correspondence to reality) stands. The discussion shows the importance of precise linguistic and legal analysis in usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
صدق (sidq): Truth; correspondence of a report with reality (Hanafi view).
كذب (kidhb): Falsehood; lack of correspondence of a report with reality.
مطابقة (mutabaqa): Correspondence; the relationship between a statement and what it describes.
جذر أصم (judhr asamm): A stubborn root; a name for the liar paradox in logic.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what defines a true report (sidq)?
A) Correspondence with the speaker's belief
B) Correspondence with reality
C) Correspondence with the listener's expectation
D) Correspondence with the majority opinion

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of truth as correspondence with reality is preserved even against the liar paradox, which is dismissed as a non-report.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

The Mu'tazilite Objection and the Hanafi Response
Refuting the Mu'tazilite definition of truth using Quranic analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Mu'tazilite definition of truth (correspondence with belief) and evaluate the Hanafi refutation using Quran 63:1.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazilite use of Quran 63:1 is refuted by analyzing the word شهادة – the falsehood is in the claim of belief, not the statement itself.

Al-Nazzam of the Mu'tazila argued that truth is correspondence with belief, not reality, citing the hypocrites' statement in Quran 63:1. This lesson examines their argument and the multiple Hanafi responses that preserve the correspondence-with-reality definition.

Guided Path
1
State the Mu'tazilite position
Al-Nazzam's definition: truth = correspondence with belief, falsehood = lack of correspondence with belief.
This is opposed to the Hanafi definition which uses reality as the criterion.
2
Identify the Mu'tazilite dalil
They use Quran 63:1 where the hypocrites say something true (you are the Messenger of Allah) but are called liars.
The verse: 'When the hypocrites come to you, they say: We bear witness that you are indeed the Messenger of Allah... and Allah bears witness that the hypocrites are indeed liars.'
3
Analyze the Hanafi response (first interpretation)
The response that Allah calls them liars in their testimony (shahada), not in the statement itself. Understand the distinction.
Shahada implies a claim of belief, so they are lying about their belief.
4
Examine alternative interpretations
The text offers multiple ta'wilat: it's a metaphor for their claim of belief, or they are deemed liars in their claim of knowledge.
These interpretations reinforce that the verse does not negate correspondence with reality.
5
Conclude the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi definition stands because the verse does not negate correspondence with reality; it only condemns their hypocrisy.
The tarjih is that the majority definition is correct, and the Mu'tazilite proof is weak.

Source Text

تعالى ﴿إِذَا جَاءَكَ الْمُتَفِقُونَ قَالُوا نَشْهَدُ إِنَّكَ لَرَسُولُ اللَّهِ وَاللَّهُ يَعْلَمُ إِنَّكَ لَرَسُولُهُ وَاللَّهُ يَشْهَدُ إِنَّ الْمُنَافِقِينَ لَكَذِبُونَ ﴾ [المنافقون: ١] فقد أثبت الله لهم الكذب في قولهم وَإِنَّكَ لَرَسُولُ اللَّهِ أنه مطابق للواقع من غير ارتياب وشك فعلم أن الصدق ليس المطابقة للواقع ولا الكذب عدمها، فبطل قولكم، وهذا ينفي قول الجاحظ أيضاً، فتعين قولنا : هو أن الصدق مطابقة الاعتقاد والكذب عدمها (وأجيب) بمنع أن الله كذبهم في قولهم إِنَّكَ لَرَسُولُ اللهِ بل المعنى أنهم كاذبون في (الشهادة فكذبهم في قولهم نشهد وذلك لأن الشهادة الإخبار عن صميم القلب والاعتقاد به، وهذا ظاهر إذا كان نشهد إخباراً كما هو مقتضى الصيغة، وأما إذا كان إنشاء للشهادة فالكذب باعتبار تضمنها الإخبار بأنهم معتقدون ولا شك أن الإخبار بالشهادة، وكذا إخبار أنهم معتقدون غير مطابق للواقع، ولك أن تقرر بأن قولهم: «نشهد أنك لرسول الله كناية عن الإخبار بإيمانهم، فمقصودهم الإخبار بأنهم مؤمنون ثابتون على إيمانهم، وعبروا عنه بما هو ملزوم الإيمان وهو الشهادة عن صميم القلب فرد الله عليهم أنهم كاذبون في دعواهم لما أنهم منافقون، وليس لهم في نفس الأمر تصديق أصلاً ، (أو) التكذيب (في ادعائهم العلم والاعتقاد اللازم للنفاق (أو ) سلمنا أن التكذيب راجع إلى قولهم ﴿إِنَّكَ لَرَسُولُ اللَّهِ لكن لا بحسب الواقع فإنهم صادقون فيه بل في زعمهم الباطل فإنهم كانوا يزعمون إنهم كاذبون، وههنا جواب آخر هو : أن المعنى أن ديدنهم الكذب وعدم مطابقة كلامهم للواقع لا الكذب في
Then according to the majority, a report (khabar) is either true or false, because it either corresponds to reality which is the reported thing, or it does not correspond; the first is true, and the second is false. And this disjunction is real, encompassing affirmation and negation. The dispute of those who dispute is only about the linguistic application of the terms 'falsehood' and 'truth' – whether they are for these two meanings – not about the truth of this disjunction. And what is said: 'Every statement I make today is false' and he does not say anything else, or 'This statement of mine, pointing to this, is false' – it is neither true nor false, otherwise it would be both false and true together, because if it were true corresponding to reality, its subject would be characterized by falsehood, and this is this very report, so it would be false; and if it were false, its predicate would be denied of its subject which is this report, so if it is denied, truth would be established. This sophism is called 'a stubborn root' (judhr asamm). We have mentioned the answer to it in al-Sullam and we have explained in its commentary that it is not complete. The verification of al-Dawani is that it is not a report, so there is no impossibility in being devoid of both. And this cuts off the sophism. It has other answers, were the art not strange, we would elaborate on it with its pros and cons. And al-Nazzam of the Mu'tazila said: A report is either true or false, because it either corresponds to belief; it is true whether it corresponds to reality or not; or it does not correspond to belief; it is false whether it corresponds to reality or not. It is not hidden that the enumeration fails when there is no belief, unless one goes to the trouble and intends by non-correspondence something more general: that it is a belief but does not correspond to it, or there is no belief at all, but it is suitable for belief to be attached, so as not to fail with insha'. And they held fast to His statement: {When the hypocrites come to you, they say: 'We bear witness that you are indeed the Messenger of Allah.' And Allah knows that you are indeed His Messenger, and Allah bears witness that the hypocrites are indeed liars.} [Al-Munafiqun: 1]. So Allah established falsehood for them in their saying 'And you are indeed the Messenger of Allah' despite it corresponding to reality without doubt. Thus it is known that truth is not correspondence to reality and falsehood is not its absence. So your statement is invalidated. And this also negates the statement of al-Jahiz. So our statement is determined: that truth is correspondence to belief and falsehood is its absence. (And it was answered) by denying that Allah called them liars in their saying 'You are indeed the Messenger of Allah'; rather the meaning is that they are liars in the testimony (shahada), so He called them liars in their saying 'We bear witness'. And that is because testimony is information from the core of the heart and belief in it. This is apparent if 'we bear witness' is informative, as is required by the form. But if it is a construction (insha') of testimony, then the falsehood is due to its implying the information that they believe, and there is no doubt that the information of testimony, and likewise the information that they believe, does not correspond to reality. And you can establish that their saying 'We bear witness that you are the Messenger of Allah' is a metaphor (kinaya) for the information of their faith. So their purpose was to inform that they are believers, steadfast in their faith, and they expressed it by what is implied by faith, which is testimony from the core of the heart. So Allah refuted them, that they are liars in their claim, because they are hypocrites, and they have no belief in reality at all. (Or) the calling them liars is in their claim of knowledge and belief necessitated by hypocrisy. (Or) we concede that the calling them liars refers to their saying {You are the Messenger of Allah}, but not in terms of reality, for they are truthful in that, rather in their false opinion, for they used to think they were liars. And here is another answer: that the meaning is that their habit is falsehood and that their speech does not correspond to reality, not that they are liars in
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage discusses the definition of truth (sidq) and falsehood (kidhb) in reports (khabar). The majority (Jumhur) define truth as correspondence (mutabaqa) with reality, and falsehood as lack thereof. The passage addresses the liar paradox and then presents the view of al-Nazzam from the Mu'tazila, who defines truth as correspondence with belief, not reality. He uses Quran 63:1 as evidence, where the hypocrites say 'You are the Messenger of Allah' which is true in reality, yet Allah calls them liars. The Hanafi response refutes this by analyzing the verse: Allah calls them liars in their testimony (shahada), not in the statement itself, because they are pretending to believe. The passage offers multiple interpretations (ta'wilat) to undermine the Mu'tazilite argument, concluding that the Hanafi definition (correspondence to reality) stands. The discussion shows the importance of precise linguistic and legal analysis in usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
صدق (sidq): Truth; correspondence of a report with reality (Hanafi view).
كذب (kidhb): Falsehood; lack of correspondence of a report with reality.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony; a declaration that implies belief from the heart.
كناية (kinaya): Metaphor; indirect expression that implies something beyond its literal meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the core of the Hanafi response to the Mu'tazilite use of Quran 63:1?
A) The verse is abrogated.
B) The hypocrites were lying in their claim of belief, not in the statement.
C) The verse only applies to the Prophet.
D) The verse is ambiguous and cannot be used as evidence.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite argument is refuted by showing that the falsehood in Quran 63:1 lies in the hypocrites' false claim of belief (shahada), not in their factual statement.

Why Knowledge is Not Only Known Truth and Falsehood: The Hanafi Critique of Exhaustive Division
Refuting the claim that knowledge is only known truth or known falsehood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify compound ignorance (al-jahl al-murakkab) and explain why the division of knowledge into known truth and known falsehood is not exhaustive according to Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Knowledge excludes compound ignorance; the binary division fails to capture this distinct epistemic category.

This passage addresses a fundamental dispute in Hanafi usul: whether knowledge can be exhaustively divided into known truth and known falsehood. The author refutes this claim by introducing a third category—compound ignorance (al-jahl al-murakkab)—which is a firm conviction that does not conform to reality. Understanding this refutation is crucial for correctly classifying reports and arguments in fiqh and usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim under attack
The author refutes the assertion that knowledge is only of two types: known truth (ma'lum al-sidq) and known falsehood (ma'lum al-kidhb). This claim implies that all cognitive states are reducible to these two.
The opponent is unnamed but represents a common rationalist view.
2
Recognize the category of compound ignorance
The author introduces compound ignorance (al-jahl al-murakkab): a firm conviction (jazm) that does not conform to reality. It is neither knowledge (because no correspondence), nor doubt (shakk), nor suspicion (zann).
In doubt and suspicion, there is allowance for the opposite; compound ignorance has no such allowance.
3
Analyze why the binary division fails
Since compound ignorance exists and is a proper epistemic state, the binary division cannot be exhaustive. The report conforming to compound ignorance does not fall into either known truth or known falsehood.
The author states: 'the purpose of the division is not exhaustive enumeration, but rather the response to one who claimed exclusivity.'
4
Examine the opponent's analogy and the Hanafi rebuttal
Opponents analogize: denying a claimant of prophethood is based on not knowing his truth. The Hanafi response: the denial is based on the norm (khilaf al-ada) which gives certainty of falsehood, not on lack of knowledge of truth. The analogy has a clear difference (farq).
The norm (ada) is a source of certainty in Hanafi epistemology.
5
Conclude the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: when evaluating reports, one must account for compound ignorance. A report based on compound ignorance is not simply 'unknown truth' but has its own ruling in classification.
This affects, for example, the admissibility of certain traditions or testimonies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المجهول فيعلم صدق نقيضه فالإخبار به من مجهول آخر ليس مما لم يعلم صدقه، بل قد علم لكون مضمونه مطابقاً للعلم ضرورياً كان أو نظرياً، لكن الأمر سهل فإن بطلان هذا الرأي ضروري غني عن الإبانة والمذكور تنبيه فافهم أقول هذا أي لزوم ارتفاع النقيضين المستلزم للاجتماع مبني على أن مطابقة الواقع معتبر في العلم كما هو مفهوم عرفاً ولغة وشرعاً، وذلك لأنه لو شمل الجهل أيضاً فلا يلزم ارتفاع النقيضين في الواقع وحينئذ يكون التقسيم المذكور إلى معلوم الصدق ومعلوم الكذب ومظنون أحدهما والمتساوي غير حاصر، إذا الاخبار المطابق للجهل المركب) وهو الجزم الغير المطابق للواقع ليس فيه علم) لعدم المطابقة (ولا ظن ولا شك إذ فيهما تجويز للجانب المخالف مرجوحاً أو مساوياً، والمجهول بالجهل المركب مجزوم لا تجويز فيه للمخالف أصلاً ( فتدبر) فإن الأمر سهل إذ ليس المقصود من التقسيم الحصر، بل الغرض الرد على من زعم الانحصار في معلوم الصدق ومعلوم الكذب فتدبر . هذا ثم أجاب عن قياسهم بقوله : (وأما تكذيب مدعي الرسالة عند عدم ظهور صدقه (فإنه بخلاف العادة) أي تكذيبه بسبب كون هذه الدعوى من غير بينة خلاف العادة (وهي) أي العادة توجب العلم قطعاً) فبهذا الوجه يعلم كذبه، لا لأنه لم يعلم صدقه، فقياسكم مع الفارق (وقيل) توجب العادة العلم (ظناً) فيظن بكذبه ، فلا علم في الأصل حتى يقاس عليه، لكن هذا خلاف الضرورة، فإن مدعي الرسالة العاجز عن إقامة معجزة مقطوع الكذب من غير ريب فافهم
The unknown [compound ignorance] is known to be false by its opposite, so reporting it from another unknown is not something whose truth is unknown; rather it is known because its content conforms to knowledge, whether necessary or theoretical. But the matter is easy, for the falsehood of this opinion is necessary and in no need of explanation, and the mentioned is a reminder, so understand. I say: This, i.e., the necessity of the two negatives rising together implying conjunction, is based on the fact that conformity to reality is considered in knowledge as understood customarily, linguistically, and legally. That is because if [the category of] ignorance also covers it, then the rising of the two negatives is not necessary in reality, and then the mentioned division into known truth, known falsehood, suspicion of either, and what is equal is not exhaustive, since the report conforming to compound ignorance (which is conviction not conforming to reality) contains neither knowledge (due to non-conformity) nor suspicion nor doubt, for in both there is allowance for the opposite side as weak or equal, while the one unknown by compound ignorance has conviction with no allowance for the opposite at all. So ponder, for the matter is easy, since the purpose of the division is not exhaustive enumeration, but rather the response to one who claimed exclusivity to known truth and known falsehood. So ponder. This. Then he answered their analogy by saying: 'As for the denial of the claimant of prophethood when his truth is not apparent, it is against the norm,' i.e., his denial because this claim without proof is against the norm, and it (i.e., the norm) gives certain knowledge, so by this aspect his falsehood is known, not because his truth is not known, so your analogy is with a difference. And it is said: The norm gives probable knowledge, so his falsehood is probable, so there is no knowledge in the original to be analogized to it, but this is contrary to necessity, for the claimant of prophethood who is incapable of bringing a miracle is certainly false without doubt, so understand.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage is a dispute in usul al-fiqh: the author refutes the claim that knowledge is exclusively divided into known truth and known falsehood. He argues that compound ignorance (al-jahl al-murakkab) — a firm belief that does not match reality — is a separate category that is neither knowledge nor doubt nor suspicion. The opponent's argument that denying a claimant of prophethood is because his truth is unknown is countered by showing that such denial is based on the norm (khilaf al-ada) which gives certainty of falsehood, not on lack of knowledge of truth. Thus, the opponent's analogy fails. The passage explains that the division of knowledge is not meant to be exhaustive but to refute those who claim exclusivity. This is a typical Hanafi rational approach in usul.

Key Terms
الجهل المركب (al-jahl al-murakkab): A firm conviction that does not conform to reality; it is neither knowledge, doubt, nor suspicion.
العلم (al-ilm): Certain knowledge that corresponds to reality, either necessary (daruri) or theoretical (nazari).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the category of knowledge that is neither known truth nor known falsehood according to this passage?
A) Doubt (shakk)
B) Suspicion (zann)
C) Compound ignorance (jahl murakkab)
D) Simple ignorance (jahl basit)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi critique shows that the epistemic binary of known truth/falsehood is insufficient; compound ignorance is a distinct category that must be recognized in usul al-fiqh.

The Hanafi Refutation of Sectarian Conditions for Tawatur
Refuting various sectarian conditions for tawatur

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on conditions for tawatur and evaluate why sectarian stipulations (infallibility, humility, etc.) are invalid based on the principle of impossibility of collusion.

Core Idea
Tawatur requires only a number making collusion impossible; infallibility, humility, and diversity are unnecessary.

In this passage, the Hanafi author refutes various sectarian conditions proposed for tawatur—such as requiring an infallible narrator, humility, or geographic diversity. These conditions, he argues, are either self-contradictory or empirically unnecessary. The core Hanafi principle is that certainty (ilm) arises from a large group's report due to the impossibility of collusion, regardless of the narrators' personal attributes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sect and its condition
For each sect (Shia, Jews, others), state what condition they add for tawatur. From the text: Shia require an infallible (ma'sum) among narrators; Jews require humility (ahl al-dhimma wa al-maskanah); some require that narrators not be from one city; others require difference in lineage, religion, and homeland.
The Shia condition is the most extensively critiqued.
2
Analyze the Hanafi refutation
Examine the logical or empirical argument the author uses to reject each condition. For the Shia, if a ma'sum narrates, his word alone gives certainty, making tawatur redundant. For the Jews, turning the argument around: fear may lead to collusion to please the powerful.
3
Detect self-contradiction
Note where the opposing school's own practice contradicts their condition. The Shia reject mutawatir Quran verses for lack of infallible narration but accept solitary reports from their imams, undermining their principle.
This shows the condition is applied inconsistently.
4
Apply the core Hanafi principle
Show how the principle of impossibility of collusion covers all cases without extra conditions. The text states: 'certainty is obtained from a group's report without any of these conditions'—this is empirical observation.
The Hanafi method relies on observable reality (dalil aqli).
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Explain the practical consequence: Hanafis accept historically established reports from non-Muslims as mutawatir, while Shia reject them if not transmitted by an infallible. This affects the corpus of accepted hadith and historical data.
The difference impacts the authority of many transmitted reports.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واشترط (الشيعة) خذلهم الله تعالى في التواتر (المعصوم فيهم) أي في الرواة وهذا بهت فإنه إذا كان روى المعصوم فروايته وحده تفيد اليقين ولا حاجة إلى التواتر والعاملي منهم لما تفطن أن هذا الشرط مكابرة لوقوع العلم بدونه اختار سبيل التكذيب والجحود وقال : هذا النقل تهمة عليهم كيف لا وأنهم لا يقبلون خبر الواحد، فيجب أن تكون الأخبار المنقولة من الإمام الثاني عشر أو الحادي عشر كلها متواترة عندهم، والعصمة قد انحصرت في أربعة عشر على زعمهم فلو كان التواتر مشروطاً بأخبار المعصوم لما كانت هذه الأخبار عندهم حجة، وأنت لا يذهب عليك أن ناقلي هذا المذهب ثقات لا يتأتى إنكاره ، وهذا العبد غفر الله له رأي في بعض كتبهم وسمع عن بعض من يتبعونه أنهم أنكروا بعض القرآن بعدم رواية المعصوم كما قالوا في قوله تعالى: ﴿فَأَنزَلَ اللهُ سَكِينَتَهُ عَلَيْهِ ﴾ [التوبة : ٤٠] إن الصحيح فأنزل الله سكينته على رسوله، فالأول مع كونه متواتراً لم : يقبلوه لعدم رواية المعصوم على زعمهم والثاني نسبوه إلى الإمام زين العابدين علي بن الحسين عليه وعلى آله الكرام الرضوان وقبلوه مع كونه من الآحاد، ونقل في «مجمع البيان» عن بعض شياطينهم الذين هم عندهم ثقات أنه ذهب من القرآن آيات كثيرة والعياذ بالله، لا يعلمها إلا المعصوم، وسيبينها الإمام محمد المهدي الموعود مع أنه قد تواتر أن القرآن هو هذا؛ وما ذكره العاملي فمع كونه لا يفيد إلا عدم اشتراط التواتر عند عدم وجود معصومهم ويجوز أن يكون الشارطون شرطوا عند وجوده ومع كونه مبنياً على عدم قبول الآحاد مع أن البعض منهم قبلوا الآحاد ، ولعل قبولهم إياه لهذا الاشتراط ليس بعد تمامه إلا اعتراضاً عليهم، فيوجب فساد مذهبهم لا عدم صحة النقل عنهم (و) اشتراط (اليهود أهل الذمة والمسكنة في التواتر لإمكان تواطؤ من عداهم من أهل العزة على الكذب لعدم خوفهم، ولك أن تقلب عليهم أن خوفهم يورث احتمال التواطؤ مرضاة لأهل العز بخلافهم فإنهم لا يطلبون مرضاة أحد لعدم الخوف (و) اشتراط (قوم أن لا يحويهم بلد لأنّ أهل بلد واحد مما يمكن اجتماعهم على الكذب لعرض (و) اشتراط (قوم اختلاف النسب والدين والوطن) لذلك (والكل) من المذاهب (باطل للعلم بالعلم أي لليقين بوجود العلم عند أخبار الجماعة (بدون ذلك) أي بدون كل واحد من الشروط الثلاثة المذكورة، وهذا ظاهر جداً.
The Shia (may Allah forsake them) stipulated the presence of an infallible (imam) among the narrators. This is false, because if an infallible narrates, his narration alone gives certainty, and there is no need for tawatur. The 'Amili among them, realizing that this condition is obstinacy since knowledge occurs without it, chose the path of denial, saying that this transmission is a charge against them. Moreover, they do not accept solitary reports, so all news from the twelfth or eleventh imam must be mutawatir according to them, yet infallibility is restricted to fourteen (individuals) in their claim. If tawatur required an infallible, these reports would not be proof for them. Their transmitters are reliable; denial is not possible. (The author) saw in some of their books and heard from some followers that they deny parts of the Quran for lack of narration by an infallible, as in the verse 'Then Allah sent down His tranquility upon him' (9:40) claiming the correct is 'upon His messenger'. The first, being mutawatir, they reject for lack of infallible narration; the second they attribute to Imam Zayn al-'Abidin and accept it despite being solitary. And in Majma' al-Bayan, it is reported from some of their devils, considered reliable by them, that many verses have been removed from the Quran - Allah forbid - known only to the infallible. Yet it is mutawatir that the Quran is this. The 'Amili's statement only indicates non-requirement of tawatur in the absence of their infallible. Possibly the condition is for when he is present. And it is based on non-acceptance of solitary reports, yet some of them accept them. Perhaps their acceptance is not after fulfilling the condition but as an objection, which ruins their school but does not invalidate transmission from them. The Jews (ahl al-dhimma and the submissive) stipulated humility, because otherwise the powerful might collude. But could be turned back: fear may lead to collusion to please the powerful, unlike them who seek no one's pleasure. Some stipulated that narrators not be from one city, because people of one city might collude for worldly reasons. Some stipulated difference in lineage, religion, and homeland. All these schools are false, because certainty is obtained from a group's report without any of these conditions. This is very clear.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage critiques various sectarian conditions for tawatur proposed by Shia, Jews, and others. Each condition is argued to be invalid because tawatur's certainty arises from the sheer number and impossibility of collusion, not from the narrators' status. The Shia condition of an infallible imam is self-defeating: if the imam transmits, his word alone suffices, making tawatur unnecessary. Moreover, Shia themselves reject some mutawatir Quran verses while accepting solitary reports from their imams, contradicting their own principle. The Jewish condition of humility is turned around by noting that fear may cause collusion to please the powerful. The geographic and diversity conditions are also baseless. The author concludes that all such stipulations are false because knowledge via tawatur is empirically observed without them.

Key Terms
المعصوم (al-ma'sum): An infallible person, according to Shia belief, who is protected from sin and error, and whose narration gives certainty.
التواتر (al-tawatur): A report transmitted by such a large number that collusion on a falsehood is impossible, yielding certain knowledge.
مكابرة (mukabarah): Stubborn denial of an obvious truth; obstinacy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi author reject the Shia condition that a ma'sum must be among the narrators for tawatur?
A) Because ma'sum narrations are not reliable
B) Because the ma'sum's narration alone gives certainty, making tawatur unnecessary
C) Because Shia do not accept solitary reports
D) Because the ma'sum cannot narrate anything

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that tawatur requires only a number that makes collusion impossible; extra conditions like infallibility, humility, or geographic diversity are baseless.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
10 min
Silence and Tawatur: Hanafi Refutation of Rawafid
Refutation of Rawafid on silence and tawatur using usul arguments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that silence is not probative when motives for concealment exist, and evaluate the tawatur status of reported miracles.

Core Idea
Silence does not prove truth; motives for concealment break its probative value, and only widespread transmission yields certainty.

The Rawafid (Shia) argue that the Companions' silence about Ali's Imamate proves its truth, and that all miracles must be mutawatir to be accepted. The Hanafi response in this passage exposes the fallacy of the silence argument by showing that motives for concealment were present. It also distinguishes between miracles that are mutawatir (like the splitting of the moon) and those that are not (like Jesus' speech in the cradle), showing that the Quran suffices as the primary miracle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested claim
What do the Rawafid assert about the Companions' silence and the tawatur of miracles? State their position clearly from the text.
The Rawafid claim silence indicates truth and all miracles must be mutawatir.
2
Analyze the Hanafi counter-argument on silence
How does the author refute the probative value of silence? Note the example of Christians not transmitting Jesus' speech, and the principle that silence yields certainty only when motives for concealment are absent.
The Hanafi response shows that motives for concealment (fear of caliphs) existed, thus silence is not proof.
3
Examine the tawatur distinction
Identify which miracles the author considers mutawatir (splitting of the moon, yearning of the trunk) and why. Why are others like Jesus' speech not mutawatir?
The splitting of the moon is in the Quran, so it is mutawatir; other miracles had few witnesses.
4
Assess the role of the Quran
How does the author argue that the Quran's inimitability suffices as a miracle, even for those who cannot appreciate its eloquence? Note the rebuttal to the objection that most people do not understand its eloquence.
The Quran's tawatur and lack of successful challenge provide certainty of its miraculous nature.
5
Evaluate the overall evidence
Summarize why the Hanafi position is preferred: silence not probative, Quran sufficient, and tawatur is properly defined.
The Rawafid claim is based on a flawed understanding of both silence and tawatur.

له المنبر
ادعته الروافض خذلهم الله تعالى في إمامة أمير المؤمنين فإنه كذب البتة ضرورة الروافض (قالوا) لعل سكوتهم لحامل حملهم على كتمانهم إنما لا يفيد السكوت القطع إلا إذا علم انتفاء الحوامل والحوامل على الكتمان كثيرة لا يمكن ضبطها، فالسكون ساكت) عن كونه كذباً ألا ترى لم ينقل النصارى كلام عيسى على نبينا وعليه الصلاة والسلام في (المهد) حين دخل القوم على مريم يتهمونها فيعظونها : قَالَ إِنِّي عَبْدُ اللَّهِ آتَانِي الْكِتَابَ وَجَعَلَنِي نَبِيًّا وَجَعَلَنِي مُبَارَكًا أَيْنَ مَا كُنتُ وَأَوْصَانِي بِالصَّلَوةِ وَالزَّكَوةِ مَا دُمْتُ حَيًّا وَبَرًّا بِوَالِدَتِي وَلَمْ يَجْعَلْنِي جَبَّارًا شَقِيًّا وَالسَّلَامُ عَلَى يَوْمَ وُلِدتُّ وَيَوْمَ أَمُوتُ وَيَوْمَ أُبْعَثُ حَيًّا ﴾ [مريم: ۳۰ - ۳۳] (ونقـل انشقاق القمر) آحاداً عن ابن مسعود قال : انشق القمر على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم فرقتين فوق الجبل وفرقة دونه فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «اشهدوا» رواه الشيخان (وتسبيح الحصى والطعام عن ابن مسعود رضي الله تعالى عنه قال : كنا نعد الآيات بركة، وأنتم تعدّونها تخويفاً وقال : كنا مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم في سفر فقل الماء، فقال: «اطلبوا فضلة من الماء فجاؤوا بماء قليل في إناء فأدخل يده صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم في الإناء قال : حي على الطهور المبارك والبركة من الله تعالى فلقد رأيت الماء ينبع من بين أصابعه صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وقد كنا نسمع تسبيح الطعام وهو يؤكل رواه البخاري وحنين الجذع) عن جابر رضي الله تعالى عنه قال : كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم إذا خطب استند إلى جذع نخلة من سواري المسجد : فلما صنع فاستوى عليه صاحت النخلة التي كان يخطب عندها حتى كادت أن تنشق، فنزل النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم حتى أخذها فضمها إليه فجعلت تئن أنين الصبي الذي يسكت حتى استقرت قال : بكت على ما كانت تسمع من الذكر رواه البخاري (وسعي الشجرة) عن ابن عمر رضي الله تعالى عنهما قال : كنا مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم في سفر، فأقبل أعرابي، فلما دنا قال له رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم: «نشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وحده لا شريك له ونشهد أن محمداً عبده ورسوله قال ومن يشهد على ما تقول قال : : هذه السلمة فدعاها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وهو بشاطيء الوادي، فأقبلت تخذ الأرض حتى قامت بين يديه فاستشهدها ثلاثاً فشهدت ثلاثاً إنه كما قال ثم رجعت إلى منبتها رواه الدارمي وتسليم الحجر والغزالة عن جابر بن سمرة أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم قال: إن بمكة حجراً كان يسلم علي ليالي بعثت وإني لأعرفه وكثير من الفروع المختلفة ككون الأذان مثنى مثنى وغير ذلك (أحاداً) متعلق بنقل، نقلت هذه الأمور آحاداً مع سكوت الباقين، ولا يقطع بالكذب (والجواب : أن شمول حامل للكل الأقاصي والأداني في كل زمان وفي كل مكان كما قالوا: (منتف عادة) والمسألة فيما إذا سكتوا مدة العمر، ثم إن الحامل الذي ذكروه في كتمان خبر الإمامة الخوف من الخلفاء الثلاثة وباقي العشرة ، فانظر إلى سفاهتهم، كيف خاف الجمع الأزيد مائة ألف من رجال معدودين وكيف يستمر هذا الخوف حتى بقي بعد وفاتهم رضوان الله تعالى عليهم، ثم

من
إنهم يقرون أيضاً أن أمير المؤمنين أشجع الناس وأن أهل بيته كلهم كانوا ناصريه، وأن مثل عمار والمقداد وأبي ذر أيضاً كانوا من ناصريه وكان أبو ذر ذا قبيلة ولم يخف من أمثال أبي جهل حين أظهر الإسلام بين أعينهم، وإذا كان خائفاً مع وجود الناصرين فأين الأشجعية؟ هو بل هذا الخوف مناف للشجاعة ومثبت لأشجعية الخلفاء الثلاثة وجلادتهم، فقد بان لك بأقوم الحجج أن مذهب الشيعة الشنيعة لا يختاره إلا سفيه انتهى إلى حدة البلادة ومفض إلى أمور مستشنعة وأما كلام عيسى) في المهد (والمعجزات المذكورة (فلو كثر مشاهدوها لتواترت كما قيل في انشقاق القمر وحنين (الجذع إنهما متواترتان وصرح بتواترهما السبكي، ولا بعد فيه، بل الانشقاق منقول في القرآن فاكتفوا في النقل به فإن قلت تحتمل الآية الاخبار عن الآخرة؟ قلت : بعيد عن السياق، فإنه قال تعالى : اقْتَرَبَتِ السَّاعَةُ وَأَنشَقَّ الْقَمَرُ وَإِن يَرَوْا عَايَةً يُعْرِضُوا وَيَقُولُوا سِحْرٌ مُسْتَمِرٌ ﴾ [القمر: ۱-۲] واحتمال معنى آخر لا يضر (وإلا) أي وإن لم يكثر مشاهدوها (فغير محل النزاع فإنه ليس مما انفرد به الواحد من بين الجماعة، وكلام عيسى عليه السلام وباقي المعجزات من هذا القبيل، قال أكثر العلماء : إن انشقاق القمر كان ليلاً والناس نيام ولم يكن شاهدها من الصحابة إلا واحد أو اثنان ومن الكفرة جماعة قليلة يمكن الكتمان منهم، فلم ينقله إلاّ منهم، فلم ينقله إلا من شاهد من الصحابة، فليس هذا من الباب في شيء (على أن القرآن مغنِ) عن سائر المعجزات، فليس هناك على نقل المعجزات الأخر دواع، فليس من الباب في شيء (قيل) في حواشي ميرزاجان»: التحقيق أن إعجازه لكمال البلاغة) بحيث لا يقدر البشر على إتيان مثله في البلاغة فلا يعلمه إلا الأفراد من البلغاء الذين لم يوجدوا في كل عصر ولا أقل من أنهم قلوا غاية القلة (فكون القرآن مستمراً لا يغني عن ذكر تلك المعجزات) لعدم علم الأكثر بإعجاز ، ولا بد من نقل معجز يعلم إعجازه ليقوم حجة، والجواب عنه أنه نقل القرآن تواتراً، ونقل إنه لم يعارض مع جد المخالفين في ذلك تواتراً، وهذا القدر كاف للعلم بالإعجاز، ويقوم حجة، فنقله على هذا الوجه يكون مغنياً (أقول) في الجواب (البلاغة صفة لازمة له فما دام موجوداً معجز، وفي ذكر المعجز الموجود كفاية) عن ذكر معجزاً آخر قد زال (لا ريب فيه) وفيه نظر ظاهر، فإن الشاك إنما شكك بأن هذا المعجز الموجود لا ينتفع به الأكثر لعدم علمهم بإعجازه، فذكره لا يغني عن ذكر المعجزات الأخر التي إعجازها بين عند كل أحد، فيقوم حجة، فينتفع به فلا جواب إلا بالمراجعة إلى ما قلنا، ويمكن الجواب أيضاً بأن نقل كل معجزة معجزة سوى القرآن وإن كان أحادياً، لكن القدر المشترك بين الكل متواتر، وهو يقوم حجة، فنقله كفاية عن نقل واحد واحد (وأما الفروع التي استدلوا بها فليست مما تتوفر الدواعي على نقله مطلقاً) والمسألة وكانت مفروضة فيما تكثر مشاهدوها وتوفرت الدواعي على نقلهم إياه، وأما الكلام بأن خبر الواحد لا يقبل فيما عمت البلوى به فكلام آخر سيتضح في المسألة الآتية .
He says: The claim of the Rawafid (may Allah disgrace them) regarding the Imamate of the Commander of the Faithful (Ali) is absolutely a lie, due to the necessity of the Rawafid (they said) perhaps their silence was due to a motive that compelled them to conceal. Indeed, silence does not yield certainty unless the motives [for concealment] are known to be absent; but the motives for concealment are many and cannot be enumerated. Thus the one who remains silent is silent about it being a lie. Do you not see that the Christians did not transmit the speech of Jesus (peace be upon our Prophet and upon him) in the cradle when the people entered upon Mary accusing her, and he rebuked them: 'He said: Indeed I am the servant of Allah. He has given me the Scripture and made me a prophet. And He has made me blessed wherever I am and has enjoined upon me prayer and zakah as long as I live, and [made me] dutiful to my mother and did not make me a tyrant disgraced. And peace is on me the day I was born and the day I will die and the day I am raised alive.' [Maryam 30-33] And (the splitting of the moon) was transmitted as single reports from Ibn Mas'ud who said: The moon split during the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and Companions) into two parts: one part above the mountain and one part below it. Then the Messenger of Allah said: 'Bear witness.' Reported by al-Bukhari and Muslim. And (the glorification of pebbles and food) from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: We used to count signs as blessings, but you count them as warnings. And he said: We were with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) on a journey and water was scarce. He said: 'Look for some leftover water.' They brought a little water in a container. He put his hand (peace be upon him) into the container and said: 'Come to the blessed purification, and blessing is from Allah Almighty.' Indeed I saw water gushing from between his fingers (peace be upon him). And we used to hear the glorification of food while it was being eaten. Reported by al-Bukhari. And (the yearning of the trunk) from Jabir (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: When the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to deliver the sermon, he would lean against a trunk of a palm tree from the pillars of the mosque. When the pulpit was made and he stood upon it, the palm tree at which he used to deliver the sermon cried out until it almost split. So the Prophet (peace be upon him) came down and took it and hugged it, and it began to moan like the moaning of a child being quieted until it settled. He said: It wept because of what it used to hear of remembrance. Reported by al-Bukhari. And (the walking of the tree) from Ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) who said: We were with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) on a journey. A Bedouin came, and when he drew near, the Messenger of Allah said to him: 'We testify that there is no god but Allah alone, without partner, and we testify that Muhammad is His servant and His messenger.' He said: 'Who testifies to what you say?' He said: 'This acacia tree.' So the Messenger of Allah called it while he was at the edge of the valley, and it came, dragging its roots, until it stood before him. He asked it to testify three times, and it testified three times that he is as he said. Then it returned to its root. Reported by al-Darimi. And (the greeting of the stone and the gazelle) from Jabir ibn Samurah that the Messenger of Allah said: 'There is a stone in Makkah that used to greet me during the nights of my mission, and I still recognize it.' And many different branches, such as the call to prayer being repeated twice, etc. (as single reports) refers to the transmission; these things were transmitted as single reports while the rest were silent, and one does not judge them as lies. (The answer: The comprehensive motive covering both far and near in every time and place, as they said, is normally absent. And the issue is when they remained silent for a lifetime. Then the motive they mentioned for concealing the report of the Imamate is fear of the three Caliphs and the rest of the ten. Look at their foolishness: how could a group of more than a hundred thousand fear a few men? And how did this fear persist until after their deaths (may Allah be pleased with them)? Then [they also claim] that the Commander of the Faithful was the bravest of people and that all his family were his supporters, and that such as 'Ammar, al-Miqdad, and Abu Dharr were among his supporters. Abu Dharr had a tribe and did not fear the likes of Abu Jahl when he declared Islam openly in front of them. If he was afraid with supporters present, where is bravery? Rather, this fear contradicts bravery and confirms the bravery of the three Caliphs and their courage. Thus it has become clear to you with the most upright arguments that the doctrine of the odious Shia is chosen only by a fool who has reached the height of stupidity and leads to repugnant matters. As for the speech of Jesus in the cradle and the mentioned miracles, if their witnesses were many, they would have become mutawatir, as has been said about the splitting of the moon and the yearning of the trunk: they are mutawatir, and al-Subki explicitly stated their tawatur. There is no improbability in this; indeed the splitting is mentioned in the Quran, so they sufficed with its transmission. If you say: The verse could indicate an event in the afterlife? I say: That is far from the context. For He Almighty said: 'The Hour has drawn near, and the moon has split. And if they see a sign, they turn away and say: Continuous magic.' [al-Qamar 1-2] The possibility of another meaning does not harm. (Otherwise) i.e., if their witnesses were not many, then it is not the subject of dispute, for it is not something that a single person from among the group reported exclusively. The speech of Jesus (peace be upon him) and the rest of the miracles are of this type. Most scholars said: The splitting of the moon occurred at night while people were sleeping, and only one or two of the Companions witnessed it, and a small group of disbelievers who could be concealed, so it was not transmitted except from those few, so it is not from this category at all. (Moreover, the Quran suffices) over other miracles, so there is no incentive to transmit other miracles. So it is not from this category at all. (It was said) in the marginalia of Mirzajan: The verification is that its inimitability is due to the perfection of eloquence, such that human beings are unable to produce its like in eloquence, so only individuals among the eloquent know it, and they do not exist in every age, or at least they are extremely rare. (So the Quran being continuous does not dispense with mentioning those miracles) because most people are unaware of its inimitability, and a miracle whose inimitability is known must be transmitted to serve as proof. The response to this is that the Quran has been transmitted mutawatir, and the fact that it was not challenged despite the strenuous efforts of the opponents is also transmitted mutawatir. This much is sufficient for knowledge of its inimitability and serves as proof. So its transmission in this manner suffices. (I say) in response: (Eloquence is an inherent quality of it; as long as it exists, it is a miracle. And mentioning the existing miracle suffices) from mentioning another miracle that has passed. (There is no doubt about it.) But there is an apparent flaw: the skeptic only doubts that this existing miracle is not beneficial for most people because they do not know its inimitability, so mentioning it does not dispense with mentioning other miracles whose inimitability is clear to everyone, so they serve as proof and benefit. So there is no answer except referring back to what we said. Another possible answer is: Even if each miracle besides the Quran is transmitted as a single report, the common element among all of them is mutawatir, and that serves as proof. So its transmission suffices for the transmission of each one individually. (As for the branches they used as evidence, they are not of the type that there are multiple motives for transmitting them absolutely.) And the issue was assumed to be in matters whose witnesses are many and for which there are multiple motives for transmission. As for the statement that a single report is not accepted in matters of common occurrence, that is another discussion that will become clear in the following issue.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul al-fiqh dispute against the Rawafid (Shia) regarding the argument from silence (sukut) and the tawatur of miracles. The author refutes the Shia claim that the Companions' silence about Ali's alleged appointment to the caliphate proves its truth, explaining that silence only yields certainty when there are no possible motives for concealment. He then enumerates various miracles (splitting of the moon, glorification of pebbles, etc.) and argues that some are mutawatir while others are not. The splitting of the moon is given as an example of tawatur because it is mentioned in the Quran. The author also addresses the objection that the Quran's inimitability is not obvious to everyone, responding that the Quran's tawatur and lack of successful challenge suffice as proof. The passage ends by transitioning to the next issue about khabar wahid in matters of general necessity.

Key Terms
السكوت (al-sukūt): Silence of a group about an event, which does not yield certainty unless absence of motives for concealment is known.
التواتر (al-tawātur): A transmission by a large number that precludes collusion on falsehood, yielding certain knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi argument in this passage, why is the splitting of the moon considered mutawatir?
A) Because it was witnessed by thousands of people.
B) Because it is mentioned in the Quran, which is transmitted mutawatir.
C) Because all hadiths about it are sahih.
D) Because the Rawafid accept it as mutawatir.

Key Takeaway
Silence is not proof when motives for concealment exist; the Quran's inimitability is sufficient as a miracle, and only mutawatir reports yield certainty.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Acceptance of Khabar Wahid in Hudud
Internal Hanafi debate on khabar wahid in hudud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the acceptance of khabar wahid in hudud and evaluate the counter-argument based on the hadith 'idra'u al-hudud bi al-shubuhat'.

Core Idea
Shubha in the proof does not prevent acceptance of khabar wahid in hudud; only shubha in the cause does.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut tackles a key usul debate: can a solitary report (khabar wahid) establish a fixed punishment (hadd)? The dispute hinges on the interpretation of shubha. Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to distinguish between different types of doubt in legal proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue and the schools involved
Determine what the dispute is about and which scholars hold each position.
The majority Hanafis include Abu Yusuf and al-Jassas; the opponents include al-Karkhi and al-Basri.
2
Examine the Hanafi majority proof
The Hanafi position relies on the general principle that a report from a trustworthy narrator is accepted in all practical matters unless a preventer exists.
The narrator is 'adl and reports a practical ruling.
3
Examine the opposing proof
The opponents cite the hadith 'Drive away hudud with shubuhat' and argue that khabar wahid involves shubha.
This hadith is narrated by Abu Hanifa in some versions.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes between shubha in the cause (sabab) and shubha in the proof (dalil). Only shubha in the cause prevents the hadd.
The hadith refers to shubuhat in establishing the cause, not after the hadd is due.
5
Apply the distinction to analogous cases
The Hanafi response is supported by analogy to shahada and zahir al-kitab, which also involve shubha but are accepted.
Shahada is accepted due to textual command (nass); zahir al-kitab is zanni but still used.

الحدود مسألة: (عند الجمهور خبر (الواحد العدل (مقبول في الحدود وهو قول الإمام أبي (يوسف) رحمه الله تعالى عليه (والشيخ أبي بكر (الجصاص) الرازي (خلافاً للكرخي) الشيخ أبي الحسن من الحنفية والبصري) من المعتزلة وأكثر (الحنفية على ما في «التحرير» (لنا) الراوي (عدل) جازم) روي (في) حكم ( عملي فيقبل) روايته (كغيره) أي كما يقبل في غير من العمليات ولعلك تقول : الخصم لا يسلم القبول في كل عملي، بل فيما إذا لم يمنع مانع، وههنا الشبهة مانعة عنده، والمقصود واضح، فإن خبر الواحد مفيد لحكم الله تعالى، فيجب العمل به وهذا واضح إنما الأهم كشف الشبهة لا غير فافهم، الإمام الكرخي وأتباعه (قالوا : قال عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وأهل بيته الصلاة والسلام) من الله تعالى العزيز العلام (ادرؤوا الحدود بالشبهات رواه الإمام أبو حنيفة رضي الله عنه ومثله في بعض السنن أيضاً (وفيه) أي خبر الواحد (شبهة) فلا يقتل في الحدود قلنا: أولاً، المراد درء الحد بالشبهة قبل اللزوم والمعنى : ادرؤوا الحدود بإحداث الشبهات في ثبوت سبب الحدد (لا) الدرء بالشبهة في الحد اللازم) يعني الشبهة في دليل ثبوت الحكم المثبت في الذمة، فإنها غير مانعة، كما في سائر العمليات وعلى هذا فالاستدلال بهذا الوجه على عدم إثبات الحد بالقياس لا يتم، بل يستدل عليه بعدم اهتداء العقل إلى التقديرات الشرعية إن تم (و) قلنا (ثانياً) دليلكم (منقوض بالشهادة لأن فيه شبهة أيضاً، فلا يقبل بل فيه شبهة في ثبوت السبب، والجواب عنه : أن أمر الشهادة تعبدي على خلاف القياس، فلا يقاس عليه (و) منقوض بـ (ظاهر الكتاب) فإنه ظني أيضاً، فلا يصلح إثباته للحدود (وربما يتخلص عن النقضين (بأن التعبد بالشهادة بالنص) القطعي فيخص به ظاهر الخبر وظاهر الكتاب قطعي) وليس فيه شبهة الانتفاء الاحتمال الناشيء عن دليل وهو المعتبر لا مجرد الاحتمال فافهم، وقد يدفع هذا الجواب بأن العموم الوارد في آيات الحدود مخصوص وهو ظني اتفاقاً، وهذا إنما يتم لو كان للتخصيص بالكلام المستقل الملاصق وإثباته خرط القتاد وقلنا ثالثاً : إنه منقوض بالخبر المشهور إذ فيه شبهة أيضاً، وجوابه بأنه مفيد للطمأنينة والشبهة بعدها غير معتبرة لعدم تشائيها عن دليل (فافهم).
The chapter on hudud. Issue: According to the majority, the report of a single 'adl is accepted in hudud, and this is the saying of Abu Yusuf and Sheikh Abu Bakr al-Jassas al-Razi, contrary to al-Karkhi, Sheikh Abu al-Hasan of the Hanafis, and al-Basri of the Mu'tazila, and most Hanafis as in al-Tahrir. Our proof: The narrator is 'adl and decisive, he reports a practical ruling, so his report is accepted like other practical rulings... And the opposing proof is the hadith: 'Drive away hudud with doubts' and khabar wahid has doubt. We say: First, the meaning is to drive away the hudud by causing doubts in the establishment of the cause of the hadd, not by doubt in the hadd itself after it is established. Second, your proof is refuted by shahada which also has doubt but is accepted, though that is ta'abbudi. Third, refuted by zahir al-kitab which is zanni. Fourth, refuted by khabar mashhur which has doubt but gives tranquility.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage discusses whether a khabar wahid from an 'adl (reliable) narrator is accepted in hudud (fixed punishments). The majority of Hanafis, including Abu Yusuf and al-Jassas, accept it, contrary to al-Karkhi and some others. The opponents cite the hadith 'Drive away hudud with doubts' (shubuhat), arguing that khabar wahid involves shubha. The Hanafi response: first, the hadith means drive away the punishment before it is established by shubuhat in the cause, not after it is established. The shubha in the proof of the ruling is not a preventer, as in other practical matters. Second, the opponent's argument is refuted by analogy to shahada (testimony) which also involves shubha but is accepted; however, shahada is based on textual evidence (ta'abbudi) and cannot be analogized. Third, it is refuted by zahir al-kitab (apparent meaning of Quran) which is also zanni but accepted. Fourth, it is refuted by khabar mashhur which also has shubha but gives tranquility. The Hanafi position is that khabar wahid is accepted in hudud.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubha): A probabilistic doubt that arises from the nature of the evidence, considered inconclusive if based on a valid proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, is khabar wahid accepted in hudud?
A) No, because of shubha
B) Yes, because it is a practical ruling like others
C) Only if it is mashhur
D) Only if it is mutawatir

Key Takeaway
Khabar wahid from an 'adl narrator is accepted in hudud because shubha in the proof does not prevent its acceptance; only shubha in the cause of the punishment does.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
