Defining 'Adala: Malaka or Mere Avoidance of Sin?
Debating whether 'adala is a settled trait or simply avoiding sin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two opinions on the nature of 'adala (malaka vs. mere avoidance of sin) and evaluate the Hanafi position based on the five arguments and counterarguments.

Core Idea
'Adala requires a stable trait of God-consciousness (malaka), not just procedural sinlessness.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut presents a foundational debate in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: is 'adala (integrity) a settled trait of character (malaka) or merely the absence of visible sin? The author advocates for the malaka view, which aligns with the later Hanafi position that a narrator or witness must possess a stable quality ensuring truthfulness. Over the course of the passage, he gives five proofs against the malaka requirement, then answers them, and finally presents his own argument based on fitra and istishab, which is then critiqued. This lesson unpacks that debate and its implications for accepting testimony and narration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed definitional element
Identify the term 'adala and the two competing definitions: malaka (stable trait) vs. salama an al-fisq (mere absence of sin).
The dispute is whether a narrator/witness must have a permanent trait or just avoid sin at the time.
2
List the five arguments for non-malaka
Extract the five arguments given in the text: (1) child at puberty, (2) repentant sinner, (3) malaka not lost by one lapse, (4) Bedouin testimony, (5) [the fifth is actually the general principle? The text lists five: first through fifth]. Summarize each.
These are the initial claims; the rejoinders will follow.
3
Analyze the rejoinder to each argument
For each of the five arguments, read the author's response: e.g., the child's case is specific to testimony not narration; the repentant must show signs; the Bedouin was probably already upright; etc.
Notice how the author reinterprets the examples.
4
Examine the fitra and istishab argument
The author then presents his own argument: birth on fitra and istishab support the malaka view. Then he critiques these arguments, showing they are not conclusive.
This section shows the author's critical method.
5
Evaluate the final tarjih
Conclude that the Hanafi position (as per this text) requires a malaka. Understand the reasoning: true avoidance must stem from opposing the lower self, which constitutes a stable trait.
The mufta bihi is that 'adala is a malaka.

يفيد كثرة الفسق في الصحابة العياذ بالله ولا يصح فيهم احتماله العياذ بالله فضلاً عن الكثرة، وحينئذ فالجواب عنه أن أعوان السلاطين الظالمين أكثر بكثير من باقي الرجال، فأين كثرة العدالة، نعم. الكذب كان فالملكة ليست شرطاً للقبول (وأما رابعاً : فلأن الملكة لا تنعدم بالتخلف مرة والعدالة تزول بالفسق ولو مرة فالملكة ليست عدالة (وأما خامساً : فأسلم أعرابي فشهد بالهلال فقبل عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام) شهادته، فأمر أن ينادي في الناس أن يصوموا غداً رواه الدارقطني، فاكتفى عليه وعلى آله الصلاة والسلام بظاهر العدالة ولم ينتظر إلى الملكة (وذلك) أي القبول وثبوت العدالة لأن الإسلام يجب ما قبله) ولم يعمل بعده سيئة فشهد وهو سالم عن أسباب الفسق والحاصل منع كون العدالة ملكة، والمذكورات إسناد والجواب : أنه هب أن الشرط ليس الملكة بل أقيم الاجتناب واعتبر لكن لا مطلقاً، بل الاجتناب لمخالفة هوى النفس، لأنه هو المرجح للصدق، وهو غير موجود في المتسور، وأما قبول شهادة الصبي بعد البلوغ فللفرق بين الشهادة والرواية، كيف وشهادة المستور مقبولة عنده في ظاهر المذهب لمكان الضرورة، وعدم حضور العدول والثقات حين المعاملات وأما قبول شهادة التائب فمشروطة بأن يظهر عليه آثار التوبة حتى يظن مخالفة الهوى فيظن صدقه، وأما قبول شهادة الأعرابي فلفظ ما روي في السنن عن ابن عباس أنه قال جاء أعرابي فقال : رأيت الهلال فقال: «أتشهد أن لا إله إلا الله؟ قال: نعم، قال: «أتشهد أن محمداً رسول الله؟ قال : نعم قال : يا بلال أذن في الناس أن يصوموا وهذا لا يقوم حجة على قبول المستور، فلعله كان مسلماً من قبل وعدلاً، وأما تقرير الشهادتين فلتقوية الشهادة باليمين فتدبر (ولك ترجيح (العدالة على الفسق بأن الولادة على الفطرة) فطرة الإسلام، قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم : «ما من مولود إلا ويولد على الفطرة» فأبواه يهودانه أو ينصرانه أو يمجسانه، كما تنتج البهيمة جمعاء هل تحسون فيها من جدعاء؟» ثم يقول أبو هريرة : فطرة الله التي فطر الناس عليها لا تبديل لخلق الله ذلك الدين القيم» رواه البخاري والإسلام على الطهارة فإنه يجب ما قبله والأصل بقاء ما كان على ما كان ما يظهر خلافه، فالأصل البقاء على الطهارة ما لم يظهر فسق (فتأمل) والجواب أولاً بأنه منقوض بمن لم يعلم منه آثار الكفر والإيمان لكن ولد في دار الإسلام فإن المقدمات جارية فيه، فإن ولادته على الفطرة فطرة الإسلام والإسلام على الطهارة، والأصل بقاء ما كان على ما كان، وثانياً : هذا الاستدلال بالاستصحاب وهو غير حجة، وإنما تكفي الأصالة للدفع عند بعض المشايخ لا للاستحقاق، فلا يصلح حجة في إثبات قبول القول وثالثاً : أصالة بقاء ما كان على ما كان إنما هي إذا لم يعارضها معارض وههنا العدالة وإن كانت أصلاً لكن ملازمة غلبة الهوى على الإنسان تعارضها فلا وجه لبقائها ما لم يدل دليل على مخالفة الهوى فافهم وتثبت
It implies much sinfulness in the Companions, God forbid, and it is not valid to assume it in them, God forbid, let alone abundance. Then the answer is that the helpers of unjust rulers are much more numerous than other men; so where is the abundance of integrity? Indeed, lying was rare, no doubt, and to this extent the Lawgiver (peace be upon him and his family and companions) attested. And if we grant abundance of sinfulness in that early period, it prevents abundance of sinfulness in the narrators of hadith, because most of them are upright. So understand, for there is a consideration apparent from the histories of those sinful rulers. And because integrity is an accidental trait opposing its contrary, so it is not original. I say: Integrity, even if it is a trait, but what is meant here—in the condition for accepting narration—is safety from sinfulness even if it has not become a trait. Firstly, because truthfulness outweighs safety with Islam over lying, so it yields probability, so it must be considered, and one should not wait for the trait, for the condition of integrity was only because it necessitates truthfulness and distances from lying. Secondly, because it is established with the jurists that when a child reaches puberty he is considered upright because he was not obligated during childhood and did not sin afterwards, so his testimony is accepted until he sins. If the required integrity were the trait, it would not be accepted. Thirdly, because if a sinner repents, his testimony is accepted as long as he is repentant without waiting for a trait. So the trait is not a condition for acceptance. Fourthly, because a trait is not nullified by a single lapse, but integrity is removed by sin even once, so the trait is not integrity. Fifthly, a Bedouin accepted Islam and testified to seeing the crescent, and the Prophet (peace be upon him and his family and companions) accepted his testimony and ordered Bilal to announce to the people to fast the next day—reported by al-Daraqutni. The Prophet was content with apparent integrity and did not wait for a trait. That is, acceptance and establishment of integrity because Islam erases what came before, and he had not committed a sin after it, so he testified while being free from causes of sinfulness. The conclusion is the prevention of integrity being a trait, and the mentioned [arguments] are a support. And the answer: Assuming the condition is not the trait but avoidance was established and considered, but not absolutely; rather avoidance from opposing the lower self, because it is what gives preference to truthfulness, and it is not present in the mustur (concealed person). As for accepting the testimony of a child after puberty, it is due to the difference between testimony and narration. How so? The testimony of the mustur is accepted according to him in the apparent madhhab due to necessity and the absence of upright and reliable persons at the time of transactions. As for accepting the testimony of a repentant person, it is conditional upon signs of repentance becoming apparent so that it is assumed that he opposes his lower self, so his truthfulness is assumed. As for accepting the testimony of the Bedouin, the wording of what is reported in the Sunan from Ibn Abbas: A Bedouin came and said: 'I saw the crescent.' The Prophet asked: 'Do you testify that there is no god but Allah?' He said: 'Yes.' He asked: 'Do you testify that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah?' He said: 'Yes.' He said: 'O Bilal, announce to the people that they should fast.' This does not constitute proof for accepting the mustur; perhaps he was Muslim before and upright. As for affirmation of the two testimonies, it was to strengthen the testimony with an oath, so ponder. And you may prefer integrity over sinfulness by saying birth is upon the fitra (natural disposition) of Islam. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and companions) said: 'Every child is born upon the fitra; his parents make him a Jew, a Christian, or a Magian, just as the animal gives birth to a perfect offspring—do you find any mutilated?' Then Abu Huraira says: 'The fitra of Allah upon which He created mankind. There is no alteration of Allah's creation. That is the straight religion.' Reported by al-Bukhari. And Islam is upon purity, for it erases what came before, and the principle is that what remains remains as it is until its opposite appears. So the principle is continuance upon purity until sinfulness appears. So reflect. And the answer: Firstly, it is disproven by one whose signs of disbelief and faith are not known, but who was born in the abode of Islam; for the premises hold for him: his birth is upon the fitra of Islam, and Islam is upon purity, and the principle is that what remains remains as it is. Secondly, this deduction is by istishab (presumption of continuity), and it is not a proof. Originality suffices for defense according to some mashayikh, not for entitlement, so it is not suitable as a proof for establishing acceptance of a statement. Thirdly, the principle of continuance of what was is only when there is no opposing factor; here, although integrity is original, the predominant adherence of the lower self to man opposes it, so there is no basis for its continuance unless evidence indicates opposition to the lower self. So understand, and it is established.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a legal debate on the nature of 'adala (integrity) as a condition for accepting hadith narration and testimony. The author presents two positions: that 'adala is a settled trait (malaka) or that it is merely the absence of sin. He first cites objections to requiring a malaka, giving five proofs: (1) truthfulness can be assumed from Islam and absence of sin without a malaka; (2) a child who reaches puberty without sinning is considered 'adl even without a malaka; (3) a repentant sinner is accepted immediately without waiting for a malaka; (4) a malaka is not lost by one sin, but 'adala is; (5) the Prophet accepted a Bedouin's testimony based on apparent integrity. The rejoinder defends the malaka view, arguing that the required avoidance must be from opposing the lower self—which constitutes a malaka—and explains away the counterexamples: the child's case differs from narration, the repentant must show signs, and the Bedouin was probably already upright. The author then strengthens his position by citing birth on fitra and istishab, but then responds to those arguments, concluding that istishab is not a strong proof and that the predominance of base desires opposes the presumption of 'adala. The lesson underscores the nuanced Hanafi usul position that 'adala requires a stable trait of God-consciousness, not mere procedural sinlessness.

Key Terms
العدالة (al-ʿadāla): السلامة عن الفسق وإن لم تصر ملكة في أحد القولين
الملكة (al-malaka): صفة مستقرة في النفس تمنع من الفسق
الفسق (al-fisq): الخروج عن طاعة الله بارتكاب الكبائر أو الإصرار على الصغائر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is one of the arguments given to show that 'adala does not require a malaka?
A) A child who reaches puberty without sin is accepted as 'adl even without a malaka.
B) A fasiq after repentance must wait for a malaka to be established.
C) The Prophet accepted a Bedouin's testimony only after investigating his past.
D) The birth on fitra is a proof of 'adala that cannot be refuted.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position is that 'adala requires a stable malaka, not just temporary avoidance of sin, to ensure the reliability of narration and testimony.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
10 min
Action on a Narration is Tazkiya, Not Ta'dil over Jarh
Refutation of al-Badi's claim that action on a narration is ta'dil over jarh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between tazkiya and ta'dil in Hanafi usul and evaluate the claim that acting on a narration necessitates precedence over jarh.

Core Idea
Acting on a hadith is tazkiya, not formal testimony; non-action may be due to other valid reasons.

In this passage, the author refutes the argument of al-Badi' who claimed that a scholar's action on a hadith constitutes a ta'dil (formal validation) that must take precedence over jarh (disparagement). The Hanafi position is that such action is merely tazkiya (indication of trustworthiness) and leaving off action is not necessarily a jarh because other factors may be at play. Understanding this distinction is crucial for hadith criticism and the methodology of accepting or rejecting narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim of al-Badi'
What does the author of al-Badi' argue about the relationship between action on a narration and the principle of ta'dil over jarh?
The claim is that rejecting a narrator due to jarh and accepting due to ta'dil falls under this chapter.
2
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal
Why does the Muhaqqiq argue that action is tazkiya, not ta'dil? What is the difference?
Tazkiya is an informal indication, not a formal testimony like ta'dil.
3
Recognize reasons for non-action that are not jarh
List the possible reasons given for leaving action: stronger evidence, abrogation, extra condition. How do these prevent jarh?
These possibilities create doubt, so jarh is not established.
4
Analyze the example of Ma'qil ibn Sinan
How does the hadith of Barwa' al-Ashhajiyya illustrate the point? What was the disagreement between Ibn Mas'ud and 'Ali?
Ibn Mas'ud accepted it; 'Ali rejected it. The passage examines whether 'Ali's rejection constitutes a jarh.
5
Evaluate counter-arguments on 'Ali's response
Why is 'Ali's statement not a clear jarh? Consider the possibility of it being a general description or due to lack of knowledge.
The passage argues that 'Ali may have meant a general characterization of Bedouins, not a specific attack on Ma'qil.

ولما كان مزعوم صاحب البديع أن هذا من باب تقديم التعديل على الجرح لأن الرد لأجل جرح في الراوي والقبول للتعديل مع التقديم للجرح كما سيجيء إن شاء الله تعالى أراد إزالة هذا الزعم وقال: (وليس) هذا (من) باب (تقديم التعديل على الجرح (كما) زعم (في البديع بل العمل) بخبره (توثيق) له فإن عمل المجتهد توثيق (والترك) لعمل ليس بجرح لجواز أن يكون لوجدان معارض أقوى أو مساو أو للعلم بانتساخه أو لزعمه شرطاً زائداً في وجوب العمل على العدالة والضبط ومع قيام هذه الاحتمالات لا يتيقن بالجرح، بل لا يظن أيضاً كما مر أن العمل بخلاف الرواية ليس جرحاً (ومثلوه بحديث معقل بن سنان أنه عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام) قضى لبروع الأشجعية حين مات عنها زوجها قبل التسمية) لمهر وكانت مفوضة بمهر المثل، قبله ابن (بمهر مسعود حيث كان حكم بهذا، فلما سمع الحديث سر به، وقد مر تخريج هذا (ورده) أمير المؤمنين (علي) رضي الله عنه قائلاً :) ما نصنع بقول أعرابي بوال على عقبيه حسبها الميراث لا مهر لها وأثر أمير المؤمنين لم يظهر ثبوته في كتب أهل الحديث، والذي مر من رواية «الصحاح لا يدل عليه وقال العيني في شرح «الكنز»: قال ابن المنذر لم يصح هذا عن علي، وقال الشيخ ابن الهمام أن أمير المؤمنين لم يلق معقلاً حتى يحلفه، وكان هو رضي الله تعالى عنه لا يرى العمل قبل التحليف ثم لو سلم ففيه جرح في معقل لا سكوت عن العمل فليس المثال ،مطابقاً، إلا أن يقال لعله رضي الله عنه أراد توصيف الجنس، يعني أنه أعرابي والأعراب فيهم البول على العقبين ولم يرد أن هذا الأعرابي شأنه ذلك، فغايته الإخبار بعدم معرفة الحال وليس فيه تبيان الجرح ، وقد يقال أيضاً: إنه لم يستدل به ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه، بل إنما كان سر به لمطابقة فتواه بالرأي الحديث، فغايته القبول لوجود التقوية بالرأي أو غيره من المتابعات وهذا أشبه بالجدل، ثم هذا الحديث ليس مما تفرد به معقل بن سنان بل رواه معقل بن يسار أيضاً، وقال العيني: الاختلاف في اسم الراوي لا يقدح إذا كان الراوي مشهوراً وقال هو أيضاً. قال البيهقي : جميع روايات هذا الحديث وأسانيدها صحيحة والله أعلم
And when the claimant of the author of al-Badi' claimed that this is from the chapter of giving precedence to ta'dil over jarh, because the rejection is due to a jarh in the narrator and the acceptance is due to ta'dil with the precedence of jarh, as will come, God willing, he intended to remove this claim and said: (And it is not) this (from) the chapter of (giving precedence to ta'dil over jarh (as) he claimed (in al-Badi' rather the action) upon his report is a tazkiya) for him, for the action of the mujtahid is a tazkiya, (and the leaving) of action is not a jarh because it is possible that it is due to finding a stronger or similar opposing evidence, or due to knowledge of its abrogation, or due to his claim of an extra condition for obligation of action upon trustworthiness and precision. And with these possibilities, one is not certain of jarh, nor even assumes it, as it has passed that acting contrary to a narration is not a jarh. (And they gave the example of the hadith of Ma'qil ibn Sinan that he (peace be upon him and his family and companions) judged for Barwa' al-Ashhajiyya when her husband died before specifying the dower, and she was a woman with delegated authority (tafwid) and entitled to the dower of the like. Ibn Mas'ud accepted it because he had ruled with this, and when he heard the hadith, he was pleased with it, and its takhrij has already passed. (And the Commander of the Faithful, Ali, may God be pleased with him, rejected it saying: 'What shall we do with the statement of a Bedouin who urinates on his heels? She deserves inheritance, not dower.' And the effect of the Commander of the Faithful has not been proven in the books of the hadith scholars. What has passed from the narration of the Sahih does not indicate it. Al-Ayni said in Sharh al-Kanz: Ibn al-Mundhir said this is not authentic from Ali. And Shaykh Ibn al-Hammam said that the Commander of the Faithful did not meet Ma'qil to make him take an oath, and he (Ali) did not consider action without oath. Then if it is granted, then there is a jarh in Ma'qil, not silence about action, so the example is not consistent. Unless it is said: perhaps he (Ali) intended to describe the genus, meaning that he is a Bedouin and Bedouins have the habit of urinating on their heels, and he did not mean that this particular Bedouin has that habit. So its utmost is informing of not knowing the state, and it does not contain a clear jarh. And it may also be said: Ibn Mas'ud did not use it as evidence, but rather he was pleased with it because his own opinion matched the hadith, so its utmost is acceptance due to reinforcement by opinion or other follow-ups, and this is more like dialectic. Then this hadith is not exclusive to Ma'qil ibn Sinan, but Ma'qil ibn Yasar also narrated it. Al-Ayni said: The difference in the name of the narrator does not harm if the narrator is well-known. And he also said: Al-Bayhaqi said: All narrations of this hadith and their chains are authentic. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a rebuttal of the claim made by the author of al-Badi' that this issue falls under the principle of giving precedence to ta'dil over jarh. The author argues that acting upon a narration is a form of tazkiya (validation), not a formal ta'dil, and that leaving off action is not necessarily a jarh because there could be other reasons such as a stronger opposing evidence, abrogation, or an extra condition. The example of Ma'qil ibn Sinan's hadith about Barwa' al-Ashhajiyya is discussed: Ibn Mas'ud accepted it, while 'Ali rejected it. The author then analyzes 'Ali's rejection, noting that it may not constitute a jarh since it could be interpreted as a description of the general nature of Bedouins rather than a specific criticism of Ma'qil. The passage concludes by noting that the hadith is narrated by multiple chains, so it is authentic.

Key Terms
تقديم التعديل على الجرح (taqdīm al-ta‘dīl ‘alā al-jarḥ): Giving precedence to the validation (ta'dil) over the disparagement (jarh) of a narrator
تزكية (tazkiya): Validation of a narrator's trustworthiness through indication, not formal testimony
جرح (jarḥ): Disparagement of a narrator's integrity or memory

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is leaving off action on a narration not necessarily a jarh?
A) Because the narrator might have been forgotten
B) Because there could be a stronger opposing evidence, abrogation, or an extra condition
C) Because the narrator is always trustworthy
D) Because jarh only applies to the Prophet's narrations

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a scholar's non-action on a hadith does not imply a jarh because it may be due to other valid reasons; action itself is tazkiya, not a formal ta'dil.

Is Tazkiyah Shahada or Khabar? A Hanafi Usul Dispute
Debate on legal classification of tazkiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul distinction between shahada and khabar to classify tazkiyah and evaluate the ihtiyat (caution) argument used by the opposing view.

Core Idea
Tazkiyah is a report (khabar), not testimony (shahada), so one trustworthy person suffices.

In Hanafi usul, the classification of a statement determines its legal requirements. The opposing view argues that tazkiyah is shahada and thus requires two witnesses, using caution (ihtiyat) to demand number. This lesson unpacks the dispute and shows how the Hanafi position refutes the caution argument by exposing its internal inconsistency and affirming the analogy to other reports.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
Read the opening lines to see the two positions: 'They said: tazkiyah is shahada... It was objected that it is a khabar.' Recognize that the classification determines whether one or two persons are needed.
The opposing view treats tazkiyah as shahada; the Hanafi view as khabar.
2
Follow the ihtiyat argument and its counter
Track the argument that 'legislating what has not been legislated is worse than abandoning what has been legislated.' Notice how both sides use caution to argue for their number requirement.
The author shows that the caution argument would logically lead to requiring two for narration as well, which is not accepted.
3
Analyze the author's rebuttal of the ihtiyat argument
See the line: 'If this were valid, it would require number in narration as well...' This reveals the flaw: the ihtiyat argument proves too much.
The caution argument is self-defeating because it would apply to all reports, including hadith narration, where one trustworthy narrator is accepted.
4
Recognize the final Hanafi response
The author concludes that shahada is a specific type of khabar, but tazkiyah does not meet its strict criteria. It remains a general khabar, so one suffices. The analogy to other reports (e.g., a slave's report) is valid.
The Hanafi position: 'It is a report that is not testimony, and every such report suffices with one.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا : التزكية شهادة وكل شهادة لا يكون فيها إلا اثنان فيتعدد وعورض بأنه إخبار فلا يتعدد كسائر الإخبارات فرجح بأن الاحتياط في إيجاب العدد فعورض بأن الاحتياط في الكفاية بالواحد لأن فيه إيجاباً على الأحوال ويدفع بأن شرع ما لم يشرع شر من ترك ما شرع كذا في التحرير فلو اكتفى بالواحد يلزم تشريع الإيجاب عند تعديل واحد وهو تشريع غير المشروع لو كان العدد شرطاً ولو شرط العدد يلزم ترك العمل به وهو ترك المشروع إن لم يكن شرطاً ففي الاكتفاء بالواحد احتياط بتشريع ما لم يشرع وفي اشتراط العدد احتياط بالاجتناب عنه مع احتمال ترك المشروع والأول شر من الثاني فالاحتياط في اشتراط العدد وفيه أن في اشتراط العدد احتمال إيجاب أمر زائد لم يجب من قبل لو كان بالواحد كفاية ففيه أيضاً تشريع ما لم يشرع كما في الاكتفاء بالواحد احتمال إباحة ما لم يكن مباحاً لو كان العدد مشروطاً فاستويا أقول : وأيضا لو تم هذا لأوجب العدد في الرواية أيضاً فإن فيه احتمال ترك المشروع وفي الكفاية بالواحد احتمال شرع ما لم يشرع فافهم وهذا إنما يرد لو كان مقصوده ترجيح إيجاب الاثنين في الشهادة وليس بل مقصوده إبطال الترجيح بالأحوطية وحينئذ لا ورود أصلاً و يدفع بأن الشهادة أخص من الإخبار فإنها إخبار خاص فاعتبارها أتم من اعتبار الإخبارية فالكبرى القائلة بأن كل إخبار يكفي فيه الواحد ممنوعة وكذا لا يصح القياس على سائر الإخبارات كذا قيل في حواشي مرزاجان أقول : مراد المعارض أنه إخبار مغاير للشهادة فالحاصل أنه إخبار غير شهادة وكل إخبار كذلك يكفي فيه الواحد ولذا يقبل فيه العبد فتدبر
They said: tazkiyah is a testimony, and every testimony only has two, so it requires multiplicity. It was objected that it is a report, so it does not require multiplicity like other reports. So they gave preponderance by saying that caution lies in requiring number. It was objected that caution lies in sufficiency with one because it imposes an obligation in all circumstances. It is repelled by saying that legislating what has not been legislated is worse than abandoning what has been legislated, as in al-Tahrir. So if one is sufficed with, it necessitates legislation of obligation upon the ta'dil of one, which is legislation of what is not legislated if number were a condition. And if number is required, it necessitates abandoning action upon it, which is abandoning what is legislated if it were not a condition. So in sufficing with one there is caution by legislating what has not been legislated, and in requiring number there is caution by avoiding it along with the possibility of abandoning what is legislated. The first is worse than the second, so caution lies in requiring number. But it is said: in requiring number there is the possibility of imposing an extra obligation that was not previously required if one were sufficient, so it too involves legislating what has not been legislated, just as in sufficing with one there is the possibility of permitting what was not permitted if number were required. So they are equal. I say: Also, if this were valid, it would require number in narration as well, because it involves possibility of abandoning what is legislated, and sufficing with one involves possibility of legislating what has not been legislated. So understand. This only applies if his intent was to give preponderance to requiring two in testimony, but his intent is not to invalidate the preponderance by caution, in which case there is no objection at all. And it is repelled by saying that testimony is more specific than report, for it is a special report, so its consideration is more complete than the consideration of being a report. So the major premise that every report suffices with one is denied, and likewise qiyas to other reports is not valid. So it is said in the margins of Mirzajan. I say: The objector's intent is that it is a report different from testimony, so it is a report that is not testimony, and every such report suffices with one, hence a slave is accepted in it. So reflect.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute over whether tazkiyah should be treated as shahada (testimony) requiring two persons, or as khabar (report) requiring only one. The Hanafi position, supported by the author, leans towards khabar. The argument begins with those who say tazkiyah is shahada, so it requires two. The objector says it is an khabar, so one suffices. The proponent tries to use the principle of caution (ihtiyat) to favor requiring two: legislating something not legislated is worse than abandoning what is legislated. But the objector counters that requiring two also risks legislating an extra obligation if one suffices. The author then notes that if this argument were sound, it would force number in narration too, which is not the case. The final resolution is that testimony is a specific kind of report, so the general rule about reports does not apply. The Hanafi view is thus that tazkiyah is a report, not a testimony, and one person suffices, just as in other akhbar (e.g., a slave's report is accepted for tazkiyah).

Key Terms
تزكية (tazkiyah): Attestation of a person's integrity or qualification, used in legal contexts to evaluate witnesses or narrators.
شهادة (shahada): Legal testimony that requires two witnesses in most cases.
إخبار (khabar): A report or narration that does not necessarily require multiplicity.
احتياط (ihtiyat): Caution or precaution in legal rulings, preferring the safer option.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position defended in this passage, why does one person suffice for tazkiyah?
A) Because tazkiyah is a form of shahada, but the rule for shahada allows one in this case.
B) Because tazkiyah is a khabar, and in khabar one person is sufficient.
C) Because the Quran explicitly states that one witness is enough for tazkiyah.
D) Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said 'One witness is enough for tazkiyah.'

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, tazkiyah is classified as khabar, so one trustworthy person suffices; the caution argument cannot override this because it would lead to absurd consequences.

The Five Madhahib on Jarh and Ta'dil: Explicit vs. Implicit
Summarizes five scholarly positions on jarh and ta'dil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the five scholarly positions on whether jarh and ta'dil require explicit reasoning, and apply the Hanafi position on ta'dil being accepted generally.

Core Idea
Jarh must be explicit; ta'dil can be general — because defects are specific but integrity is broad.

In usul al-fiqh and hadith criticism, a key question is whether a witness or narrator must be discredited or accredited with specific details or whether a general statement suffices. This passage presents five different positions (madhahib) on this issue, showing the Hanafi preference for allowing general ta'dil while requiring explicit jarh. Understanding this distinction helps in evaluating the reliability of testimony and narrations.

Guided Path
1
List the five positions
First, enumerate the five views as given in the text: (1) Majority of Hanafis and muhaddithin: jarh must be explicit (or in the ruling of explicit), ta'dil accepted generally. (2) Opposite view: ta'dil must be explicit, jarh general. (3) Both must be explicit. (4) Qadi's view: absolute suffices from a person of insight. (5) Imam Abu Hanifa's view: absolute suffices from a knowledgeable person; otherwise not.
2
Identify the Hanafi majority position
The first position (majority of Hanafis and muhaddithin) is the most relied upon in the Hanafi school: jarh must be explicit (or its ruling) because the specific cause of discrediting matters, while ta'dil can be general because grounds for integrity are numerous.
3
Contrast with the opposing view
The second position reverses the rule: it requires explicit ta'dil but allows general jarh. Reflect on why some might prefer this — perhaps because discrediting is easier to justify generally? Note that Hanafis reject this.
4
Analyze the third position
The third view requires both to be explicit. This is the strictest and most cautious approach, but the Hanafis consider it impractical, especially for ta'dil.
5
Merge the final two positions
The fourth (Qadi) and fifth (Imam) positions both depend on the person's knowledge. The author merges them because accepting jarh/ta'dil from an ignorant person is not permissible. Understand that ultimately there are effectively four distinct views.
The Hanafi school adopts a nuanced position: general ta'dil is sufficient from a reliable person, but jarh requires detail.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: أكثر الفقهاء والمحدثين قالوا لا يقبل الجرح إلا مبيناً ولا حكماً كما روي عن علماء هذه الشأن فإنه وإن لم يكن مبيناً لكن إنما قالوا به التدقيق ومعرفة الجرح على الخصوص فهو في حكم المبين بخلاف التعديل يعني أن التعديل يقبل غير مبين أيضاً وقيل بالعكس أي لا يقبل التعديل إلا مبيناً بخلاف الجرح وقيل لا يكفي الاطلاق فيهما بل يجب التبيين وقال القاضي يكفي الإطلاق فيهما من ذي بصيرة في الجرح والتعديل فلا وهذا بعينه ما روي عن الإمام إن كان المزكي عالماً كفى الإطلاق فيهما وإلا فلا يكفي فيهما وبعضهم نقلوا مذهب القاضي أنه يكفي الاطلاق فيهما مطلقاً ومذهب الإمام يكفي الاطلاق من العالم البصير ولما كان هذا بعيداً محضاً فإنه لا يليق بحال أحد أن يقبل الجرح أو التعديل ممن لا معرفة له جعل المصنف المذهبين واحداً وقال الحق أنه لا خامس
Issue: Most jurists and hadith scholars said: jarh is not accepted unless it is made explicit, not as a ruling; as narrated from scholars of this field, even if it is not explicit, but they said it due to precision and specific knowledge of jarh, so it is in the ruling of explicit. Contrary to ta'dil, meaning ta'dil is accepted even if not explicit. And it was said the opposite: i.e., ta'dil is not accepted unless explicit, contrary to jarh. And it was said that absolute (unqualified) is not sufficient in both, rather specification is required. And Qadi said: absolute is sufficient in both from one who has insight in jarh and ta'dil. So this is exactly what is narrated from Imam: if the one giving tazkiyah is knowledgeable, absolute is sufficient in both; otherwise it is not sufficient in both. Some transmitted the madhhab of Qadi as absolute sufficiency in both, and the madhhab of Imam as sufficiency of absolute from the knowledgeable and insightful. And since this is purely far-fetched, because it is not fitting in any situation to accept jarh or ta'dil from one who has no knowledge, the author made the two madhhabs one and said: the truth is that there is no fifth.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage enumerates the different scholarly positions (madhahib) on whether jarh (discrediting) and ta'dil (accrediting) of a witness or narrator must be done with explicit detail (mubayyan) or can be left general (mutlaq). The majority view of the Hanafis and muhaddithin is that jarh must be explicit (or at least in the ruling of explicit) because knowing the specific cause of discrediting is necessary to verify its validity, whereas ta'dil can be general because the grounds for trustworthiness are many and difficult to enumerate. An opposing view says the opposite: ta'dil must be explicit. A third view says both require specification. A fourth view from Qadi (Qadi Khan?) allows absolute statements from a person of insight. The fifth view from Imam Abu Hanifa is that if the one giving tazkiyah is knowledgeable (alim), absolute is sufficient; otherwise not. The author notes that the fourth and fifth can be merged because both require knowledge, so essentially there are only four distinct positions, not five. The Hanafi position adopted is that ta'dil is accepted without detail due to difficulty, while jarh requires detail due to potential differences in what constitutes a defect.

Key Terms
جرح (jarh): Discrediting a witness or narrator by pointing out a defect in their integrity.
تعديل (ta'dil): Accrediting a witness or narrator by affirming their integrity.
مبين (mubayyan): Made explicit or detailed, as opposed to general (mutlaq).
مطلق (mutlaq): General or unqualified, not specifying details.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafis and muhaddithin in this passage, what is the ruling on accepting jarh and ta'dil?
A) Both jarh and ta'dil must be explicit (mubayyan).
B) Jarh must be explicit, but ta'dil is accepted even if general.
C) Ta'dil must be explicit, but jarh is accepted even if general.
D) Both can be accepted in general form from any person.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows general ta'dil but requires explicit jarh due to the difficulty of enumerating all grounds for integrity while needing specific reasons for discrediting.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
12 min
Hanafi Reasoning for Differentiating Jarh and Ta'dil
Derives the Hanafi ruling that ta'dil may be general due to necessity, while jarh requires detail due to ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principles of necessity (haraj) and disagreement (ikhtilaf) to derive the rule that ta'dil may be general while jarh must be explicit.

Core Idea
Ta'dil is accepted generally due to necessity; jarh requires detail due to ikhtilaf — a reasoned asymmetry in evidence law.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi reasoning behind a key evidentiary rule: why a general declaration of a witness's integrity ('adalah) is accepted, but a general accusation of discrediting (jarh) is not. The Hanafis ground this distinction in two usul principles: avoidance of hardship (haraj) and the existence of disagreement (ikhtilaf) over what constitutes a defect. We will trace the istinbat chain and examine the rebuttal of the Shafi'i counterargument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and its Context
The text states the principle: 'Jarh is only accepted if explicit; ta'dil is accepted without being explicit.' Understand this as a rule of evidence for witness testimony and hadith narration.
The ruling is procedural, not a hukm taklifi.
2
Analyze the Hanafi Proof (Ta'lil)
The reasoning is aqli: ta'dil covers many obligations and prohibitions, making detail burdensome (haraj → necessity). Jarh is a single defect, easily specified; moreover, jarh causes are subject to ikhtilaf.
This is an istinbat via ta'lil (casual reasoning).
3
Identify the Usul Principles Used
Principle 1: 'Hardship begets ease' (al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir) for ta'dil. Principle 2: 'Taqlid is prohibited' for jarh because accepting a general jarh forces taqlid of the critic's opinion.
Both principles are well-established in Hanafi usul.
4
Examine the Cross-Madhhab Dispute
The Shafi'i position (as presented) argues that jarh causes differ in prohibition, so detail is needed; but ta'dil has no ikhtilaf. The Hanafi response: avoiding those causes is part of 'adalah, so ikhtilaf affects both; ta'dil is exceptional due to necessity.
The dispute turns on what is the criterion for requiring detail.
5
Synthesize the Final Ruling and Its Practical Application
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi: ta'dil is accepted in general form; jarh is accepted only if explicit (or by way of ruling, i.e., explicit in effect). This prevents procedural deadlock while preserving rigor against biases.
This ruling applies in courts and hadith criticism.

لنا : التعديل لا يقبل التفصيل فإن العدالة الاجتناب عن الممنوعات الشرعية والإتيان بالواجبات وتفصيلها لكثرتها متعسر يكلف به دفعاً للحرج بخلاف الجرح فإنه الإخلال بواحد من الأمور الشرعية وتعيينه غير متعذر ثم إن أسباب الجرح مختلف فيها فإن بعضها جارح عند البعض غير جارح عند الآخر كركض الدابة فلعل المزكي جرح بما ليس بجرح في الواقع أو عند المجتهد فلو قبل قوله يلزم تقليده وهو ممنوع عنه فلا يقلد إلا من علم صحة رأيه ولا يعلم إلا بالتفصيل حقيقة أو حكماً فلا يقبل إلا المبين فالمناط لوجوب البيان وجود الاختلاف في نفس الجرح أنه جارح أم لا لا وجود الاختلاف في كون ما جرح به معصية أولاً كاللعب بالشطرنج وأكل متروك التسمية عمداً حتى يرد أن الارتكاب بالأمور المجتهد فيها لا يوجب المعصية ولا يضر بالعدالة والحاصل أن مقتضى الدليل وجوب تفصيل الجرح والتعديل جميعاً لمكان الاختلاف إلا أنا جوزنا في التعديل الإطلاق للضرورة وأما احتجاج الشافعية بأن للجرح أسباباً وفيها اختلاف كما مر تقريره ويظهر من بعض كتبهم أن مناط الاختلاف في حرمة سبب الجرح فلعل المزكي رأى رجلاً يلعب بالشطرنج فحكم بالفسق وجرح وهو ليس فسقاً عند المجتهد فلا يقلده وبهذا افترق عما سلف فيرد عليه ما أورده ولو حمل على ما مر فالتفارق بما ذكروا في دليل التعديل بخلاف العدالة فإنها الاستقامة في الدين ولا يختلف فيها أصلاً ففيه أن اجتناب أسباب الجرح أسباب للعدالة فالاختلاف فيها اختلاف فيها والجرح والتعديل سيان وهذا ظاهر جداً وما في الحاشية أن الكذب حرام في كل مذهب فالتعديل من متمذهب بأي مذهب كان توثيق له بالصدق ولا يضر فيه الاختلاف في أسباب العدالة فيظن بالصدق بتعديل كل متمذهب فإن مناط قبول الرواية والشهادة هو الصدق ففيه أنه إن أراد التوثيق بالصدق سواء كان مع العدالة أو لا فغير نافع لأن هذا الظن مهدر شرعاً بالاجماع فإن رب فاسق بترك الصلاة لا يتعاطى الكذب بل يظن بصدقه ظناً قوياً ولا يقبل خبره إجماعاً وإن أراد التوثيق بالصدق الحاصل من جهة أنه لا يتعاطى محذور دینه فظاهر رب محذور عند رجل غير محذور آخر فرجع الأشكال قهقرى فافهم وما قيل في الجواب ثانياً أن الجرح إنما يثبت بالفسق في الجملة وهو مختلف فيه وأما التعديل فإنما يثبت بارتفاع الفسق مطلقاً وهذا مما لا يشوبه شبهة واختلاف ففيه أن ارتفاع الفسق مطلقاً إنما يكون باجتناب كل محذور والمحذور مختلف فيه فيكون الاجتناب أيضاً مختلفاً فيه نعم لو كان التعديل باجتناب كل محذور ولو في مذهب لتم لكنه ليس كذلك واعترض بأن عمل الكل من الأئمة في الكتب على إبهام التضعيف إلا قليلاً وقد قبلوا هذا التضعيف أن
Our proof: Ta'dil does not accept detail, because 'adalah (integrity) is avoiding forbidden things and performing obligations, and detailing them is difficult due to their abundance; it would impose hardship. Unlike jarh, for it is failing to fulfill one of the shariah matters, and specifying it is not impossible. Moreover, the causes of jarh are subject to disagreement: some are considered jarh by some but not by others, like racing a horse. Perhaps the one giving tazkiyah discredited by something that is not actually a discrediting factor in reality or according to the mujtahid. So if his statement is accepted, it would entail taqlid of him, which is prohibited. One cannot do taqlid except of one whose correctness of opinion is known, and that is only known through detail, either explicitly or in ruling. So only the explicit is accepted. Thus the criterion for requiring explication is the existence of disagreement about whether the cause itself is a discrediting factor or not, not the existence of disagreement about whether the act is a sin. For example, playing chess or eating meat without basmalah intentionally; it may be said that committing matters of ijtihad does not entail sin nor harm 'adalah. The conclusion is that the evidence requires detail in both jarh and ta'dil due to disagreement, except that we allowed generality in ta'dil out of necessity. As for the Shafi'i argument that jarh has causes with disagreement as discussed, and from some of their books the criterion of disagreement is the prohibition of the cause of jarh, so perhaps the one giving tazkiyah saw a man playing chess and ruled him a fasiq and discredited him, while it is not fisq according to the mujtahid, so he cannot be followed. By this it differs from what preceded. So the objection raised against them is answered. And if it is interpreted as previously, then the difference is what they mentioned in the proof of ta'dil. Unlike 'adalah, for it is uprightness in religion and there is no disagreement in it at all. But it is said: avoiding the causes of jarh are causes of 'adalah, so disagreement about them is disagreement about 'adalah, and jarh and ta'dil are the same. This is very apparent. And what is in the marginal note that lying is forbidden in every madhhab, so ta'dil by a follower of any madhhab is a confirmation of his truthfulness, and disagreement about causes of 'adalah does not harm it, so truthfulness is assumed by ta'dil of every follower. For the criterion of accepting narration and testimony is truthfulness. In it is that if he intends confirmation of truthfulness whether with 'adalah or not, it is of no benefit, because such a presumption is legally disregarded by consensus. Indeed, a fasiq who neglects prayer does not engage in lying; in fact, strong presumptions of his truthfulness exist, yet his report is not accepted by consensus. And if he intends confirmation of truthfulness arising from the fact that he does not engage in anything harmful to his religion, then it is apparent that what is harmful in one man's view may not be harmful to another. So the problem returns. So understand. And what is said in the second response: jarh is established only by fisq in general, and it is disputed; while ta'dil is established by the removal of fisq absolutely, and this is free from doubt and disagreement. In it is that removal of fisq absolutely can only happen by avoiding every harm, and harm is disputed, so avoidance is also disputed. Yes, if ta'dil were by avoiding every harm even within a madhhab, it would be correct, but it is not so. And it is objected that the practice of all imams in books is to leave jarh ambiguous except rarely, and they accepted this ambiguous jarh.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage provides the detailed Hanafi reasoning for why ta'dil can be accepted in general terms while jarh requires explicit detail. The argument is based on necessity (darurah) and disagreement (ikhtilaf). Integrity ('adalah) requires avoiding all prohibitions and performing all obligations; enumerating them all is extremely difficult and would cause hardship (haraj). Therefore, general statements of ta'dil are accepted out of necessity. In contrast, jarh involves a specific defect, which is not impossible to specify. Moreover, the causes of jarh are subject to ikhtilaf among scholars; what one considers a defect (e.g., racing horses, playing chess, eating without basmalah) may not be considered so by another. If a general jarh were accepted, it would force the qadi to follow the opinion of the one who gave tazkiyah (taqlid), which is not allowed unless his opinion is known to be correct. Hence, detail is needed to verify whether the cause is indeed a valid defect according to the scholar's own madhhab. The author rebuts the Shafi'i argument that the criterion is the prohibition of the act, by showing that avoiding causes of jarh are themselves part of 'adalah, so ikhtilaf applies to both. Then he addresses a marginal note suggesting that ta'dil confirms truthfulness, and truthfulness is the criterion; he shows that truthfulness alone is insufficient, as a fasiq might be truthful but his testimony is rejected. The overall conclusion is that ta'dil is accepted generally only due to necessity, while jarh requires detail due to ikhtilaf. This is a distinctive Hanafi position.

Key Terms
عدالة ('adalah): Integrity: avoiding all prohibited acts and performing all obligations.
حرج (haraj): Hardship or difficulty in religious obligations.
تقليد (taqlid): Following another's opinion without proof; prohibited in certain contexts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason the Hanafis give for accepting ta'dil in general (unqualified) form?
A) Because the causes of ta'dil are agreed upon by all scholars.
B) Because detailing all aspects of 'adalah would cause hardship (haraj).
C) Because the Quran commands accepting ta'dil in general.
D) Because the narrators themselves forbade detailing ta'dil.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between ta'dil (general accepted) and jarh (detail required) based on necessity (haraj) and disagreement (ikhtilaf) — a principled asymmetry in evidence law.

Preference of Jarh over Ta'dil: Evidence and Rationale
Establishes preference of jarh over ta'dil with evidentiary reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that jarh is preferred over ta'dil and explain its evidentiary basis in certainty and the muthbit/nafi distinction.

Core Idea
Jarh prevails over ta'dil because it is based on certainty and is affirmative, while ta'dil is only speculative.

In Islamic legal procedure, the credibility of witnesses is paramount. When a witness's character is impugned by one party (jarh) and defended as trustworthy by another (ta'dil), a conflict arises. This passage from 'Fawatih al-Rahamut' establishes the Hanafi rule that jarh takes precedence over ta'dil, and unpacks the logical and evidentiary basis for this preference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The ruling is that jarh (impugning) is preferred over ta'dil (declaring trustworthy) when they conflict. Understand that this applies when the mu'adil's denial is not absolutely certain.
2
Analyze the scenarios of denial
The text outlines cases: (a) denial without certainty – jarh preferred; (b) denial with certainty – requires tarjih; (c) admission but claiming repentance – ta'dil preferred by consensus.
3
Understand the epistemic basis
The core rationale: 'adala (uprightness) is speculative because it is based on outward observation and can be feigned. Jarh is based on eyewitnessing a forbidden act, giving it certainty.
4
Examine the muthbit/nafi argument
The jarh is muthbit (affirmative), the mu'adil is nafi (negative). Affirmative evidence is stronger. This is a universal principle in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هي الجارح سبباً لم ينفه المعدل أو نفاه لكن لا بيقين أما إذا نفي يقيناً) كما إذا ادعى الجارح أنه زنى بفلانة في بلدة كذا وقال المعدل : لم يدخل هو أو هي تلك البلدة قط، أم ماتت قبل لقائه (فالمصير إلى الترجيح (اتفاقاً لا أنه يقدم التعديل حينئذ إذ لا ترجيح لقول المعدل (ولو قال المعدل : هب أنه فعل ما قلت في الجرح، لكنه تاب عنه وحسن توبته (قدم التعديل) اتفاقاً، لكون الجارح غير مكذب ولا المعدل لنا في تقديم الجرح على التعديل (صدقهما) أي صدق المعدل والجارح (لأن العدالة ظنية) لأنها بالنظر إلى الظاهر فإن المعدل لم يلازمه آناء الليل والنهار، مع أن باب التصنع أيضاً مفتوح، فقصوى أمر المعدل الظن بالعدالة، فالمعدل لا يمكنه الإخبار إلا بحسب ظنه والجرح إنما يكون بارتكاب أمر من محذورات دينه، وهو متحقق بالمعاينة، فالجارح مخبر عن عمله فلا يلزم تكذيب المعدل (أقول هذا بناء على أن الجرح لا يجوز عن ظن) فإنه لو كان عن الظن والظن بالظن فلا يلزم في تقديم التعديل كذب الجارح إن تم) عدم جواز الجرح بالظن (تم البيان وإلا لا لكن ينبغي أن يعلم أنه لا حاجة إلى ذلك، فإن للجارح قوة العلم من علم المعدل، فإنه إنما يعتمد على ظاهر الأمر وحسن الظن، والجارح يدعي ارتكاب المحذور، ولا يتمكن العدل من نسبة المحذور إليه إلا عن تفتيش بالغ والعلم به عن دليل أو الظن به عن أمارة قوية وهذا القدر يكفينا فافهم. ولنا أيضاً : أن الجارح مثبت والمعدل ناف وللمثبت قوة فافهم.
The jarh is a cause that the mu'adil (one who declares trustworthy) does not deny, or he denies but not with certainty. As for when he denies with certainty, such as when the jarh claims that he committed zina with so-and-so in such-and-such a town, and the mu'adil says: 'He or she never entered that town at all,' or 'She died before meeting him,' then the recourse is to tarjih (preponderance) by agreement, not that ta'dil is given precedence, for there is no preponderance for the mu'adil's statement. And if the mu'adil says: 'Suppose he did what you said in the jarh, but he repented from it and his repentance was good,' then ta'dil is given precedence by agreement, because the jarh is not belied nor the mu'adil. For us, in preferring jarh over ta'dil, (we accept) the truthfulness of both, i.e., the mu'adil and the jarh, because 'adala (uprightness) is speculative (zanniyya) — for it is based on outward appearance, as the mu'adil does not accompany him day and night, and moreover the door of dissimulation is open. So the utmost of the mu'adil is speculation (zann) about uprightness; the mu'adil cannot inform except according to his speculation. Whereas jarh only occurs by committing something forbidden in his religion, which is realized by eyewitnessing. So the jarh reports about his action, and thus belittling the mu'adil is not required. I say this is based on the principle that jarh is not permissible based on speculation. For if it were based on speculation, then speculation on speculation would not necessitate regarding the mu'adil as a liar in giving precedence to ta'dil — if (the principle of) impermissibility of jarh by speculation is established, then the explanation is complete; otherwise no. But one should know that there is no need for that, for the jarh has the strength of knowledge over the knowledge of the mu'adil. The mu'adil only relies on outward appearance and good opinion, while the jarh claims the commission of a prohibited act. And the adil (upright person) cannot attribute a prohibited act to him except through thorough investigation and knowledge by evidence, or speculation based on a strong indication. And this much suffices us, so understand. And we also argue that the jarh is a muthbit (affirmative) and the mu'adil is a nafi (negative), and the muthbit has strength, so understand.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the rule concerning the preference of jarh (impugning a witness's credibility) over ta'dil (declaring him trustworthy). The author begins by stating that if the mu'adil denies the jarh's claim but not with certainty, the general rule is to prefer jarh. However, if the denial is with certainty (e.g., the mu'adil proves that the alleged event could not have happened), then the matter requires tarjih (weighing of evidence); ta'dil is not simply preferred. Conversely, if the mu'adil admits the act but claims repentance and its acceptance, then ta'dil is preferred by consensus, because neither party is lying. The author then explains the rationale: 'adala is based on speculation (zann), as it is judged from outward behavior and can be feigned. Jarh, in contrast, is based on witnessing a forbidden act, so it is more certain. The jarh thus has the strength of knowledge compared to the mu'adil's speculation. The author adds that even if jarh were permissible by speculation, it would still be stronger because the mu'adil only speculates about outward condition, while the jarh has investigated thoroughly. Finally, an additional argument is given: the jarh is muthbit (affirms a defect), and the mu'adil is nafi (denies it), and the affirmative has precedence. This is a standard Hanafi principle in the science of jarh wa ta'dil.

Key Terms
الجرح (al-jarh): Impugning the credibility of a witness by pointing out a specific forbidden act that he committed.
التعديل (al-ta'dil): Declaring a witness trustworthy based on apparent uprightness and good conduct.
الظن (al-zann): Speculation or probable opinion, as opposed to certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is jarh preferred over ta'dil in Hanafi usul?
A) Because the mu'adil is likely lying
B) Because jarh is based on certainty (muhaqqaq) while ta'dil is based on speculation (zann)
C) Because the jarh witness is always more numerous
D) Because ta'dil is not accepted in any case

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the preference of jarh over ta'dil is based on the greater evidentiary certainty of eyewitnessed facts over speculative assessments of character.

The 'Adala of the Companions: Hanafi Position
Discusses three opinions on 'adala of Sahaba and refutes Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that all Sahaba are 'udul, explain the ijtihad-based reasoning for those involved in fitna, and apply the Quranic evidence (48:18) to support this view.

Core Idea
All Companions are 'udul; those in fitna acted on ijtihad, so their narrations are accepted.

The uprightness ('adala) of the Companions is a foundational principle in Hanafi usul al-fiqh because it determines whether their hadith are accepted without scrutiny. This passage presents three opinions, clarifies that no Companion participated in 'Uthman's murder, and refutes the Mu'tazila who exclude fighters against 'Ali. The Hanafi view, grounded in Quranic praise and ijtihad theory, upholds the 'adala of all Sahaba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three opinions
Locate the three positions on the 'adala of the Sahaba: (1) all are 'udul by default, (2) they are like other Muslims needing tazkiya, (3) they are 'udul until entering fitna. Understand the refinement of the third: those who entered fitna are fasiq with certainty, but no Sahabi entered the fitna of 'Uthman's murder.
The author rejects the third position's extreme version and aligns with the first.
2
Analyze the Mu'tazila objection
Read the Mu'tazila claim that those who fought 'Ali without repentance lose 'adala. The author refutes this by listing major Companions who fought but are unanimously considered upright, like 'A'isha, al-Zubayr, and Talha.
The refutation relies on their manifest virtue and later withdrawal.
3
Understand the ijtihad defense
The author argues that these Companions acted on their ijtihad, believed they were obeying Allah, and later realized their error and withdrew. This preserves their 'adala because the sin is excused by ijtihad.
This is the core Hanafi principle: good faith ijtihad prevents fisq.
4
Examine the dalil
The author cites Quran 48:18 (pleasure with those under the tree) to show that even Mu'awiya's party included al-Mughira, who is explicitly praised by Allah. Thus, the entire group's actions were based on ijtihad, not sin.
This verse is used to argue that Allah's pleasure covers the participants, so their 'adala is established.
5
Apply to usul al-fiqh
Derive the rule: acceptance of hadith from any Sahabi without tazkiya, even those who were on opposing sides in the fitna, because their 'adala is default and their involvement was ijtihad.
This contrasts with the Mu'tazila who would reject reports from those they deem fasiq.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(مسألة: الأكثر من أهل القبلة هم أهل السنة والجماعة القامعين للبدعة قالوا: (الأصل في الصحابة (العدالة فلا يحتاج إلى التزكية وقيل : هم كغيرهم من المسلمين، منهم عدول وغير عدول فيحتاج إلى التزكية (وقيل) هم عدول إلى الدخول في الفتنة وهي قتل أمير المؤمنين (عثمان) رضي الله عنه أو بغي معاوية) على أمير المؤمنين علي رضي الله تعالى عنه (فلا يقبل الداخلون في إحدى الفتنتين (إلا) بالتزكية، لأن الفاسق غير معين) لأن أحد الفريقين على الحق، والآخر على الباطل، ولا معين لعدم العلم فيه ما فيه، فإن عدم التعين ممنوع إلا إذا بني على اجتهاد كل فحينئذ لا شائبة لفسق أحد، ويمكن أن يكون مرادهم أن الداخلين في الفتنة غير معينين فلا بد من التزكية ليعلم أن أياً منهم داخل وأياً خارج، وفي «شرح المختصر حرر هذا المذهب بأنه يزكي غير الداخل. وأما الداخلون فهم فاسقون بيقين، فإن أراد أن غير الداخلين يزكون قبل دخولهم وبعد الدخول فاسقون فهو ليس مذهب أحد. واعلم أن قتل أمير المؤمنين عثمان رضي الله تعالى عنه من أكبر الكبائر، فإنه إمام حق، وقد أخبر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم بأنه يقتل مظلوماً، وقد أفنى عمره في طاعة الله تعالى ورسوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم ولم يدخل أحد من الصحابة رضوان الله عليهم في قتله رضي الله عنه، ولم يرض به أحد أيضاً، بل جماعة من الفساق اجتمعوا كاللصوص وفعلوا ما فعلوا وأنكر الصحابة كلهم كما ورد في الأخبار الصحاح، فالداخلون في القتل أو الراضون به فاسقون البتة، لكن لم يكن فيهم أحد من الصحابة، كما صرح به غير واحد من أهل الحديث (وقالت المعتزلة الصحابة كلهم عدول إلا من قاتل) أمير المؤمنين (علياً) كرّم الله وجهه ووجوه ره آله الكرام ولم يتب) عن هذا الصنع، ظاهر هذا القول بهت وهذيان فإن ممن قاتل أمير المؤمنين علياً كرّم الله وجهه ووجوه آله الكرام أم المؤمنين عائشة الصديقة التي فضلها على النساء كفضل الثريد على سائر الطعام كما ورد في الحديث الصحيح المروي في صحيح البخاري والزبير بن العوام، وطلحة بن عبيد الله من العشرة المبشرة وحواري رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وعدالتهم جلية كظهور الشمس على نصف النهار، ولعلهم يدعون التوبة وهو الصواب فإن أم المؤمنين، قد اعتزلت عن الحرب، واستقرت في المدينة المطهرة، والزبير أيضاً قد اعتزل وامتنع عن إرادة الحرب فقتله شقي مظلوماً، وطلحة رضي الله عنه وإن مات بالطعنة التي طعن في الجمل على ما في جامع الأصول لكنه بقي حياً إلى أن أدرك رجلاً من أصحاب أمير المؤمنين علي رضي تعالى عنه فبايعه وقال : هذه بيعة علي ثم إنه يخدش بأنه على هذا يلزم ارتكابهم الكبيرة، والتزامه لا يخلو عن حماقة، كيف وعدالتهم مقطوعة، وقد أخبر الله تعالى أنه راض عنهم، بل الحق أنهم في هذا الصنع كانوا يعملون على مقتضى اجتهادهم وهم فيه مطيعون الله ورسوله، ونرجو أن يثابوا عليه ، ثم لما تبين أنهم أخطأوا في اجتهادهم اعتزلوا وامتنعوا عن القتال، وهذا مما يجب أن يعتقد فيه والله أعلم بقي أمر بغي معاوية والذي عليه جمهور أهل السنة أن هذا أيضاً خطأ في الاجتهاد ولا يلزم منه بطلان العدالة، لكن يخدشه عدم إظهار الحجية في مقاتلة أمير المؤمنين علي، وكان هو ألين للحق واستمراره على الصنع الذي صنع من أن قتل عمار كان من أبين الحجج على حقية رأي أمير المؤمنين علي، ولم ينقل في الدفع إلا أمر بعيد هو أن الجائي برجل شيخ في المعركة قاتل إياه، وهو كما ترى، لكن الذي يؤيد ما ذهبوا إليه أن المغيرة بن شعبة رضي الله تعالى عنه كان مع كان معاوية رضي الله عنه، وهو من أصحاب الحديبية الذين قال الله تعالى فيهم : ﴿لَقَدْ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ إِذْ يُبَايِعُونَكَ تَحْتَ الشَّجَرَةِ فَعَلِمَ مَا فِي قُلُوبِهِمْ ﴾ [الفتح: ۱۸] فرضاً الله تعالى عنهم مقطوع به فعلم أن الصنع الذي أيده ورضي به الله
Issue: The majority of the people of the Qibla are Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a who suppress innovation. They said: The original ruling regarding the Companions is that they are 'udul (upright), so they do not need tazkiya (validation). And it was said: They are like other Muslims; among them are upright and not upright, so they need tazkiya. And it was said: They are 'udul until they enter into fitna (civil strife), which is the murder of Ameer al-Mu'mineen 'Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) or the rebellion of Mu'awiya against Ameer al-Mu'mineen 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him). So those who enter into either of the two fitnas are not accepted except with tazkiya, because the fasiq (sinner) is not specified. Because one of the two parties is upon truth and the other upon falsehood, and there is no specification due to lack of knowledge in that matter. But the lack of specification is precluded unless it is based on each one's ijtihad, then there is no stain of fisq for anyone. And it is possible that their intent is that those who entered the fitna are unspecified, so tazkiya is necessary to know which of them entered and which remained out. In Sharh al-Mukhtasar, this madhhab was refined as: one does tazkiya for those who did not enter. As for those who entered, they are fasiq with certainty. If he meant that those who did not enter are declared upright before they enter, and after entering they are fasiq, then that is not a madhhab of anyone. And know that the murder of Ameer al-Mu'mineen 'Uthman (رضي الله عنه) is among the greatest major sins, for he was a rightful Imam, and the Messenger of Allah (صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم) informed that he would be killed unjustly. He spent his life in obedience to Allah and His Messenger, and none of the Companions participated in his murder, nor did any approve of it. Rather, a group of fasaq (sinners) gathered like thieves and did what they did, and all the Companions denounced it as reported in authentic reports. So those who participated in the murder or were pleased with it are definitely fasiq, but none of them were among the Companions, as stated by more than one scholar of hadith. The Mu'tazila said: All the Companions are 'udul except those who fought against Ameer al-Mu'mineen 'Ali (may Allah ennoble his face and the faces of his noble family) and did not repent from this action. The apparent meaning of this statement is false and nonsense, for among those who fought against Ameer al-Mu'mineen 'Ali are the Mother of the Believers 'A'isha al-Siddiqa, whom he preferred over women as tharid (a dish) is preferred over other foods, as reported in the authentic hadith in Sahih al-Bukhari, and al-Zubayr ibn al-'Awwam, and Talha ibn 'Ubaydullah, who are among the ten promised paradise and are the disciples of the Messenger of Allah. Their 'adala (uprightness) is as clear as the sun at midday. Perhaps they claim repentance, and that is correct, for the Mother of the Believers withdrew from the war and settled in Medina; al-Zubayr also withdrew and refrained from desiring war, and was killed unjustly by a wretch; and Talha (رضي الله عنه) even though he died from the stab that he received in the Camel (Battle) according to Jami' al-Usul, he remained alive until he met a man from the companions of Ameer al-Mu'mineen 'Ali (رضي الله عنه), gave him allegiance and said: 'This is the allegiance of 'Ali.' Then there is a criticism: based on this, they committed a major sin, and its affirmation is not devoid of foolishness? How can that be when their 'adala is established, and Allah has said He is pleased with them? Rather, the truth is that in this action they acted according to their ijtihad, and in it they were obeying Allah and His Messenger. We hope they will be rewarded for it. Then when it became clear that they erred in their ijtihad, they withdrew and refrained from fighting. This is what must be believed, and Allah knows best. There remains the matter of Mu'awiya's rebellion. The view of the majority of Ahl al-Sunna is that this too was an error in ijtihad and does not entail nullification of 'adala. But it is tarnished by his not showing argument for fighting Ameer al-Mu'mineen 'Ali, and he was more lenient toward the truth; his persistence in his action despite the fact that the killing of 'Ammar was among the clearest proofs of the correctness of 'Ali's view. And no defense is reported except a far-fetched matter that a man came with an old man in the battlefield and fought him. You can see this. But what supports their view is that al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba (رضي الله عنه) was with Mu'awiya (رضي الله عنه), and he was among the companions of the tree (Bay'at al-Ridwan) concerning whom Allah said: 'Certainly Allah was pleased with the believers when they pledged allegiance to you under the tree' (Al-Fath: 18). So Allah's pleasure with them is definitely established, so it is known that the action that he supported and with which Allah was pleased...
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage addresses the critical issue of the 'adala (uprightness) of the Companions (Sahaba). The author presents three positions: (1) All Sahaba are 'udul by default and need no validation. (2) They are like other Muslims; some are upright, some not, so they need tazkiya. (3) They are 'udul until they enter into the fitna of the murder of 'Uthman or the rebellion of Mu'awiya; those who entered such fitna are not accepted unless validated. The author then refines the third: those who entered are fasiq with certainty, but those who did not enter are 'udul. He then emphasizes that no Companion participated in 'Uthman's murder. He then refutes the Mu'tazila claim that all Sahaba are 'udul except those who fought 'Ali and did not repent. He argues that this would exclude major figures like 'A'isha, al-Zubayr, and Talha, whose uprightness is unquestionable. Instead, he explains that they acted on ijtihad, then realized their error and withdrew. Regarding Mu'awiya, the majority view is that he erred in ijtihad but his 'adala remains intact, though some objections are noted. The implication of this discussion for usul al-fiqh is that the testimony and reports of all Sahaba are accepted without questioning their integrity, except where there is clear evidence of sin. This principle affects the acceptance of hadith transmitted by them.

Key Terms
الصحابة (al-Sahaba): Those who met the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم) as believers and died as believers.
العدالة (al-'adala): Uprightness or moral integrity, a prerequisite for accepting testimony and narration.
الفتنة (al-fitna): Civil strife or trial, specifically the conflicts that occurred among the Sahaba after the death of 'Uthman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi position on the 'adala of the Sahaba who participated in the fitna?
A) They are all fasiq and their reports are rejected
B) They are 'udul because they acted on ijtihad and later withdrew or repented
C) They are accepted only if they provide tazkiya
D) They are considered hypocrites

Key Takeaway
All Companions are 'udul; involvement in fitna is excused by ijtihad, and their narrations are unconditionally accepted.
