Refuting the Shafi'i Claim: The Prophet's Exclusive Use of 'Hiba' in Marriage
Refuting the Shafi'i claim that 'hiba' is exclusive to the Prophet

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of 'al-ma'na la yalzam al-lafz' to distinguish between specifications of meaning and wording, and evaluate the Shafi'i position using the Quranic context.

Core Idea
The Prophet's privilege to marry by 'hiba' is about the dower, not the word—meaning does not necessitate lexical exclusivity.

This lesson examines a key usul dispute: Did the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) have an exclusive right to use the word 'hiba' to contract marriage? The Shafi'is argue that since the meaning (ownership without compensation) is exclusive to the Prophet, the word must also be exclusive. The Hanafis respond by distinguishing between meaning and wording, citing the Quranic context of removing hardship and the general permissibility of figurative language. By the end of this lesson, you will understand not only the ruling but the linguistic and usul principles that underlie the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Issue
Determine exactly what the Shafi'is claim: that the Prophet's exclusive permission to marry by 'hiba' (a woman giving herself) without dower extends to the very word 'hiba'. That is, only the Prophet can use this word in a marriage contract.
The dispute is over the scope of khususiyya (exclusive privilege).
2
State the Opposing Position and Its Dalil
The Shafi'is cite Quran 33:50, which says 'khalisatan laka min dun al-mu'minin' (exclusively for you, not for the believers). They argue that the word follows the meaning (al-lafz tabi' lil-ma'na); since the meaning is exclusive, the word is exclusive.
Their proof is based on a linguistic principle: necessary concomitance between meaning and wording.
3
Analyse the Hanafi Response
The Hanafis respond by denying the necessary connection. The Quranic specification 'khalisatan laka' refers to the ruling (no dower), not the lexical word. The verse immediately explains the reason: 'li-kayla yakuna 'alayka haraj' (so that there be no hardship upon you). This causation (ta'lil) indicates the privilege is the removal of the dower obligation, not the wording.
The Hanafi usul principle: al-khass yufidu al-takhsis fi al-hukm la fi al-lafz.
4
Apply the Hanafi Principle: Meaning Does Not Entail Word
Figurative language (majaz) is available to all competent speakers. The meaning 'ownership without dower' is not a necessary property of the word 'hiba'; rather, the word is an auditory vehicle that can be used for various meanings by convention. Therefore, exclusivity of meaning does not entail exclusivity of wording.
This is a key usul distinction: between dalala mutabaqa (conformative indication of meaning) and dalala iltizam (implicative indication of necessary concomitants).
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence (thamarah) is: If a Muslim other than the Prophet uses the word 'hiba' to contract marriage, in the Hanafi school the marriage is valid with a dower due by analogy to normal marriage contracts. In the Shafi'i school, such a marriage may be invalid because the word 'hiba' cannot be used by others.
The dispute thus affects the validity of actual marriages.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشافعية النكاح بلفظ الهبة خص به (عليه وآله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام لقوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّا أَحْلَلْنَا لَكَ أَزْوَجَكَ الَّتِي عَاتَيْتَ أُجُورَهُنَّ وَمَا مَلَكَتْ يَمِينُكَ مِمَّا أَفَاءَ الله عليك وبنات عمك وبنات عمتك وبنات خَالِكَ وَبَنَاتِ خَلَكَ الَّتِي هَاجَرْنَ مَعَكَ وَامْرَأَةٌ مُؤْمِنَةً إِن وَهَبَتْ نَفْسَهَا لِلنَّبِي إِنْ أَرَادَ النَّبِيُّ أَن يَسْتَنكِحَهَا خَالِصَةً لَكَ مِن دُونِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٥٠] وذلك لأن اللفظ تابع للمعنى ولازم له (وقد خص صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم بالمعنى فإن معناها التملك بلا عوض، وهو عليه وآله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام يختص بالتملك من غير عوض (فيخص) كذلك (باللفظ فالاختصاص بالمعنى بالدلالة المطابقية، وباللفظ بالإشارة لكونه من لوازمه فلا يرد ما في «التحرير» أنه يأبى عن الاختصاص باللفظ التعليل بنفي الحرج بلزوم المهر بقوله تعالى: ﴿ لِكَيْلَا يَكُونَ عَلَيْك حَرم ﴾ [الأحزاب: ۳۷] بل التعليل يقتضي اختصاص المعنى، كذا في «الحاشية (وعندنا يرجع) الخصوص إلى نفي المهر فقط، وهو الحق، لأنه لا حجر في التجوز) فإنه تصرف لفظي يشترك فيه كل من هو أهل محاورة (فالمعنى ليس بلازم له أي اللفظ (إرادة ) فلا يلزم من اختصاص المعنى اختصاص اللفظ، ويمكن حمل عبارة «التحرير» عليه أيضاً فتأمل
The Shafi'is [say that] marriage by the word 'hiba' is a specific privilege for him (peace and blessings be upon him and his family and Companions) due to His saying: 'Indeed, We have made lawful for you your wives to whom you have given their due compensation... and a believing woman if she gives herself to the Prophet, if the Prophet desires to marry her, exclusively for you, not for the believers.' [al-Ahzab: 50] And that is because the word follows the meaning and is necessary for it. And he (peace and blessings be upon him and his family and Companions) was specified with the meaning: its meaning is ownership without compensation, and he (peace and blessings be upon him and his family and Companions) is distinguished by ownership without compensation. Thus he is also specified with the word. So the specification of the meaning is by conformative indication, and of the word by implication because it is a necessary concomitant. So what is in al-Tahrir is not challenged: that specification by the word is repelled by the causation of removing hardship regarding the obligation of dower in His saying: 'so that there be no hardship upon you' [al-Ahzab: 37]. Rather, the causation requires specification of the meaning. Like that in al-Hashiya. And with us, the specificity refers only to the negation of dower, and that is correct, because there is no restriction on figurative usage. For it is a verbal action in which every competent speaker participates. So the meaning is not necessary for the word; rather, the word is intended. So specification of the meaning does not necessitate specification of the word. And the expression of al-Tahrir can be interpreted accordingly as well, so reflect.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (ikhtilaf) between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the nature of the Prophet's special privilege (khususiyya) in marriage. The Shafi'is argue that because the Prophet was permitted to marry a woman who 'gives herself' (hiba nafsaha) without a dower, the very wording 'hiba' becomes exclusive to him. They claim that the word follows the meaning, and since the meaning (ownership without dower) is exclusive, the wording must also be exclusive. The Hanafi response, stated as 'indana' (with us), is that the Prophet's privilege is only in the absence of a dower, not in the wording. Figurative language is available to all competent speakers. The meaning of a word does not necessitate that the word itself is exclusive. The Hanafi position is that the verse's specification ('khalisatan laka') applies only to the negation of the dower, not to the word 'hiba'. Therefore, other Muslims can also use the word 'hiba' in marriage contracts, though they would still require a dower analogically. The commentary resolves the objection from al-Tahrir by showing that the verse reducing hardship ('li-kayla yakuna 'alayka haraj') actually supports the meaning-based exclusivity, not the wording.

Key Terms
الهبة (al-hiba): In this context, a woman giving herself to the Prophet in marriage without a dower, as a gift.
خصوصية (khususiyya): An exclusive privilege of the Prophet (peace be upon him).
لفظ (lafz): The word or verbal expression.
معنى (ma'na): The meaning, content, or legal ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the extent of the Prophet's special privilege in marrying by the word 'hiba'?
A) The exclusive right to use the word 'hiba' in marriage.
B) The negation of the dower (mahr) only.
C) The exclusive right to marry without witnesses.
D) The exclusive right to marry more than four wives.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the Prophet's exclusive marriage by 'hiba' only removed the dower requirement; the word itself is not exclusive, and other Muslims may use it with the dower obligation remaining.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
6 min
Hanafi Critique of al-Masalih al-Mursalah
Hanafi critique of masalih mursalah and response to Malik's arguments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on al-masalih al-mursalah and apply the default rule of ibaha when no specific text exists.

Core Idea
No specific text means permissibility, not a gap.

This passage defends the Hanafi rejection of unrestricted interests (masalih mursalah) as a source of law. It addresses the Maliki argument that without this source, some incidents would lack rulings, and the claim that the Companions acted on interests. The Hanafi response relies on general texts and the default of permissibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed source
Recognize that al-masalih al-mursalah refers to interests not recognized or rejected by texts. The passage defines the 'gharib' type where no suitability is known but cancellation is not known either.
This is the type Malik accepts; Hanafis reject.
2
State the Hanafi default rule
Note the Hanafi principle: absence of a specific textual ruling indicates permissibility (ibaha) by virtue of general revealed evidence.
The passage explicitly states: 'عدم المدرك دليل الاباحة'.
3
Critique the Maliki entailment argument
Malik argues that without masalih mursalah, incidents would lack rulings. Hanafis deny the entailment because general texts and accepted analogies cover all cases, and ibaha fills gaps.
The Hanafi response: نمنع الملازمة.
4
Understand the exception: mula'im mursal
If some suitability (mula'im) is known—even from genus—the mursal is accepted even by many Hanafis. This is not the same as the unrestricted gharib type.
Imam al-Haramayn and al-Shafi'i accept this category.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالمال كله مشغول بها فيكون فقيراً فصار غير واجد للعبد ،وغيره، فوجب الصوم بالنص، وليس فيه اعتبار ما علم الغاؤه وإلى ما لم يعلم) عطف على قوله : إلى ما علم فإن لم يعلم فيه أحد اعتبارات الملائم من اعتبار نوعه أو جنسه في جنس الحكم، أو جنسه في عين الحكم ، لكن لم يعلم الغاؤه أيضاً فهو الغريب من المرسل، وهو المسمى بالمصالح المرسلة حجة عند مالك رحمه الله (والمختار عند الجمهور) من أهل الأصول والفقهاء (رده لنا لا دليل بدون الاعتبار من الشارع (وإن كان على سنن العقل فلا يعتبر أصلاً، وهذا لا يتأتى ممن يقول بالإحالة إذ الإخالة تفيد العلية ههنا أيضاً فافهم أصحاب المصالح المرسلة (قالوا : أولاً: لو لم تعتبر المصالح المرسلة (الخلت الوقائع من الأحكام وهو باطل، فوجب قبولها (قلنا) لنا : أن نمنع الملازمة لأن العمومات من الكتاب والسنة (والأقيسة) المأخوذة من المؤثرات والملائمات عامة ) للوقائع كلها على ما يظهر بالاستقراء وأيضاً : عدم المدرك) للحكم بخصوصه في واقعة واقعة مدرك للاباحة الشرعية لدلالة الدليل السمعي عليه كما مر في الأحكام فتذكر (و) قالوا :(ثانياً : الصحابة كانوا يقنعون برعاية المصالح) ولم ينكر عليهم فصار إجماعاً (قلنا) كونهم قانعين عليها ممنوع (بل) إنما اعتبروا من العلل ما اطلعوا على اعتبار نوعه أو جنسه في نوع الحكم أو جنسه (هذا) وعليك بالاستقراء حتى يظهر لك جلية الحال (وإن علم فيه ذلك أي أحد اعتبارات الملائم (فهو المرسل الملائم قبله الإمام) إمام الحرمين (ونقل عن الإمام الشافعي وعليه جمهور (الحنفية قال في «التحرير» : يجب على الحنفية قبول القسم الأخير من المرسل وقبوله أحق بالقبول وقال في «البديع : المرسل الذي لم يعلم الغاؤه مردود عندنا (ورده) الأكثر ومنهم الآمدي) من الشافعية وابن الحاجب من المالكية (متمسكين بعدم الدليل على اعتباره إذ لم يشهد باعتباره أصل (وربما يمنع) عدم الدليل (فإن اعتبار الجنس نوع من الاعتبار يفيد ظناً ما وههنا قد وجد الاعتبار في الشرع بجنسه في عين الحكم أو جنسه أو بعينه في جنس الحكم فتأمل فيه
All the wealth is occupied by it, so he becomes poor, thus he is not a possessor of a slave, and other than that, so fasting is obligatory by text. And in it is not consideration of that whose cancellation is known, and to that which is not known (it is an apposition to his saying: to that which is known). For if none of the considerations of suitability (al-mula'im) are known in it—whether consideration of its type or its genus in the genus of the ruling, or its genus in the specific ruling—but its cancellation is also not known, then it is the gharib (strange) type of mursal, and it is called al-masalih al-mursalah. It is a proof according to Malik (may Allah have mercy on him). And the chosen position according to the majority of usul scholars and jurists is its rejection, because there is no proof for us without consideration from the Lawgiver. And if it is in accordance with reason, it is not considered at all. And this cannot be had from one who claims suitability (ikhala), for suitability indicates causality here too, so understand, O proponents of masalih mursalah. They said: First: If masalih mursalah were not considered, incidents would be devoid of rulings, and that is invalid; therefore their acceptance is obligatory. We said: We deny the entailment, because the general texts of the Book and the Sunnah and the analogies derived from effective (mu'assirat) and suitable (mula'imat) descriptions are general for all incidents, as appears by induction. Also: the lack of a specific source for a ruling in a particular incident is a source for permissibility (ibaha) under Shari'ah, due to the evidence of the revealed proof upon it, as passed in the rulings, so remember. And they said: Secondly: The Companions acted upon considerations of interests and no one objected, so it became consensus. We said: The claim that they acted upon them is denied; rather, they only considered from the effective causes (ilal) those whose type or genus they had discovered to be considered in the type or genus of the ruling. This—and upon you is induction until the clarity of the matter becomes apparent. And if that (i.e., one of the considerations of suitability) is known in it, then it is the suitable mursal (al-mursal al-mula'im), accepted by Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni), and transmitted from Imam al-Shafi'i, and upon it are the majority of Hanafis. He said in al-Tahrir: It is obligatory upon Hanafis to accept the last category of mursal, and its acceptance is more worthy. And he said in al-Badi': The mursal whose cancellation is not known is rejected by us. And the majority rejected it, among them al-Amidi from the Shafi'is and Ibn al-Hajib from the Malikis, holding to the lack of proof for its consideration, since no principle has witnessed to its consideration. And perhaps the lack of proof is denied, for consideration of the genus is a type of consideration that yields some probability, and here consideration in the Shari'ah has been found of its genus in the specific ruling or its genus, or of its specific in the genus of the ruling, so reflect on that.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute about the validity of al-masalih al-mursalah (unrestricted interests) as a source of law. The passage first defines the gharib category of mursal descriptions: those where no recognized suitability is found, nor is its cancellation known—this is what Malik accepts. The Hanafi/Jumhur position is rejection because there is no explicit textual consideration. The passage then presents two arguments from proponents and Hanafi responses: (1) Without mursal, incidents lack rulings; Hanafis reply that general texts (Quran, Sunnah, and accepted analogies) cover all cases, and the absence of a specific ruling indicates permissibility by the default rule of ibaha. (2) Companions used interests; Hanafis reply they only used effective causes whose type/genus had textual basis. The passage then notes a nuance: if any suitability is known, it becomes the 'mula'im mursal' which even Hanafis accept, and al-Juwayni and al-Shafi'i also accept it. The majority rejection is based on lack of textual evidence, but the author suggests that considering the genus itself provides some probability, so the blanket denial of proof may be debated.

Key Terms
المصالح المرسلة (al-masalih al-mursalah): Interests not explicitly recognized or rejected by Shari'ah texts
الملائم (al-mula'im): A description whose suitability is known from textual evidence
الغريب (al-gharib): A suitable description whose cancellation is not known but no textual recognition
عدم المدرك (adam al-mudrak): Lack of a specific textual source for a ruling

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling on a new incident that has no specific text?
A) It is forbidden until a source is found.
B) It is permissible due to the general permissibility (ibaha) as indicated by revealed proof.
C) It must be analogized to masalih mursalah.
D) It is left without a ruling.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul principle: absence of specific evidence for prohibition is itself evidence for permissibility, making masalih mursalah unnecessary.
